2:32:2093:0:14:72:482:700:12:Times:12:Times:A Macroeconomic Model with Financially Constrained Producers and Intermediaries
2:33:2172:14:14:72:364:686:12:Times:12:Times:Vadim Elenev, Tim Landvoigt, and Stijn Van Nieuwerburgh
2:34:2227:14:14:72:234:672:12:Times:12:Times:NBER Working Paper No. 24757
2:35:2255:14:14:72:121:658:12:Times:12:Times:June 2018
2:36:2264:14:28:72:283:644:12:Times:12:Times:JEL No. E02,E1,E20,E44,E6,G12,G18,G21
2:37:2301:28:28:273:338:616:12:Times:12:Times:ABSTRACT
2:38:2309:28:14:72:545:588:12:Times:12:g_d0_f1:How much capital should financial intermediaries hold? We propose a general equilibrium model 
2:39:2402:14:14:72:546:574:12:Times:12:Times:with a financial sector that makes risky long-term loans to firms, funded by deposits from savers. 
2:40:2501:14:14:72:546:560:12:Times:12:Times:Government guarantees  create  a  role  for  bank  capital  regulation.  The  model  captures  the  sharp 
2:41:2606:14:14:72:546:546:12:Times:12:Times:and  persistent  drop in  macro-economic  aggregates  and  credit  provision  as  well  as  the  sharp 
2:42:2708:14:14:72:546:532:12:Times:12:Times:change in credit spreads observed during the Great Recession. Policies requiring intermediaries to 
2:43:2806:14:14:72:545:518:12:Times:12:Times:hold  more  capital  reduce  financial fragility,  reduce  the  size  of  the  financial  and  non-financial 
2:44:2914:14:14:72:546:504:12:Times:12:Times:sectors,  and  locally  increase  macro-economic volatility.  They  redistribute  wealth  from  savers  to 
2:45:3020:14:42:72:527:490:12:Times:12:Times:the owners of banks and non-financial firms. Current capital requirements are close to optimal.
2:46:3114:42:14:72:141:448:12:Times:12:Times:Vadim Elenev
2:47:3126:14:14:72:197:434:12:Times:12:Times:Johns Hopkins University
2:48:3150:14:14:72:185:420:12:Times:12:Times:100 International Drive
2:49:3173:14:14:72:124:406:12:Times:12:Times:Suite 1329
2:50:3183:14:14:72:178:392:12:Times:12:Times:Baltimore, MD 21202
2:51:3202:14:28:72:156:378:12:Times:12:Times:velenev@jhu.edu
2:52:3217:28:14:72:144:350:12:Times:12:Times:Tim Landvoigt
2:53:3230:14:14:72:172:336:12:Times:12:Times:The Wharton School
2:54:3248:14:14:72:203:322:12:Times:12:Times:University of Pennsylvania
2:55:3274:14:14:72:161:308:12:Times:12:Times:3620 Locust Walk

2:57:3312:14:14:72:124:280:12:Times:12:Times:and NBER

2:64:3456:14:14:306:358:378:12:Times:12:Times:and NBER
2:65:3464:14:0:306:427:364:12:Times:12:Times:svnieuwe@stern.nyu.edu
3:66:3486:0:37:64:200:715:17:g_d0_f2:17:g_d0_f2:1    Introduction
3:67:3503:37:21:64:546:678:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:The financial crisis and Great Recession of 2007-09 underscored the importance of the financial
3:68:3598:21:21:64:546:657:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:system for the broader economy.  Borrower default rates, bank insolvencies, government bailouts
3:69:3693:21:21:64:546:636:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:of financial institutions, and credit spreads all spiked while real interest rates were very low. The
3:70:3794:21:21:64:546:615:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:disruptions in financial intermediation fed back on the real economy.  Consumption, investment,
3:71:3889:21:25:64:314:594:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:and output all fell substantially and persistently.
3:72:3940:25:21:75:547:569:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:These events have prompted a vigorous yet unresolved debate among policymakers and aca-
3:73:4027:21:21:64:546:548:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:demics on whether the economy would be better off with stricter bank capital requirements.
3:74:4117:21:21:64:546:527:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:The December 2017 Minneapolis Plan reflects the Federal Reserve’s view and proposes raising
3:75:4208:21:21:64:546:506:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:bank capital requirements to 23.5% of risk-weighted assets, with further increases to 38% for
3:76:4301:21:20:64:546:485:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:banks that remain systemically important.  In their seminal book, Admati and Hellwig (2013)
3:77:4392:20:21:64:546:465:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:propose raising capital requirements to 25% of assets.  Larger equity capital buffers would re-
3:78:4487:21:21:64:546:444:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:sult  in  less  risk-taking,  lower  risk  of  bank  failure  and  concomitant  government  bailouts,  but
3:79:4593:21:21:64:546:423:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:also in a smaller banking sector that lends less to the real economy, depressing investment and
3:80:4688:21:21:64:546:402:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:output.  Considering this trade-off,  Admati and Hellwig argue that “for society,  there are in
3:81:4783:21:21:64:546:381:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:fact  significant  benefits  and  essentially  no  cost  from  much  higher  equity  requirements.”  The
3:82:4887:21:21:64:546:360:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:authors of the Minneapolis Plan agree, writing that their plan “will have paid for itself many
3:83:4981:21:21:64:546:339:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:times over if it avoids one financial crisis.” This argument is not without controversy in the
3:84:5075:21:25:64:402:318:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:academy (Calomeris, 2013) and heavily contested by the industry.
3:85:5139:25:21:75:547:293:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:What  is  missing  in  this  debate  is  a  quantitative  general  equilibrium  model  that  embeds  a
3:86:5241:21:21:64:546:272:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:financial sector in a model of the macro-economy, and that can capture infrequent but large
3:87:5332:21:21:64:546:251:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:financial  crises.   Our  paper  proposes  such  a  model.   In  the  model,  banks  extend  long-term
3:88:5434:21:21:64:546:230:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:loans to firms who invest and are subject to aggregate and idiosyncratic productivity shocks.
3:89:5527:21:21:64:546:209:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Firm  default  results  in  losses  for  their  lenders,  which  can  trigger  bank  default.   Even  banks
3:90:5634:21:21:64:546:188:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:that remain standing become fragile and cut lending to firms.  A large and persistent decline
3:91:5727:21:21:64:546:167:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:in credit depresses output persistently.  The high leverage of banks, which far exceeds that of
3:92:5822:21:21:64:546:146:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:firms, amplifies modest credit losses into financial disasters.  The nonlinear behavior of credit
3:93:5919:21:21:64:546:125:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:spreads reflects this financial distress.  The government bails out the creditors of the banks that
3:94:6018:21:20:64:546:104:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:fail by issuing government debt, gradually repaid through future taxation.  Because financial
3:95:6111:20:0:64:546:84:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:intermediaries  are  constrained  in  their  ability  to  re-lever  and  raising  new  equity  from  their
4:96:6218:0:21:64:546:715:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:shareholders is expensive, the banking sector shrinks substantially and persistently.  Real inter-
4:97:6316:21:21:64:546:694:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:est rates must fall to induce savers to accommodate the reduction in deposits.  Banks’ reduced
4:98:6410:21:21:64:546:673:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:ability to absorb aggregate risk in financial crises results in a deterioration of risk sharing and
4:99:6509:21:21:64:546:652:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:higher macro-economic volatility.  The intermediary-driven dynamics arise in equilibrium since
4:100:6603:21:25:64:313:631:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:all aggregate shocks emerge from the real sector.
4:101:6652:25:21:75:547:606:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:The calibrated model matches many features of the data, both in terms of macro-economic
4:102:6739:21:21:64:546:585:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:quantities  and  prices.   It  matches  the  average  credit  spread  and  its  volatility.   Faced  with  a
4:103:6847:21:21:64:546:564:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:realistic corporate bond rate, firms choose the observed amount of leverage.  The non-financial
4:104:6942:21:21:64:546:543:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:leverage ratio is 37%, close to the U.S. data. The model delivers a 93% leverage ratio for financial
4:105:7042:21:21:64:546:522:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:firms, a key moment not directly targeted by the calibration, which is close to the data.  Debt
4:106:7137:21:21:64:546:501:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:is attractive to banks for four reasons.  First, debt enjoys a tax shield.  Second, the government
4:107:7235:21:21:64:546:480:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:guarantees the liabilities of the bank.  This guarantee captures not only deposit insurance but
4:108:7330:21:21:64:546:459:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f4:also broader too-big-to-fail guarantees to banks and the rest of the levered financial system.1
4:109:7425:21:20:64:546:438:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Third, banks face equity adjustment costs which increase the cost of equity relative to debt.
4:110:7518:20:21:64:546:418:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Fourth, banks provide a safe asset to patient households with a strong preference for holding
4:111:7611:21:21:64:546:397:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:such risk-free assets. While the first motive for debt financing also applies to non-financial firms,
4:112:7712:21:21:64:546:376:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:the other three do not.  The large wedge between financial and non-financial sector leverage is a
4:113:7809:21:21:64:546:355:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:key feature of many developed economies and crucial to understanding systemic risk in society.
4:114:7903:21:21:64:546:334:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:The equilibrium fully takes into account that the cost of bank debt changes endogenously with
4:115:7996:21:25:64:231:313:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:the safety of the financial sector.
4:116:8031:25:21:75:547:288:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Our  main  exercise  is  to  study  macro-prudential  policy  in  this  environment.   We  study  in-
4:117:8132:21:21:64:546:267:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:creasing the minimum bank equity capital requirement from its pre-crisis level of 6% of assets.
4:118:8227:21:21:64:546:246:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Higher capital requirements reduce financial fragility but at the cost of shrinking the economy
4:119:8322:21:21:64:546:225:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:and, in some cases, increasing macroeconomic volatility.  They are successful at reducing finan-
4:120:8418:21:21:64:546:204:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:cial leverage and the bank failure rate.  Banks that hold more equity capital become effectively
4:121:8514:21:21:64:546:183:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:more  risk  averse  and  stay  away  farther  from  their  regulatory  constraint.   They  also  become
4:122:8617:21:21:64:546:162:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:smaller,  shrinking  both  assets  and  liabilities.   The  charter  value  of  a  bank  shrinks  because
4:123:8722:21:18:64:546:141:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:banks with more onerous equity capital requirements have reduced ability to take advantage of
4:124:8815:18:15:78:546:123:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:1We use the labels intermediaries and banks interchangeably to mean the entire levered financial sector.  That
4:125:8925:15:12:64:546:108:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:sector also includes broker-dealers and insurance companies, which are subject to macro-prudential regulation
4:126:9034:12:12:64:546:96:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:and  enjoy  explicit  or  implicit  government  guarantees  on  their  liabilities.   Appendix  C.7  provides  a  detailed
4:127:9156:12:0:64:224:84:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:definition of our intermediary sector.
5:128:9195:0:25:64:169:715:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:the low cost of debt.
5:129:9216:25:21:75:547:690:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Corporate debt also becomes safer and loss rates fall.  Firms borrow less and reduce leverage.
5:130:9310:21:21:64:546:669:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Equilibrium  credit  spreads  are  higher  despite  a  reduction  in  loss  rates.   In  other  words,  the
5:131:9417:21:21:64:546:648:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:price of credit increases strongly with bank capital requirements since intermediaries are forced
5:132:9514:21:21:64:546:627:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:to move away from cheap deposit financing.  Higher credit spreads are consistent with lower
5:133:9605:21:25:64:178:606:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:non-financial leverage.
5:134:9628:25:21:75:547:581:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:The reduction in firm and bank bankruptcies is good news for the economy, as it frees up
5:135:9716:21:21:64:546:560:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:resources  otherwise  spent  on  deadweight  losses  from  bankruptcy.   However,  firms’  reduced
5:136:9814:21:21:64:546:539:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:ability to borrow from smaller banks reduces investment, the capital stock, and output.  The
5:137:9906:21:25:64:530:518:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:reduced size of the economy is the first adverse effect from tighter macro-prudential policy.
5:138:9999:25:21:75:547:493:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A  second  adverse  effect  is  that  macro-economic  volatility  rises,  locally,  with  tighter  bank
5:139:10102:21:21:64:546:472:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:capital  constraints.   Two  offsetting  effects  determine  macro  volatility.   First,  a  reduction  in
5:140:10208:21:21:64:546:451:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:financial fragility lowers macro-economic volatility.  Second, a reduction in risk sharing increases
5:141:10308:21:20:64:546:430:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:macro-economic  volatility.   The  latter  effect  dominates  the  former  as  minimum  bank  equity
5:142:10408:20:21:64:546:410:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:increases from 6% to 15% of assets, and macro-economic volatility increases.  Increasing bank
5:143:10501:21:21:64:546:389:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:equity  capital  further  gradually  lowers  volatility.   Loosening  capital  requirements  from  6%
5:144:10602:21:25:64:406:368:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:downward also increases volatility as the fragility effect dominates.
5:145:10671:25:21:75:547:343:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:To rank economies that differ in capital requirement, we calculate welfare for the two types of
5:146:10766:21:21:64:546:322:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:households in the model:  patient savers who invest in risk-free assets and impatient borrowers
5:147:10861:21:21:64:546:301:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:who are the equity holders of the non-financial and financial firms.  Tighter capital requirements
5:148:10959:21:21:64:546:280:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:redistribute wealth from savers to borrowers.  A smaller banking sector reduces deposits and
5:149:11051:21:21:64:546:259:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:thereby the wealth of the savers.  Borrower-equity holders receive a larger fraction of aggregate
5:150:11148:21:21:64:546:238:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:income as banks and firms shift their capital structure towards equity.  Thus, perversely, the
5:151:11242:21:21:64:546:217:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:owners of the banks gain from tighter regulation.  Depending on the aggregation scheme, welfare
5:152:11337:21:21:64:546:196:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:maximizing capital requirements are either slightly higher or slightly lower than the pre-crisis
5:153:11433:21:21:64:546:175:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:level.  A utilitarian social welfare function generates modest positive aggregate welfare gains
5:154:11528:21:21:64:546:154:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:from  tighter  bank  equity  capital  requirements,  with  gains  reaching  a  maximum  at  a  9%  eq-
5:155:11630:21:21:64:546:133:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:uity capital-asset ratio.  A tax-and-transfer scheme that induces Pareto improvements instead
5:156:11723:21:21:64:546:112:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:suggests that slightly looser capital requirements,  at 4%,  would be optimal.  Current capital
5:157:11818:21:21:64:546:91:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:requirement levels are straddled by these two numbers.  An alternative counter-cyclical capital
5:158:11913:21:0:64:546:70:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:requirement policy that tightens capital requirements in good times and relaxes them in times
6:159:12007:0:21:64:546:715:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:of financial stress allows for a larger financial sector and for improved risk sharing.  Out of the
6:160:12106:21:25:64:387:694:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:policies we evaluate, it admits the largest Pareto improvement.
6:161:12169:25:21:75:547:669:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Our  work  is  at  the  intersection  of  macro-economics,  asset  pricing,  corporate  finance,  and
6:162:12270:21:21:64:546:648:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:banking.   We  contribute  to  the  literature  on  the  role  of  credit  constraints  in  models  of  the
6:163:12377:21:21:64:546:627:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:macro-economy.  Building on early work that emphasized the importance of credit markets in
6:164:12467:21:21:64:546:606:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:amplifying business cycle shocks, notably Bernanke, Gertler, and Gilchrist (1996) and Kiyotaki
6:165:12561:21:21:64:546:585:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:and  Moore  (1997),  a  second  generation  of  models  has  explored  nonlinear  dynamics,  notably
6:166:12661:21:21:64:546:564:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Brunnermeier and Sannikov (2014) and He and Krishnamurthy (2013).  A first modeling con-
6:167:12749:21:21:64:546:543:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:tribution is to separate out the role of producers and banks, while the prior literature usually
6:168:12845:21:21:64:546:522:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:combines their roles.  Combining balance sheets implicitly assumes that financial intermediaries
6:169:12941:21:21:64:546:501:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:hold  equity  claims  in  productive  firms,  while  in  reality,  banks  hold  debt-like  claims.   These
6:170:13047:21:21:64:547:480:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:debt contracts are subject to default risk of the borrowers.2Intermediaries help to allocate risk
6:171:13144:21:21:64:546:459:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:between borrowers and savers, and their risk-bearing capacity is a key state variable.  The sep-
6:172:13240:21:20:64:546:438:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:aration of producers and intermediaries not only allows us to generate the large wedge between
6:173:13334:20:21:64:546:418:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:financial and non-financial leverage, it also activates a second financial accelerator in addition
6:174:13432:21:21:64:546:397:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:to the traditional financial accelerator mechanism.  Losses on corporate loans reduce intermedi-
6:175:13528:21:21:64:546:376:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:ary net worth, reduce banks’ ability and willingness to extend loans to producers, which hurts
6:176:13622:21:25:64:287:355:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:investment and output in the real economy.
6:177:13664:25:21:75:547:330:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:The second new model ingredient is to introduce the possibility of default for financial in-
6:178:13756:21:21:64:546:309:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:termediaries, with the government guaranteeing bank debt for savers (deposit insurance).  As
6:179:13848:21:21:64:546:288:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Reinhart and Rogoff (2009) and Jorda, Schularick, and Taylor (2014) make clear, financial in-
6:180:13941:21:21:64:546:267:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:termediaries frequently become insolvent.  When they do,  their creditors (mostly depositors)
6:181:14034:21:21:64:546:246:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:are typically bailed out by the government.  The combination of limited liability and govern-
6:182:14127:21:21:64:546:225:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:ment guarantees affects banks’ risk taking incentives and creates scope for regulation that limits
6:183:14225:21:18:64:547:204:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:bank leverage.3We model a Basel-style regulatory capital requirement that limits intermediary
6:184:14318:18:15:78:546:186:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:2It  is  well  understood  that  debt-like  contracts  arise  in  order  to  reduce  the  cost  of  gathering  information
6:185:14440:15:12:64:546:171:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:and to mitigate principal-agent problems.  See the costly state verification models in the tradition of Townsend
6:186:14552:12:12:64:546:159:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:(1979) and Gale and Hellwig (1985), and the work on the information insensitivity of debt by Dang, Gorton,
6:187:14658:12:12:64:546:147:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:and Holmstrom (2015).  Our debt is non-state contingent which confers the advantage that loan defaults induce
6:188:14767:12:12:64:546:135:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:losses for the intermediaries.  Costly state verification models also justify the existence of financial intermediaries
6:189:14886:12:12:64:546:123:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:who avoid the duplication of verification costs, as in Williamson (1987), Krasa and Villamil (1992), Diamond
6:190:14994:12:12:64:546:111:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:(1984).  Recent work by Klimenko,  Pfeil,  Rochet,  and Nicolo (2016),  Rampini and Viswanathan (2017),  and
6:191:15102:12:12:64:546:99:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:Gale and Gottardi (2017) also models intermediaries separately from producers.  The setting is simpler since
6:192:15210:12:8:64:262:87:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:their focus is theoretical; ours is quantitative.
6:193:15259:8:0:78:546:79:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:3See Kareken and Wallace (1978), Van den Heuvel (2008), Farhi and Tirole (2012), or Gomes, Grotteria, and
7:194:15365:0:21:64:546:715:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:liabilities to a certain fraction of their assets.  The minimum regulatory capital that banks must
7:195:15463:21:21:64:546:694:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:hold is the key macro-prudential policy parameter.  Banks optimally trade off the costs and
7:196:15554:21:21:64:546:673:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:benefits of default for their shareholders.  Our equilibrium features a counter-cyclical fraction
7:197:15651:21:21:64:546:652:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:of banks defaulting, consistent with the data.  In case of bank default, the government steps
7:198:15744:21:21:64:546:631:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:in, liquidates the bank’s assets and makes whole their creditors.  By allowing for the possibility
7:199:15842:21:21:64:546:610:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:of bank insolvencies, our model helps explain how a corporate default wave triggers financial
7:200:15935:21:21:64:546:589:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:fragility.  Intermediaries perform the traditional role of maturity and risk transformation.  Most
7:201:16033:21:21:64:547:568:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:models in the intermediary literature feature no default on corporate loans.4Those that do
7:202:16123:21:21:64:546:547:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:feature default employ short-term debt, abstracting from a key source of risk associated with
7:203:16216:21:21:64:546:526:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:financial intermediation.  Long-term debt allows us to realistically model liquidity-based default
7:204:16314:21:25:64:176:505:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:of non-financial firms.
7:205:16337:25:21:75:547:480:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:The third key model element is the inclusion of savers who do not participate in risky asset
7:206:16429:21:21:64:546:459:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:markets and the endogenous determination of safe asset rates.  The data reveal that a large
7:207:16520:21:20:64:546:438:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:fraction of households indeed do not participate in risky asset markets.  These savers are the
7:208:16614:20:21:64:546:418:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:marginal agents in the market for safe debt.  With risk averse savers and endogenous safe asset
7:209:16709:21:21:64:546:397:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:rates, the dynamics of the model change substantially.  In a crisis, intermediaries contract the
7:210:16805:21:21:64:546:376:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:size of their balance sheet, reducing the supply of safe assets.  This is only partially offset by
7:211:16903:21:21:64:546:355:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:an increase in government debt due to counter-cyclical fiscal policy.  To clear the market, the
7:212:16998:21:21:64:546:334:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:equilibrium  real  interest  rates  must  fall.   The  low  cost  of  debt  allows  the  intermediaries  to
7:213:17105:21:21:64:546:313:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:recapitalize more quickly,  dampening the effect of the crisis.  More generally,  a key question
7:214:17201:21:21:64:546:292:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:in  the  literature  is  how  tighter  bank  capital  regulation  affects  bank  profitability.   To  answer
7:215:17309:21:21:64:546:271:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:this question, one needs to understand how supply and demand in both major markets banks
7:216:17397:21:21:64:546:250:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:operate in, the loan market and the market for safe debt, respond in general equilibrium.  Our
7:217:17491:21:21:64:546:229:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:model endogenously determines supply, demand, and risk in both markets.  While the safe debt
7:218:17583:21:21:64:546:208:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:issued by banks is guaranteed by the government and therefore risk-free for savers,  it is not
7:219:17677:21:25:64:355:187:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:risk-free to society due to the possibility of bank default.
7:220:17737:25:21:75:547:162:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Our paper belongs to the literature on quantitative models of optimal bank regulation, includ-
7:221:17831:21:12:64:546:141:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:Wachter (2018).  Others justify the presence of bank leverage or net worth constraints by the ability of banks
7:222:17941:12:9:64:350:129:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:to divert cash flows, as in Gertler, Kiyotaki, and Queralto (2012).
7:223:18008:9:15:78:546:120:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:4For  example,  C ́urdia  and  Woodford  (2008),  Goodfriend  and  McCallum  (2007),  Meh  and  Moran  (2010),
7:224:18118:15:12:64:546:105:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:and Christiano, Motto, and Rostagno (2014).  A few exceptions are Gertler and Kiyotaki (2010), Angeloni and
7:225:18225:12:12:64:546:93:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:Faia (2013), Hirakata, Sudo, and Ueda (2013), Clerc, Derviz, Mendicino, Moyen, Nikolov, Stracca, Suarez, and
7:226:18333:12:0:64:226:81:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:Vardoulakis (2015), and Gete (2016).
8:227:18370:0:21:64:546:715:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:ing Van den Heuvel (2008), Nguyen (2015), Begenau (2016), Begenau and Landvoigt (2017),
8:228:18457:21:21:64:546:694:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Corbae and D’Erasmo (2017),  and Davydiuk (2017).  Relative to the previous literature,  we
8:229:18548:21:21:64:546:673:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:study a general equilibrium model that features severe financial recessions arising due to the
8:230:18642:21:21:64:546:652:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:nonlinear interaction of financial constraints in the production and intermediation sectors.  This
8:231:18740:21:21:64:546:631:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:allows us to quantify the benefit of preventing such financial crises using regulation.  A different
8:232:18840:21:21:64:546:610:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:branch of the normative literature instead studies the interactions between conventional and
8:233:18932:21:25:64:383:589:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f4:unconventional monetary policy and financial intermediation.5
8:234:18993:25:21:75:547:564:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Our work also contributes to the intermediary-based asset pricing literature.6The model fea-
8:235:19085:21:21:64:546:543:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:tures a market for long-term defaultable bonds and for short-term risk-free bonds.  It generates
8:236:19181:21:21:64:546:522:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:the unconditional credit spread, a puzzle in the asset pricing literature (Chen, 2010).  It also
8:237:19277:21:21:64:546:501:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:generates the volatility and counter-cyclicality of that spread, consistent with patterns docu-
8:238:19372:21:21:64:546:480:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:mented by Krishnamurthy and Muir (2017).  For the observed amount of credit risk, substantial
8:239:19465:21:21:64:546:459:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:variation in intermediary wealth generates a high enough price of credit risk.  The (shadow)
8:240:19557:21:20:64:546:438:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:stochastic discount factor of the intermediaries, driven by the intermediary net worth dynamics,
8:241:19653:20:25:64:222:418:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:is volatile and counter-cyclical.
8:242:19686:25:21:75:547:393:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:We also contribute to the literature on second-moment shocks to firm productivity, since a
8:243:19776:21:21:64:546:372:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:key shock in our model is an increase in the cross-sectional dispersion of firm-level productivity
8:244:19874:21:21:64:546:351:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:growth.7In our setup, these shocks cause costly firm defaults and intermediary losses, which
8:245:19966:21:21:64:546:330:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:in turn lead to lower credit supply and investment.  This is a complementary mechanism to
8:246:20055:21:21:64:546:309:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:the inaction effect of Bloom (2009), where increased uncertainty causes depressed investment
8:247:20147:21:21:64:546:288:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:because of fixed costs.  Alfaro, Bloom, and Lin (2016) study how financial frictions amplify the
8:248:20243:21:25:64:339:267:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:effect of uncertainty shocks on investment and hiring.
8:249:20297:25:18:75:547:242:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:More  broadly,  our  model  creates  room  for  macro-prudential  regulation  due  to  incomplete
8:250:20394:18:15:78:546:224:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:5See Gertler and Karadi (2011), Angeloni and Faia (2013), Drechsler, Savov, and Schnabl (2017b, 2017a),
8:251:20497:15:12:64:546:209:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:C ́urdia  and  Woodford  (2016),  Del  Negro,  Eggertsson,  Ferrero,  and  Kiyotaki  (2016),  Elenev  (2016),  and  De
8:252:20615:12:9:64:211:197:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:Fiore, Hoerova, and Uhlig (2017).
8:253:20648:9:15:78:546:188:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:6In addition to the work cited above, notable contributions are He and Krishnamurthy (2012, 2013, 2014),
8:254:20752:15:12:64:546:173:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:Gˆarleanu and Pedersen (2011), Adrian and Boyarchenko (2012), Maggiori (2013), and Moreira and Savov (2016).
8:255:20860:12:12:64:546:161:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:On the empirical side, He, Kelly, and Manela (2017) develop a risk factor which captures the systematic risk
8:256:20968:12:12:64:546:149:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:associated  with  declines  in  intermediary  equity  capital,  and  Adrian,  Etula,  and  Muir  (2014)  document  that
8:257:21087:12:9:64:414:137:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:intermediary leverage performs well in pricing the cross-section of stock returns.
8:258:21169:9:15:78:546:128:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:7The shock is calibrated from firm-level evidence in Bloom, Floetotto, Jaimovich, Saporta-Eksten, and Terry
8:259:21276:15:12:64:546:113:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:(2012).  Christiano, Motto, and Rostagno (2014) introduce a similar “risk” shock and argue it is an important
8:260:21385:12:12:64:546:101:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:driver of business cycle dynamics.  Jermann and Quadrini (2012) study how financial shocks affect balance sheet
8:261:21496:12:12:64:546:89:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:variables.  One interpretation of our uncertainty shocks is as aggregate misallocation shocks, as in Hsieh and
8:262:21606:12:0:64:527:77:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:Klenow (2009).  Ai, Li, and Yang (2016) study the role of intermediaries in reducing capital misallocation.
9:263:21714:0:21:64:546:715:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:markets  and  borrowing  constraints.8Our  model  is  set  up  to  study  imperfect  risk  sharing
9:264:21812:21:21:64:546:694:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:between borrower, saver, and intermediation sectors.  The only purpose of heterogeneity within
9:265:21906:21:25:64:513:673:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:the borrower sector and within the intermediary sector is to generate fractional default.
9:266:21995:25:21:75:547:648:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Finally, our paper contributes in its solution technique.  The model has two exogenous and
9:267:22085:21:21:64:546:627:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:persistent sources of aggregate risk and five endogenous aggregate state variables, which capture
9:268:22182:21:21:64:546:606:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:the wealth distribution.  It features default and occasionally binding borrowing constraints in
9:269:22277:21:21:64:546:585:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:both non-financial and financial sectors.  To solve this problem, we provide a nonlinear global
9:270:22372:21:21:64:546:564:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:solution  method.   The  algorithm,  detailed  in  computational  appendix  B,  solves  for  a  set  of
9:271:22475:21:25:64:505:543:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:nonlinear equations including the Euler, Kuhn-Tucker, and market clearing equations.
9:272:22559:25:21:75:547:518:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:The rest of the paper is organized as follows.  Section 2 discusses the model setup.  Section 3
9:273:22654:21:21:64:546:497:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:presents the calibration.  Section 4 contains the main results.  Section 5 uses the model to study
9:274:22752:21:21:64:546:476:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:various macro-prudential policies.  Section 6 concludes.  All model derivations, some details on
9:275:22848:21:53:64:510:455:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:the calibration, and some additional quantitative results are relegated to the appendix.
9:276:22936:53:42:64:186:402:17:g_d0_f2:17:g_d0_f2:2    The Model

9:298:23448:9:31:460:547:221:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f3:,(1)

9:301:23558:18:16:78:546:151:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:8Papers that have studied the qualitative role of these frictions in determining optimal policy are Lorenzoni
9:302:23667:16:11:64:546:135:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:(2008),  Mendoza (2010),  Korinek (2012),  Bianchi and Mendoza (2013),  Guerrieri and Lorenzoni (2015),  and
9:303:23775:11:0:64:151:124:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:Clerc et.  al.  (2015).
10:304:23799:0:21:64:547:715:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f3:TechnologyNon-financial firms, or firms for short, operate the production technology, which
10:305:23890:21:38:64:300:694:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:turns capital and labor into aggregate output:
10:306:23936:38:39:261:547:656:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f3:Yt=ZAtK1−αtLαt,(2)
10:307:23954:39:21:64:547:617:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:whereKtis capital,Ltis labor, andZAtis total factor productivity (TFP). Shocks toZAare
10:308:24040:21:21:64:546:596:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:the  first  source  of  aggregate  risk  in  the  model.   In  addition  to  the  technology  for  producing
10:309:24148:21:21:64:546:575:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:consumption goods, firms also have access to a technology that turns consumption into capital
10:310:24241:21:25:64:242:554:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:goods subject to adjustment costs.
10:311:24275:25:20:75:547:529:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Firms are funded by long-term corporate debt issued by intermediaries, and by equity pro-
10:312:24364:20:21:64:546:509:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:vided by borrower-entrepreneurs.  There are no frictions associated with changing the equity
10:313:24456:21:21:64:546:488:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:capital of non-financial firms.  This is equivalent to assuming that borrower-entrepreneurs hold
10:314:24552:21:25:64:226:467:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:the firms’ capital stock directly.
10:315:24586:25:21:75:547:442:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Financial intermediaries,  or banks for short,  are profit-maximizing firms that extend loans
10:316:24679:21:21:64:546:421:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:to non-financial firms.  They fund these loans through deposits that they issue to savers and
10:317:24772:21:21:64:546:400:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:equity capital that they raise from borrower-entrepreneurs.  Banks face equity issuance costs,
10:318:24866:21:25:64:353:379:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:an important financial friction described in detail below.
10:319:24924:25:21:75:547:354:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:We assume that savers only hold risk-free assets to capture the reality of limited participation
10:320:25020:21:21:64:546:333:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:in risky asset markets.  The provision of safe assets to savers is an important function of the
10:321:25115:21:21:64:547:312:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:intermediary sector.  Borrower-entrepreneurs and savers are endowed with ̄LBand ̄LSunits of
10:322:25206:21:25:64:518:291:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:labor, respectively.  Both types of households supply their labor endowment inelastically.
10:323:25296:25:21:75:547:266:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:As explained below, both firms and banks face idiosyncratic shocks.  This within-type het-
10:324:25386:21:21:64:546:245:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:erogeneity  allows  us  to  capture  fractional  default.   Perfect  within-type  risk  sharing  implies
10:325:25490:21:21:64:546:224:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:no further implications from within-type heterogeneity, and allows us to focus on incomplete
10:326:25582:21:25:64:203:203:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:risk-sharing between types.
10:327:25609:25:21:75:547:178:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Figure  1  illustrates  the  balance  sheets  of  the  model’s  agents  and  their  interactions.   Each
10:328:25713:21:21:64:546:157:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:agent’s  problem  depends  on  the  wealth  of  others;  the  entire  wealth  distribution  is  a  state
10:329:25817:21:20:64:546:136:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:variable.  Each agent must forecast how that state variable evolves, including the bankruptcy
10:330:25910:20:42:64:278:116:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:decisions of borrowers and intermediaries.

11:369:26791:21:31:94:493:213:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:owed to depositors, the government provides the shortfall (deposit insurance).

12:386:28133:47:32:64:350:391:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:2.3    Borrower-Entrepreneurs and Firms
12:387:28172:32:21:64:547:359:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:There is a unit-mass of identical borrower-entrepreneurs indexed byi.  The borrowers form a
12:388:28263:21:25:64:440:338:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:collective (“family”) that provides insurance against idiosyncratic shocks.
12:389:28338:25:21:75:547:313:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Each entrepreneur owns a technology, a firm, that creates consumption goodsYi,tfrom cap-
12:390:28426:21:21:64:547:292:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:italKi,tand  laborLi,t.   At  the  beginning  of  the  period,  each  firm  receives  an  idiosyncratic

12:394:28669:30:21:64:546:199:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Theωi,t-shocks are uncorrelated across firms and time.  However, the cross-sectional dispersion
12:395:28764:21:21:64:547:178:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:of theω-shocks varies over time; specifically,σω,tfollows a first-order Markov process.  Produc-
12:396:28860:21:21:64:546:157:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:tivity dispersion is the second exogenous source of aggregate risk in the model.  We refer to
12:397:28953:21:25:64:256:136:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:changes inσω,tas uncertainty shocks.
12:398:28989:25:21:75:547:111:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:While each individual entrepreneur manages her own firm’s production, the family manages
12:399:29077:21:21:64:546:90:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:the allocation of production inputs and consumption and issues debt to intermediaries.  Because
12:400:29172:21:0:64:546:69:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:all firms are identical at the start of each period, they are given the same capital, labor, and
13:401:29270:0:21:64:546:715:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:debt  allocation.   Corporate  debt  is  long-term,  modeled  as  perpetuity  bonds.   Bond  coupon
13:402:29369:21:21:64:546:694:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:payments decline geometrically,{1,δ,δ2,...}, whereδcaptures the duration of the bond.  We

13:405:29603:25:21:75:542:627:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f8:At  the  beginning  of  the  period,  the  family  jointly  holdsKBtunits  of  capital,  and  hasABt
13:406:29703:21:21:64:546:606:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:bonds outstanding.  Producers jointly hire their own labor and the labor of savers, denoted by

15:489:34309:46:33:64:202:315:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:2.4    Intermediaries
15:490:34330:33:33:64:139:282:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:2.4.1    Setup
15:491:34344:33:21:64:546:249:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Intermediaries (“banks”) are financial firms that buy long-term risky corporate debt issued by
15:492:34438:21:21:64:546:228:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:producers (AIt) and use this debt as collateral to issue short-term debt to savers (BIt).  They
15:493:34533:21:20:64:547:207:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:maximize the present discounted value of net dividend paymentsdItto their shareholders, the
15:494:34624:20:35:64:478:187:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:borrower-entrepreneurs.  There are two important frictions in the banking sector:
15:495:34705:35:21:79:547:152:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:1.  Moving equity into or out of banks is costly, i.e.  paying a (positive or negative) dividend
15:496:34801:21:21:94:546:131:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f3:dItis subject to a cost Σ(dIt) that is convex in deviation ofdItfrom a target level.  The
15:497:34890:21:19:94:455:110:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:total cost of paying out dividenddItisdIt+ Σ(dIt) for the intermediary.
15:498:34961:19:15:74:546:91:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:11The full model in the appendix adds a hard borrowing constraint for firms.  The model is calibrated so that
15:499:35070:15:0:64:503:76:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:this constraint is rarely binding; the constraint plays a minor role for the results.  See Appendix C.3.
16:500:35176:0:21:79:547:715:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:2.  Limited liability.  Intermediaries receive idiosyncratic profit shocks-It, realized at the time
16:501:35275:21:21:94:547:694:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:of dividend payouts.  The net dividend received by the shareholders isdIt−-It.  The profit
16:502:35365:21:21:94:547:673:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:shocks are i.i.d.  across banks and time with E(-It) = 0 and c.d.f.F-.12Intermediaries
16:503:35451:21:21:94:547:652:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:optimally decide to default on their liabilities.  Intermediary debt is guaranteed by the
16:504:35540:21:35:94:484:631:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:government (deposit insurance or TBTF guarantees) and therefore risk-free.
16:505:35614:35:21:75:547:596:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:The coupon payment on performing loans in the current period isAItΩA(ω∗t).  For firms that
16:506:35704:21:21:64:546:575:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:default and enter into foreclosure, banks repossess the firms, sell current period’s output, pay
16:507:35800:21:38:64:477:554:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:current period’s wages, and sell off the assets.  Payments on defaulted bonds are:
16:508:35882:38:0:64:126:516:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f3:Mt= (1−ζ)
16:509:35891:0:10:127:132:526:12:g_d0_f11:12:g_d0_f11:[

16:511:35941:0:10:425:430:526:12:g_d0_f11:12:g_d0_f11:]
16:512:35942:10:0:430:500:516:12:g_d0_f9:12:g_d0_f3:−(1−ΩA(ω∗t))

16:518:36035:25:20:75:547:443:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:At  the  beginning  of  the  period,  after  aggregate  and  idiosyncratic  productivity  shocks  are
16:519:36136:20:39:64:546:423:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:realized and a fraction 1−ΩA(ω∗t) of firms has defaulted, the wealth (net worth) of a bank is:

16:521:36268:38:21:64:543:346:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f8:Each  intermediary  optimally  decides  on  bankruptcy,  conditional  on  the  realization  ofWIt
16:522:36365:21:21:64:547:325:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:and the idiosyncratic profit shock-It.  Bankrupt intermediaries are liquidated by the govern-
16:523:36458:21:21:64:546:304:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:ment,  which redeems deposits at par value.  Immediately thereafter,  shareholders (borrower-
16:524:36551:21:21:64:546:283:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:entrepreneurs) replace all bankrupt intermediaries with new banks that receive initial equity
16:525:36644:21:21:64:547:262:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:equal to that of the non-defaulting banks,WIt.  This ensures that at the time of the dividend
16:526:36737:21:21:64:546:241:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:payout and portfolio decisions, all banks have identical wealth and face identical decision prob-
16:527:36834:21:21:64:546:220:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:lems.   In  appendix  A.2.1,  we  show  more  formally  that  given  our  assumptions,  the  problem
16:528:36934:21:25:64:397:199:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:reduces to that of a representative intermediary with wealthWIt.
16:529:36998:25:21:75:547:174:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:In addition to making loans, intermediaries can trade in short-term bonds with savers and the
16:530:37091:21:20:64:546:153:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:government.  They are allowed to take a short position in these bonds (issuing deposits), using
16:531:37186:20:18:64:546:133:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:their loans to borrower-entrepreneurs as collateral.  Intermediary debt is subject to a leverage
16:532:37282:18:16:74:546:115:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:12The idiosyncratic shocks to bank profitability capture unmodeled heterogeneity in bank portfolios, such as
16:533:37390:16:12:64:546:99:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:that resulting from differences in credit quality across banks’ loan portfolios or from differences in consumer
16:534:37501:12:12:64:546:87:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:lending.  Technically, the assumption guarantees that there is always a fraction of banks which defaults.  The
16:535:37611:12:0:64:466:75:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:shocks only affect the dividend payout, but have no effect on bank net worth going forward.
17:536:37704:0:21:64:118:715:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:constraint:
17:537:37715:21:31:257:547:694:12:g_d0_f9:12:g_d0_f3:−qftBIt≤ξqmtAIt+1.(11)
17:538:37737:31:20:64:546:663:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A  negative  position  in  the  short-term  bond  must  be  collateralized  by  banks’  loan  portfolio.
17:539:37841:20:21:64:546:643:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:The  parameterξdetermines  how  much  debt  can  be  issued  against  a  dollar  of  assets.   The
17:540:37939:21:21:64:546:622:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:constraint (11) is a Basel-style regulatory bank capital constraint.  The parameterξis the key
17:541:38033:21:21:64:546:601:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:macro-prudential policy parameter in the paper.  We have chosen to have market prices on the
17:542:38125:21:21:64:546:580:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:right-hand side of (11) because levered financial intermediaries face regulatory constraints that
17:543:38222:21:25:64:201:559:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f4:depend on market prices.13
17:544:38248:25:21:75:546:534:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Intermediaries are subject to corporate profit taxes at rateτIΠ.  Their profit for tax purposes
17:545:38343:21:38:64:367:513:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:is defined as the net interest income on their loan business:
17:546:38404:38:39:226:384:475:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f7:ΠIt= (1−θ)ΩA(ω∗t)AIt+rftBIt.
17:547:38432:39:21:64:547:436:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:They need to pay a deposit insurance feeκto the government that is proportional to the amount
17:548:38525:21:21:64:546:415:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:of short-term bonds they issue.  Banks’ leverage choice is affected by the same tax benefit and
17:549:38620:21:21:64:546:394:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:cost of distress trade-off faced by firms.  Additionally, banks enjoy deposit insurance, face costly
17:550:38720:21:41:64:382:373:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:equity issuance, and provide safe assets to patient households.

18:569:39518:0:21:64:546:715:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:the  regulatory  capital  constraint  (11),  and  the  definition  of  wealth  (10).   The  continuation

20:657:43636:39:21:64:546:337:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:The last equation is the economy’s resource constraint. It states that total output (GDP) equals

20:662:44017:47:33:64:155:207:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:2.7    Welfare
20:663:44031:33:21:64:547:174:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:In order to compare economies that differ in the policy parameter vector Θt, we must take a
20:664:44122:21:21:64:546:153:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:stance on how to weigh the two households, borrowers and savers.  We propose two different
20:665:44212:21:21:64:546:132:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:measures of aggregate welfare.  First, we compute an ex-post utilitarian social welfare function
20:666:44308:21:38:64:264:111:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:summing value functions of the agents:
20:667:44346:38:0:245:366:73:12:g_d0_f9:12:g_d0_f7:Wpopt(·; Θt) =VBt+VSt,

21:669:44464:21:25:64:447:694:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:already incorporate the mass of agents of each type (population shares`i).
21:670:44538:25:21:75:547:669:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Second, we compute an ex-ante measure of welfare based on compensating variation similar
21:671:44626:21:21:64:547:648:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:to Alvarez and Jermann (2005).  Consider the equilibrium of two different economiesk= 0,1,

21:673:44808:21:21:64:547:606:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:agentjin economykby ̄Vj,k=  E0[Vj1(·; Θk)].  Denote the time-0 price of the consumption
21:674:44895:21:38:64:245:585:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:stream of agentjin economykby:
21:675:44925:38:0:235:280:547:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f4: ̄Pj,k= E0

21:682:44959:45:21:64:547:499:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:whereMj,kt,t+1is the SDF of agentjin economyk.  The percentage welfare gain for agentjfrom
21:683:45049:21:38:64:392:478:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:living in economy Θ1relative to economy Θ0, in expectation, is:
21:684:45112:38:0:263:299:440:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:∆ ̄Vj=

21:687:45133:32:21:64:546:402:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Since the value functions are expressed in consumption units,  we can multiply these welfare
21:688:45225:21:39:64:498:381:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:gains with the time-0 prices of consumption streams in the Θ0economy and add up:
21:689:45305:39:38:228:383:342:12:g_d0_f9:12:g_d0_f7:Wcev= ∆ ̄VB ̄PB,0+ ∆ ̄VS ̄PS,0.
21:690:45336:38:21:64:546:304:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:This measure is the minimum one-time wealth transfer in the Θ0economy (the benchmark)
21:691:45421:21:21:64:547:283:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:required  to  make  agents  at  least  as  well  off  as  in  the  Θ1economy  (the  alternative).   If  this
21:692:45529:21:21:64:546:262:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:number is positive, a transfer scheme can be implemented to make the alternative economy a
21:693:45619:21:21:64:546:241:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Pareto improvement.  If this number is negative, such a scheme cannot be implemented because
21:694:45711:21:25:64:487:220:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:it would require a bigger transfer to one agent than the other is willing to give up.
21:695:45796:25:21:75:547:195:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:We  solve  the  model  using  projection-based  numerical  methods  and  provide  a  detailed  de-
21:696:45894:21:0:64:370:174:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:scription of the globally nonlinear algorithm in appendix B.
22:697:45956:0:37:64:189:715:17:g_d0_f2:17:g_d0_f2:3    Calibration
22:698:45972:37:21:64:546:678:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:The model is calibrated at annual frequency.  The parameters of the model and their targets
22:699:46063:21:21:64:546:657:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:are  summarized  in  Table  1.   Appendix  C.1  conducts  a  parameter  sensitivity  analysis  of  the
22:700:46165:21:21:64:546:636:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:type suggested by Andrews, Gentzkow, and Shapiro (2017) that helps clarify what moments
22:701:46252:21:42:64:259:615:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:structurally identify what parameters.
22:702:46290:42:20:64:542:573:12:g_d0_f2:8:g_d0_f8:Aggregate  ProductivityFollowing  the  macro-economics  literature,  the  TFP  processZAt
22:703:46379:20:21:64:547:553:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:follows an AR(1) in logs with persistence parameterρAand innovation volatilityσA.  Because
22:704:46469:21:21:64:546:532:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:TFP is persistent, it becomes a state variable.  We discretizeZAtinto a 5-state Markov chain
22:705:46561:21:21:64:546:511:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:using  the  Rouwenhorst  (1995)  method.   The  procedure  chooses  the  productivity  grid  points
22:706:46660:21:21:64:546:490:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:and the transition probabilities between them to match the volatility and persistence of HP-
22:707:46752:21:21:64:546:469:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:detrended GDP. GDP is endogenously determined but heavily influenced by TFP. Consistent
22:708:46839:21:21:64:546:448:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:with the model, our measurement of GDP excludes net exports and government investment.
22:709:46925:21:21:64:546:427:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:We define the GDP deflator correspondingly.  Observed real per capita HP-detrended GDP has
22:710:47015:21:21:64:546:406:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:a volatility of 2.53% and its persistence is 0.55.  The model generates a volatility of 2.43% and
22:711:47112:21:42:64:171:385:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:a persistence of 0.55.
22:712:47134:42:21:64:546:343:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f3:Idiosyncratic  ProductivityWe  calibrate  the  firm-level  productivity  risk  directly  to  the
22:713:47230:21:21:64:547:322:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:micro  evidence.   We  normalize  the  mean  of  idiosyncratic  productivity  atμω=  1.   We  let
22:714:47327:21:21:64:547:301:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:the cross-sectional standard deviation of idiosyncratic productivity shocksσt,ωfollow a 2-state
22:715:47422:21:20:64:547:280:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Markov  chain,  with  four  parameters.   Fluctuations  inσt,ωgovern  aggregate  corporate  credit
22:716:47520:20:21:64:547:260:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:risk  since  high  levels  ofσt,ωcause  a  larger  left  tail  of  low-productivity  firms  to  default  in
22:717:47627:21:21:64:546:239:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:equilibrium.   We  refer  to  periods  in  the  highσt,ωstate  ashigh uncertaintyperiods.   We  set
22:718:47726:21:21:64:547:218:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:(σL,ω,σH,ω)  =  (0.095,0.175).   The  value  forσL,ωtargets  the  unconditional  mean  corporate
22:719:47822:21:21:64:547:197:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:default  rate.   The  model-implied  average  default  rate  of  2.2%  is  similar  to  the  data.14The
22:720:47925:21:21:64:547:176:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:high value,σH,ω, is chosen to match the time-series standard deviation of the cross-sectional
22:721:48018:21:18:64:546:155:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:interquartile range of firm productivity, which is 4.9% according to Bloom, Floetotto, Jaimovich,
22:722:48115:18:16:74:546:137:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:14We look at two sources of data:  corporate loans and corporate bonds.  From the Federal Reserve Board
22:723:48218:16:12:64:546:121:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:of Governors, we obtain delinquency and charge-off rates on Commercial and Industrial loans and Commercial
22:724:48324:12:12:64:546:109:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:Real Estate loans by U.S. Commercial Banks for the period 1991-2015.  The average delinquency rate is 3.1%.
22:725:48431:12:11:64:546:97:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:The second source of data is Standard & Poors’ default rates on publicly-rated corporate bonds for 1981-2014.
22:726:48540:11:12:64:546:86:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:The average default rate is 1.5%; 0.1% on investment-grade bonds and 4.1% on high-yield bonds.  The model is
22:727:48648:12:0:64:188:74:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:in between these two values.
23:728:48678:0:21:64:546:715:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Saporta-Eksten, and Terry (2012) (their Table 6).  The transition probabilities from the low to
23:729:48773:21:21:64:546:694:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:the high uncertainty state of 9% and from the high to the low state of 20% are also taken directly
23:730:48871:21:21:64:547:673:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:from Bloom et al.  (2012).15The model spends 31% of periods in the high uncertainty regime.
23:731:48962:21:21:64:546:652:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Like in Bloom et al., our uncertainty process is independent of the first-moment shocks.  About
23:732:49057:21:21:64:546:631:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:10% of periods feature both high uncertainty and low TFP realizations.  We will refer to those
23:733:49151:21:21:64:546:610:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:periods as financial recessions or financial crises, since those periods will feature (endogenous)
23:734:49249:21:21:64:546:589:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:financial fragility in the equilibrium of the model. Using a long time series for the U.S., Reinhart
23:735:49349:21:41:64:402:568:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:and Rogoff (2009) find the same 10% frequency of financial crises.
23:736:49415:41:21:64:547:527:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f3:ProductionAdjustment costs are quadratic.  We set the marginal adjustment cost parameter
23:737:49503:21:21:64:547:506:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f3:ψ= 2 in order to match the observed volatility of the ratio of investment to GDP,X/Y, of
23:738:49591:21:21:64:546:485:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:1.58%.  The model generates a value of 1.56%.  The adjustment costs on average amount to
23:739:49679:21:21:64:547:464:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:0.04% of GDP. We set the parameterαin the Cobb-Douglas production function equal to 0.71,
23:740:49768:21:21:64:546:443:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:which  yields  an  overall  labor  income  share  of  65%,  the  standard  value  in  the  business  cycle
23:741:49874:21:21:64:546:422:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:literature.  We choose an annual depreciation of capitalδKof 8% to match the investment-to-
23:742:49965:21:41:64:277:401:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:output ratio of 18% observed in the data.
23:743:50006:41:21:64:547:360:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f3:Population and Labor Income SharesTo pin down the population shares of our two dif-
23:744:50089:21:21:64:546:339:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:ferent types of households we turn to the Survey of Consumer Finance (SCF). We use all survey
23:745:50182:21:21:64:546:318:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:waves from 1995 until 2013 and average across them.  We compute for each SCF household the
23:746:50272:21:21:64:546:297:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:share of assets (excluding real estate) held in stocks or private business equity, considering both
23:747:50371:21:21:64:546:276:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:direct and indirect holdings of stock.  Using this definition of the risky share, we then calculate
23:748:50470:21:21:64:546:255:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:the fraction of households whose risky share is less than one percent.  This amounts to 69%
23:749:50561:21:21:64:547:234:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:of  SCF  households.   These  are  the  savers  in  our  model  who  hold  only  safe  assets  (`S).   The
23:750:50667:21:21:64:546:213:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:remaining`B= 31% of households have a nontrivial risky asset share.  The labor income share
23:751:50758:21:21:64:546:192:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:of savers in the SCF is 60%.  The income share of the borrower-entrepreneurs is the remaining
23:752:50851:21:41:64:460:171:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:40%.  The income shares determine the Cobb-Douglas parametersγBandγS.
23:753:50920:41:21:64:547:130:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f3:Corporate LoansIn the model,  a corporate loan is a geometric bond.  The issuer of one
23:754:51006:21:17:64:547:109:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:unit of the bond at timetpromises to pay 1 at timet+ 1,δat timet+ 2,δ2at timet+ 3, and
23:755:51092:17:16:74:546:92:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:15They estimate a two-state Markov chain for the cross-sectional standard deviation of establishment-level
23:756:51198:16:12:64:546:76:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:productivity using annual data for 1972-2010 from the Census of Manufactures and Annual Survey of Manufac-
23:757:51304:12:0:64:349:64:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:tures.  We annualize their quarterly transition probability matrix.

25:797:53493:0:21:64:547:715:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:so on.  Given that the present value of all payments (1/(1−δ)) can be thought of as the sum
25:798:53584:21:21:64:547:694:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:of a principal (shareθ) and an interest component (share 1−θ), we define the book value of
25:799:53674:21:21:64:546:673:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:the debt asF=θ/(1−δ).  We setδ= 0.937 andθ= 0.582 (F= 9.238) to match the observed
25:800:53756:21:21:64:546:652:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:duration of corporate bonds.  Appendix C.2 contains the details.  The model’s corporate loans
25:801:53849:21:25:64:268:631:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:have a duration of 6.8 years on average.
25:802:53889:25:21:75:547:606:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:We set the bankruptcy cost parameterζ= 0.6 to match the observed average severity rate
25:803:53975:21:21:64:546:585:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:of 44% on corporate bonds rated by S&P and Moody’s rated during 1985-2004.  The model
25:804:54060:21:21:64:546:564:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:produces a similar unconditional loss-given-default rate of 43%.  Combined with the average
25:805:54151:21:21:64:546:543:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:default rate,  this LGD number implies a loss rate on corporate loans of 1.0%.  Our baseline
25:806:54243:21:25:64:506:522:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:model generates a modest quantity of corporate default risk, consistent with the data.
25:807:54329:25:21:75:547:497:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A fractionηof the cost of distress to intermediaries is a deadweight loss to the economy.  The
25:808:54423:21:21:64:547:476:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:remainder 1−ηis transfer income that enters in the budget constraint of the agents.  We set
25:809:54514:21:21:64:546:455:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f3:η= 0.2 based on evidence in Bris, Welch, and Zhu (2006) showing that firms loose on average
25:810:54605:21:24:64:432:434:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:20% of assets between the beginning and end of a Chapter 7 procedure.
25:811:54674:24:21:75:547:410:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:We set the profit default threshold toπ= 0.04 to target average non-financial leverage.  The
25:812:54766:21:21:64:546:389:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:higher  this  threshold,  the  more  firms  will  default  on  average  for  a  given  level  of  firm  debt.
25:813:54875:21:21:64:547:368:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Since  defaults  are  costly  to  the  borrower  family,  borrower  leverage  is  decreasing  inπ.   The
25:814:54979:21:21:64:546:347:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:model generates a ratio of borrower book debt-to-assets of 36%.  In the Flow of Funds data,
25:815:55070:21:21:64:546:326:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:the average ratio of loans and debt securities of the nonfinancial corporate and non-financial
25:816:55164:21:42:64:376:305:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:non-corporate businesses to their non-financial assets is 37%.
25:817:55226:42:21:64:546:263:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f3:Intermediary  ParametersThe  intermediary  profit  shocks  are  distributed  Gaussian  with
25:818:55317:21:21:64:547:242:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:mean zero.  The cross-sectional standard deviationσ-= Var(-It)0.5governs the average inter-
25:819:55408:21:21:64:547:221:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:mediary failure rate.  The benchmark model withσ-=.025 generates an average failure rate of
25:820:55499:21:21:64:546:200:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:0.54%, which is exactly the asset-weighted failure rate of depository institutions in the FDIC
25:821:55593:21:25:64:90:179:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:data.
25:822:55598:25:38:75:518:154:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:We adopt the following functional form for the dividend payout cost of intermediaries:
25:823:55684:38:0:252:293:116:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Σ(dIt) =
25:824:55692:0:16:297:308:124:12:g_d0_f7:8:g_d0_f8:σI
25:825:55694:16:0:300:306:108:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:2
25:826:55695:0:38:310:359:116:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f7:(dIt− ̄d)2,
25:827:55706:38:0:64:546:78:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:The marginal dividend payout cost for intermediaries is set toσI=  5 to match the average
26:828:55797:0:21:64:546:715:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:credit spread.  The higherσI,  the more costly it becomes for intermediaries to deviate from
26:829:55889:21:21:64:547:694:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:their  dividend  target ̄d.   We  set  the  target  to  the  dividend  level  in  the  deterministic  steady
26:830:55997:21:21:64:546:673:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:state of the model.  A higher adjustment cost causes a higher risk premium in the corporate
26:831:56088:21:21:64:546:652:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:loan  market  and  thus  increases  the  credit  spread.   We  define  the  credit  spread  in  the  data
26:832:56193:21:21:64:546:631:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:as a weighted average of the Moody’s Aaa and Baa yields and subtract the one-year constant
26:833:56283:21:21:64:546:610:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:maturity Treasury rate.  To determine the portfolio weights on the Aaa versus Baa grade bonds,
26:834:56377:21:21:64:546:589:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:we use market values of the amounts outstanding from Barclays.  The weights are 80% and 20%,
26:835:56469:21:21:64:546:568:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:respectively.  The mean spread over the 1953-2015 period is 2.08%, while the model generates
26:836:56561:21:25:64:189:547:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:a mean spread of 2.05%.
26:837:56584:25:21:75:547:522:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:The intermediary borrowing constraint parameterξcan be interpreted as a minimum reg-
26:838:56668:21:21:64:546:501:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:ulatory equity capital requirement.  Under Basel II and III, corporate loans have a 100% risk
26:839:56761:21:21:64:546:480:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:weight and corporate bonds have a risk weight that depends on their credit rating.  The risk
26:840:56853:21:21:64:546:459:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:weight on corporate bonds under the standardized approach of Basel II ranges from 20% for
26:841:56942:21:20:64:546:438:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:AAA  to  AA-,  50%  for  A+  to  A-,  to  100%  for  BBB+  to  B-.   A  blended  regulatory  capital
26:842:57042:20:21:64:546:418:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:requirement of 6% (8% times a blended risk weight of 75%) seems appropriate given the assets
26:843:57134:21:21:64:547:397:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:of the levered financial sector.16This implies thatξ= 0.94.  This is the key parameter we vary
26:844:57228:21:25:64:283:376:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:in or macro-prudential policy experiments.
26:845:57270:25:21:75:547:351:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:We set the deposit insurance fee parameterκto 8.4 basis points.  To compute this number,
26:846:57358:21:21:64:546:330:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:we  divide  the  total  assessment  revenue  reported  by  the  FDIC  for  2016,  $10  billion,  by  the
26:847:57462:21:21:64:546:309:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:total short-term debt of U.S. chartered financial institutions from the Flow of Funds, $11,849
26:848:57556:21:42:64:107:288:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f4:billion.17
26:849:57566:42:21:64:548:246:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f3:Preference ParametersPreference parameters affect many equilibrium quantities and prices
26:850:57654:21:21:64:546:225:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:simultaneously, and are harder to pin down directly by data.  For simplicity, we assume that
26:851:57746:21:21:64:547:204:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:both borrowers and savers have log utility:σB=νB= 1 andσS=νS= 1.18The subjective
26:852:57826:21:17:64:547:183:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:time discount factor of borrowersβB= 0.931 targets the capital-to-GDP ratio, as it governs
26:853:57916:17:16:74:546:166:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:16Corporate  loans  are  $7.6  trillion  and  corporate  bonds  are  $5.1  trillion  as  of  2016  year-end.   Given  the
26:854:58037:16:12:64:546:150:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:observed 40%-40%-20% split of corporate bonds in the three ratings categories (reflecting the same 80-20 split
26:855:58147:12:12:64:546:138:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:between investment grade and high yield bonds from Barclays), the risk weight for corporate bonds is 48%, and
26:856:58256:12:8:64:195:126:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:the overall risk weight is 79%.
26:857:58287:8:16:74:546:118:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:17Banks pay 14.2 cents per $100 dollar of insured deposits but 8.4 cents per $100 of insured and uninsured
26:858:58393:16:8:64:407:102:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:deposits.  Since the model has only insured deposits, we use the latter number.
26:859:58472:8:16:74:546:94:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:18We  have  solved  the  model  for  Epstein-Zin  preferences  with  a  range  of  risk  aversion  and  EIS  parameter
26:860:58590:16:0:64:363:78:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:choices.  Results are qualitatively similar and available upon request.
27:861:58663:0:21:64:546:715:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:borrowers’ desire to accumulate wealth.  The capital-to-output ratio is 2.25 in the model, and
27:862:58757:21:21:64:546:694:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:2.24 in the data.  The time discount factor of the saver disproportionately affects the mean of
27:863:58852:21:21:64:546:673:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:the short-term interest rate.  We setβS= 0.982 to generate a low average real rate of interest
27:864:58946:21:42:64:105:652:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:of 2.2%.
27:865:58954:42:21:64:547:610:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f3:Government  ParametersTo  add  quantitative  realism  to  the  model,  we  match  both  the
27:866:59045:21:21:64:546:589:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:unconditional average and cyclical properties of discretionary spending, transfer spending, labor
27:867:59142:21:25:64:347:568:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:income tax revenue, and corporate income tax revenue.
27:868:59195:25:21:75:547:543:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Discretionary and transfer spending as a fraction of GDP are modeled as follows:Git/Yt=
27:869:59282:21:20:64:547:522:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f3:Giexp{bi(gt− ̄g)},i=o,T.   The  scalarsGoandGTare  set  to  match  the  observed  average
27:870:59371:20:21:64:546:502:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:discretionary spending to GDP of 17.58% and transfer spending to GDP of 3.18%, respectively,
27:871:59463:21:21:64:547:481:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:in the 1953-2014 NIPA data.19The model produces 17.56% and 3.19%.  We setbo=−2.5 and
27:872:59547:21:21:64:547:460:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f3:bT=−25 in order to match the slope in a regression of log discretionary/transfer spending-to-
27:873:59640:21:21:64:546:439:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:GDP on GDP growth and a constant.  We match these slopes:  -0.75 and -7.26 in the model
27:874:59727:21:25:64:294:418:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:versus -0.71 and -7.14 in the 1953-2014 data.
27:875:59772:25:21:75:547:393:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Similarly, we model the labor income tax rate asτt=τexp{bτ(gt− ̄g)}.  We set the tax rate
27:876:59861:21:21:64:546:372:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f3:τ= 29.5% in order to match observed average income tax revenue to GDP of 17.3%.  Appendix
27:877:59950:21:21:64:546:351:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:C.4 details how labor income tax revenue is computed in the data.  The model generates an
27:878:60039:21:21:64:546:330:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:average of 18.6%.  We set the sensitivity of the tax rate to aggregate productivity growthbτ= 2
27:879:60134:21:21:64:546:309:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:to  match  the  observed  sensitivity  of  log  income  tax  revenue  to  GDP  to  GDP  growth.   The
27:880:60235:21:21:64:546:288:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:regression slope of log income tax revenue to GDP on GDP growth and a constant produces
27:881:60322:21:25:64:383:267:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:similar pro-cyclicality:  0.86 in the model and 0.70 in the data.
27:882:60387:25:21:75:547:242:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Fourth, we set the corporate tax rate that both financial and non-financial corporations pay
27:883:60479:21:21:64:547:221:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:to a constantτBΠ=τIΠ= 20% to match observed corporate tax revenues of 3.41% of GDP. The
27:884:60566:21:21:64:546:200:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:model generates an average of 3.62%.  The tax shield of debt and depreciation that firms and
27:885:60658:21:21:64:546:179:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:banks  enjoy  in  the  model  substantially  reduces  the  effective  tax  rate  corporations  pay,  both
27:886:60763:21:21:64:546:158:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:in the model and in the data.  We set the tax rate on financial income for savers (interest on
27:887:60857:21:24:64:537:137:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:short-term debt) equal toτD= 13.2%.  Appendix C.5 contains the details of the calculation.
27:888:60947:24:18:75:547:113:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Government debt to GDP averages 60% of GDP in a long simulation of the benchmark model.
27:889:61034:18:16:74:547:95:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:19We divide by exp{bi/2σ2g/(1−ρ2g)(bi−1)},  a Jensen correction,  to ensure that average spending means
27:890:61137:16:0:64:144:79:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:match the targets.
28:891:61157:0:21:64:546:715:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:While it fluctuates meaningfully over prolonged periods of time (standard deviation of 50%),
28:892:61249:21:54:64:500:694:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:the government debt to GDP ratio remains stationary as explained in Appendix C.6.
28:893:61330:54:37:64:155:640:17:g_d0_f2:17:g_d0_f2:4    Results
28:894:61342:37:21:64:546:603:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:This section studies the behavior of key macro-economic and balance sheet variables. The model
28:895:61436:21:21:64:546:582:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:captures important features of macro-economic quantities, corporate and bank balance sheets,
28:896:61528:21:21:64:546:561:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:and asset prices in normal times and in crises.  The benchmark model’s fit lends credibility to
28:897:61623:21:46:64:339:540:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:the macro-prudential policy experiments in Section 5.
28:898:61676:46:33:64:224:494:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:4.1    Macro Quantities
28:899:61699:33:21:64:546:461:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:We report means and standard deviations from a long simulation of the model (10,000 years),
28:900:61790:21:21:64:547:440:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:as well as averages conditional on being in a good state (high TFP, low uncertainty, i.e.σω,L),
28:901:61885:21:21:64:546:419:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:non-financial  recession  (low  TFP,  low  uncertainty),  and  financial  recession  (low  TFP,  high
28:902:61986:21:25:64:157:398:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:uncertaintyσω,H).
28:903:62003:25:21:75:547:373:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Table 2 reports the standard deviation of aggregate quantities, their correlation with GDP,
28:904:62094:21:21:64:546:352:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:and their autocorrelation.  Moments in the data are computed from HP-detrended log series.
28:905:62184:21:21:64:546:331:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Moments in the model are by assumption stationary, and are also computed from log series.
28:906:62273:21:21:64:546:310:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:The model matches the volatility of GDP and it autocorrelation.  TFP shocks with 2% volatility
28:907:62367:21:20:64:546:289:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:are amplified and lead to 2.43% GDP volatility.  The model further matches the volatility of
28:908:62459:20:21:64:546:269:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:the investment to GDP ratio and the investment rate.  The latter series display modest pro-
28:909:62550:21:21:64:546:248:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:cyclicality in both data and model.  Investment rates are insufficiently persistent in the model.
28:910:62647:21:21:64:546:227:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:The model somewhat overstates consumption volatility.  Consumption in the model exhibits
28:911:62735:21:21:64:546:206:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:the right cyclicality, but is slightly too persistent relative to the data.  We return to the source
28:912:62835:21:25:64:317:185:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:of the consumption volatility in the model below.
28:913:62884:25:21:75:547:160:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:We  present  impulse-response  graphs  to  explore  the  behavior  of  macro-economic  quantities
28:914:62981:21:21:64:546:139:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:conditional  on  the  state  of  the  economy.   We  start  off  the  model  in  year  0  in  the  average
28:915:63087:21:21:64:546:118:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:TFP state (the middle of the five points on the TFP grid) and in the low uncertainty state
28:916:63177:21:21:64:547:97:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:(σω,L).   The  five  endogenous  state  variables  are  at  their  ergodic  averages.   In  period  1,  the
28:917:63284:21:0:64:546:76:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:model undergoes a change to a lower TFP grid point.  In one case (red line), the recession is
29:918:63379:0:25:154:456:717:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Table 2:  Unconditional Macroeconomic Quantity Moments
29:919:63433:25:14:243:415:692:11:g_d0_f20:11:g_d0_f20:DataModel

29:921:63488:13:14:149:462:665:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:GDP2.53%1.00    0.552.43%1.00    0.55
29:922:63525:14:14:149:462:651:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:CONS    1.75%0.88    0.422.43%0.87    0.60
29:923:63567:14:13:149:462:637:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:X/Y1.58%0.73    0.571.56%0.55    0.18
29:924:63604:13:36:149:462:624:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:X/K0.82%0.63    0.720.81%0.60    0.21
29:925:63641:36:21:64:547:588:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:accompanied  by  a  switch  to  the  high  uncertainty  state  (σω,H);  a  financial  recession.   In  the
29:926:63747:21:21:64:546:567:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:second case, the economy remains in the low uncertainty state; a non-financial recession (blue
29:927:63841:21:21:64:546:546:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:line).  From period 2 onwards, the two exogenous state variables follow their stochastic laws of
29:928:63937:21:21:64:546:525:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:motion.  For comparison, we also show a series that does not undergo any shock in period 1 but
29:929:64031:21:21:64:546:504:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:where the exogenous states stochastically mean revert from the low-uncertainty state in period
29:930:64125:21:21:64:546:483:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:0 (black line).  For each of the three scenarios,  we simulate 10,000 sample paths of 25 years
29:931:64219:21:21:64:546:462:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:and average across them.  Figure 2 plots the macro-economic quantities.  The top left panel is
29:932:64313:21:21:64:547:441:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:for the productivity levelZA.  By construction,  it falls by the same amount in financial and
29:933:64406:21:21:64:546:420:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:non-financial recessions;  a 2% drop.  Productivity then gradually mean reverts over the next
29:934:64499:21:25:64:546:399:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:decade.  The black line shows how productivity would have evolved absent a shock in period 1.
29:935:64592:25:21:75:547:374:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:The other three panels show impulse-responses for output, consumption, and investment.  In
29:936:64682:21:21:64:546:353:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:the initial period of the shock, the drop in output is the same when the economy is additionally
29:937:64778:21:21:64:546:332:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:hit by an uncertainty shock (red line) and when it is not (blue line).  This has to be the case
29:938:64873:21:21:64:546:311:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:because capital is a state variable, labor is supplied inelastically, and productivity is identical.
29:939:64973:21:21:64:546:290:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:In  financial  recessions,  the  economy  suffers  from  a  second  period  of  decline  in  consumption,
29:940:65078:21:21:64:546:269:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:despite the rebound in productivity.  Output remains lower for longer in a financial recession.
29:941:65173:21:21:64:546:248:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:The added persistence resembles the slow recovery that typically follows a financial crisis.  The
29:942:65270:21:20:64:546:227:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:bottom  right  panel  shows  a  28%  drop  in  investment  in  financial  recessions  but  only  a  mod-
29:943:65374:20:21:64:546:207:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:est drop in non-financial recessions.  Despite the bounce back in period 2, investment remains
29:944:65468:21:21:64:546:186:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:depressed for a prolonged period of time.  Aggregate consumption partially offsets the initial
29:945:65562:21:21:64:546:165:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:decline in investment in a financial recession:  the initial drop in consumption is smaller than in
29:946:65661:21:21:64:546:144:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:a non-financial recession.  The low rate of return on savings induces the saver to consume more
29:947:65756:21:18:64:547:123:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:in a financial crisis.20Consumption drops subsequently and remains below the non-financial
29:948:65846:18:16:74:546:105:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:20Since output in the first period is by construction identical for both types of recessions, the approximately
29:949:65957:16:12:64:546:89:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:2.5% of output that are not reflected in consumption and investment in a financial recession are accounted for
29:950:66067:12:0:64:338:77:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:by deadweight losses from firm and intermediary bankruptcies.
