30:978:66364:147:12:64:546:398:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:The graphs show the average path of the economy through a recession episode which starts at time 1.  In period
30:979:66474:12:12:64:546:386:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:0,  the economy is in the average TFP state.  The recession is either accompanied by high uncertainty (high
30:980:66581:12:12:64:547:374:10:g_d0_f18:10:g_d0_f6:σω), a financial recession plotted in red, or low uncertainty (lowσω), a non-financial recession plotted in blue.
30:981:66694:12:12:64:546:362:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:From period 2 onwards, the economy evolves according to its regular probability laws.  The black line plots the
30:982:66805:12:12:64:546:350:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:dynamics of the economy absent any shock in period 1.  We obtain the three lines via a Monte Carlo simulation
30:983:66914:12:12:64:547:338:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f20:of 10,000 paths of 25 periods, and averaging across these paths.Blue line:non-financial recession,Red line:
30:984:67021:12:35:64:251:326:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:financial recession,Black line:no shocks.
30:985:67062:35:21:64:546:291:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:recession level for the remaining periods, as the capital stock remains depressed.  It is these pro-
30:986:67162:21:21:64:546:270:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:tracted declines in consumption and investment in financial recessions that macro-prudential
30:987:67254:21:21:64:546:249:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:policy aims to remedy.  In appendix D.1, we include IRF graphs that compare a financial reces-
30:988:67348:21:21:64:547:228:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:sion to a pure uncertainty shock, which is a switch toσω,Hwith TFP remaining constant.  This
30:989:67440:21:21:64:546:207:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:comparison demonstrates that the combination of both shocks leads to significant amplification,
30:990:67535:21:21:64:546:186:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:i.e.,  the financial recession triggered by the combination is much larger than the sum of the
30:991:67629:21:15:64:234:165:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f4:effects of each individual shock.21
30:992:67664:15:16:74:546:150:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:21This feature of  our model is consistent  with the empirical finding that  uncertainty shocks  alone  have at
30:993:67775:16:12:64:546:134:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:most moderate negative effects on output and investment, see for example Bachmann and Bayer (2013) or Vavra
30:994:67882:12:0:64:94:122:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:(2014).
31:995:67891:0:33:64:270:715:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:4.2    Balance Sheet Variables
31:996:67921:33:21:64:546:682:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Next,  we  turn  to  the  key  balance  sheet  variables  in  Table  3.   The  first  two  columns  report
31:997:68027:21:21:64:546:661:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:the unconditional mean and volatility.  The last three columns report conditional averages in
31:998:68120:21:41:64:441:640:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:expansions, non-financial recessions, and financial recessions, respectively.
31:999:68197:41:21:64:546:599:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f3:Non-financial Corporate SectorThe first panel focuses on firms.  Rows 1 and 2 display
31:1000:68282:21:21:64:547:578:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:the market value of assets (ptKBt) and the market value of liabilities (qmtABt), both scaled by
31:1001:68377:21:21:64:546:557:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:GDP.  Their  difference  is  the  market  value  of  firm  equity  scaled  by  GDP.  Their  ratio  is  the
31:1002:68483:21:21:64:546:536:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:market leverage ratio (row 4).  Book leverage, defined as the book value of debt to the book
31:1003:68575:21:21:64:546:515:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:value of assets in row 5,  is 35.2%,  and matches the low observed corporate leverage ratio in
31:1004:68669:21:21:64:546:494:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:the data.  Entrepreneurs own 64.8% of firms in the form of corporate equity.  Total credit to
31:1005:68762:21:25:64:343:473:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:non-financial firms amounts to 79.1% of GDP (row 3).
31:1006:68814:25:21:75:547:448:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Firms  default  when  their  profits  fall  below  the  thresholdπ.   This  is  more  likely  when  un-
31:1007:68917:21:21:64:545:427:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f8:certaintyσωis  high,  as  the  mass  of  firms  with  productivity  shocks  below  the  thresholdω∗t
31:1008:69017:21:21:64:546:406:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:increases.  The model generates average corporate default and loss rates of 2.25% (row 6) and
31:1009:69110:21:21:64:546:385:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:0.96% points (row 8), respectively, implying an average loss-given-default rate of 43.1% (row
31:1010:69203:21:21:64:546:364:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:7).  Default and loss rates are 6-7 times higher in financial recessions (5.50% and 2.31%) than in
31:1011:69301:21:21:64:546:343:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:non-financial recessions and expansions (about 0.9% and 0.4% in both).  The model generates
31:1012:69392:21:21:64:546:322:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:the right amount of corporate credit risk on average (as discussed in the calibration section).
31:1013:69487:21:25:64:495:301:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f4:It also generates the strong cyclicality in the quantity of risk observed in the data.22
31:1014:69575:25:21:75:547:276:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Firms reduce their reliance on debt financing in financial recessions.  They face a higher cost
31:1015:69670:21:21:64:546:255:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:of debt in these periods (rows 19 and 20), reflecting both a higher expected loss rate (row 8)
31:1016:69764:21:20:64:546:234:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:and a higher risk premium charged by banks.  The latter reflects financial fragility, as discussed
31:1017:69862:20:21:64:546:214:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:below.  Hence, financial sector fragility feeds back on the real economy and amplifies the initial
31:1018:69960:21:21:64:546:193:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:shock emanating from the real sector, a second financial accelerator.  Firms do not pursue the
31:1019:70054:21:21:64:546:172:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:investment projects they would otherwise undertake.  Relative to expansions, output falls by
31:1020:70146:21:19:64:371:151:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:4.5% and investment by 20% in financial recessions (row 9).
31:1021:70205:19:15:74:546:132:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:22In the 1991 recession, the delinquency rate spiked at 8.2% and the charge-off rate at 2.2%.  For the 2007-09
31:1022:70315:15:12:64:546:117:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:crisis, the respective numbers are 6.8% and 2.7%.  These are far above the unconditional averages of 3.1% and
31:1023:70424:12:12:64:546:105:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:0.7% cited in footnote 14.  Similarly, during the 2001 recession, the default rate on high-yield bonds was 9.9%,
31:1024:70536:12:0:64:242:93:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:far above the 1981-2014 average of 4.1%.
32:1025:70578:0:25:192:419:717:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Table 3:  Balance Sheet Variables and Prices
32:1026:70622:25:14:254:545:692:11:g_d0_f20:11:g_d0_f20:Unconditional   Expansions   Non-fin Rec.   Fin Rec.
32:1027:70674:14:13:254:534:678:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:meanstdevmeanmeanmean

32:1029:70700:14:14:70:545:651:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:1.  Mkt val of capital / Y (in %)225.04.3226.5227.3219.9

32:1031:70810:14:13:70:544:623:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:3.  Book val of corp debt / Y (in %)79.14.579.280.278.8

32:1047:71482:14:14:383:417:405:11:g_d0_f20:11:g_d0_f20:Prices
32:1048:71488:14:14:70:544:391:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:17.  Tobin’s q1.000.0171.010.990.97
32:1049:71523:14:13:70:544:377:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:18.  Risk-free rate (in %)2.192.862.454.100.26
32:1050:71569:13:14:70:544:364:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:19.  Corporate bond rate (in %)4.240.204.134.404.55
32:1051:71620:14:13:70:544:350:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:20.  Credit spread (in %)2.052.941.680.304.28
32:1052:71665:13:38:70:545:337:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:21.  Excess ret.  corp.  bonds (in %)1.093.441.87-0.15-0.49
32:1053:71724:38:21:64:547:299:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f3:Financial  IntermediariesThe  second  panel  of  Table  3  focuses  on  banks.   Intermediary
32:1054:71817:21:21:64:546:278:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:leverage  is  93.3%  on  average  in  market  values  (row  10)  and  93.3%  in  market  values.   The
32:1055:71919:21:21:64:546:257:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:average ratio of total intermediary book debt-to-assets in the 1953-2014 data is 91.5%, close to
32:1056:72015:21:21:64:546:236:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:the intermediaries in our model; see Appendix C.7 for the data calculations.  Financial leverage
32:1057:72111:21:21:64:546:215:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:was not directly targeted in the calibration, yet is close to the data.  Several model ingredients
32:1058:72209:21:20:64:546:194:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:contribute  to  the  high  financial  leverage.   Like  the  non-financial  firms,  they  are  owned  by
32:1059:72313:20:21:64:546:174:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:impatient  shareholders.   They  enjoy  a  tax  shield.   Unlike  firms,  they  benefit  from  deposit
32:1060:72415:21:21:64:546:153:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:insurance and they produce safe assets for patient savers, both of which keep down their cost
32:1061:72508:21:21:64:546:132:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:of funding (2.19%,  row 18).  Finally,  they face dividend adjustment costs,  which makes debt
32:1062:72602:21:21:64:546:111:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:issuance relatively attractive.  We explore the various drivers of leverage in Appendix D.2 and
32:1063:72697:21:21:64:546:90:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:find that the dominant force is the wedge between the time discount factor of borrowers and
32:1064:72788:21:0:64:98:69:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:savers.
33:1065:72797:0:21:75:547:715:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Banks suffer losses on their credit portfolio in financial recessions (row 21),  reducing their
33:1066:72892:21:21:64:546:694:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:book value of assets.  At the same time risk is high.  Low prices (high yields, row 19) of corporate
33:1067:72992:21:21:64:546:673:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:loans reflect the higher default risk (row 9) and the higher credit risk premium (row 20).  This
33:1068:73088:21:21:64:546:652:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:reduces the market value of intermediary assets,  amplifying the decline in the book value of
33:1069:73181:21:21:64:546:631:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:assets.  A lower value of bank assets in turn tightens the regulatory bank capital constraint.
33:1070:73275:21:21:64:546:610:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:The constraint binds in 91.1% of the financial crises compared to 61.3% unconditionally and
33:1071:73366:21:21:64:546:589:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:31.5% in expansions (row 12).  When binding,  intermediaries must reduce liabilities to meet
33:1072:73458:21:21:64:546:568:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:capital requirements, as measured by deposits to GDP in row 15, which explains the drop in
33:1073:73548:21:21:64:546:547:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:banks’ debt.  The decline in debt exceeds the decline in book assets, so that bank book leverage
33:1074:73644:21:21:64:546:526:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:is pro-cyclical.  Book leverage falls from 98.4% in expansions to 92.2% in financial recessions.
33:1075:73740:21:21:64:546:505:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:The decline in the price of loans, i.e., the larger fall in the market value of bank assets, results
33:1076:73840:21:21:64:546:484:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:in a-cyclical market leverage.  This pattern is directionally consistent with the data.  Adrian,
33:1077:73936:21:21:64:546:463:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Boyarchenko,  and  Shin  (2015)  show  that  book  leverage  is  pro-cyclical  for  commercial  banks
33:1078:74037:21:24:64:375:442:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:and broker-dealers, while market leverage is counter-cyclical.
33:1079:74099:24:21:75:547:418:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:While banks are roughly equally likely to be constrained in financial and non-financial reces-
33:1080:74193:21:21:64:546:397:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:sions, the reasons for the tightness of the bank capital constraint are fundamentally different.
33:1081:74289:21:21:64:546:376:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:In financial recessions,  banks suffer large credit losses and are forced to shrink,  delever,  and
33:1082:74388:21:21:64:546:355:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:issue equity.  Going forward, banks earn high risk yields on corporate debt (4.55%) and face low
33:1083:74484:21:21:64:546:334:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:borrowing costs (0.26%), making lending very profitable.  They would like to expand lending,
33:1084:74576:21:21:64:546:313:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:but are up against their borrowing constraint which prevents raising new debt.  They can and
33:1085:74668:21:21:64:546:292:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:do raise outside equity (negative dividends of 1.26% of GDP, line 14), but are held back by the
33:1086:74763:21:25:64:173:271:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:cost of raising equity.
33:1087:74786:25:21:75:547:246:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:In  contrast,  in  non-financial  recessions,  banking  becomes  much  less  profitable  due  to  the
33:1088:74887:21:21:64:546:225:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:shrinking net interest margin (0.3%).  These recessions resemble standard TFP-induced reces-
33:1089:74979:21:21:64:546:204:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:sions in real business cycle models: as productivity and labor income are temporarily low, savers
33:1090:75076:21:21:64:546:183:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:reduce their demand for safe assets in order to smooth consumption.  In addition, the supply
33:1091:75168:21:21:64:546:162:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:of government debt goes up due to increased government spending and lower tax revenue (row
33:1092:75258:21:21:64:546:141:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:16).   The  risk  free  rate  has  to  rise  to  4.1%  to  clear  the  market  for  short-term  debt.   At  the
33:1093:75369:21:21:64:546:120:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:same time, low productivity reduces corporate loan demand.  In response to the drop in profits
33:1094:75463:21:21:64:546:99:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:which depletes equity, banks lower dividend payments to 0.06% of GDP. To avoid raising costly
33:1095:75556:21:0:64:316:78:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:equity, banks exhaust their borrowing constraint.
34:1096:75607:0:21:75:547:715:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:The size of the intermediary sector,  relative to GDP, shrinks in financial recessions.  Bank
34:1097:75700:21:21:64:546:694:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:assets shrink about 3-5% relative to their levels in expansions (rows 2 and 3).  At the same time,
34:1098:75798:21:21:64:546:673:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:their liabilities shrink from 78% of GDP in expansions to 72% of GDP in financial recessions
34:1099:75890:21:25:64:367:652:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:(row 15).  Since GDP itself falls, bank deposits fall by 11%.
34:1100:75951:25:21:75:547:627:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:In  the  equilibrium  of  our  model,  0.54%  of  banks  are  insolvent  in  a  typical  year  (row  13).
34:1101:76056:21:21:64:546:606:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Intermediary  failures  are  concentrated  in  financial  recessions  (hence  the  name),  when  2.23%
34:1102:76158:21:21:64:546:585:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:of banks are insolvent, 22 times as many as in expansions and 2.8 times as many as in non-
34:1103:76248:21:21:64:546:564:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:financial recessions.  The model generates rare financial disasters when a non-trivial fraction of
34:1104:76346:21:21:64:546:543:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:the banking system is insolvent and needs to be bailed out.  These banking crises result from
34:1105:76439:21:21:64:546:522:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:the balance of two forces.  Bank equity owners try to avoid low intermediary net worth states
34:1106:76532:21:21:64:546:501:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:because they are risk averse and because of the cost of equity issuance.  But when net worth is
34:1107:76627:21:25:64:444:480:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:sufficiently low they have an incentive to shift the risk onto the tax payer.
34:1108:76704:25:21:75:547:455:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:An important quantitative success of the model is that it can generate the large observed
34:1109:76793:21:20:64:546:434:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:credit  spread  for  the  small  observed  amount  of  credit  risk,  a  challenge  in  standard  macro-
34:1110:76897:20:21:64:546:414:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:finance models; see Chen (2010).  The model generates not only the average spread, but also
34:1111:76988:21:21:64:546:393:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:high  volatility  and  counter-cyclicality.   As  Appendix  D.3  explains  in  more  detail,  the  credit
34:1112:77093:21:21:64:546:372:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:spread is high when intermediary net worth is low.  Intermediaries’ marginal value of equity
34:1113:77185:21:21:64:546:351:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:capital (shadow SDF) is high in those states of the world.  Like in Santos and Veronesi (2017),
34:1114:77280:21:21:64:546:330:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:our model generates a large credit spread in a model where all aggregate shocks emanate form
34:1115:77372:21:25:64:153:309:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:the real economy.
34:1116:77389:25:21:75:547:284:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Figure 3 show the impulse-response functions for assets and liabilities of both non-financial
34:1117:77482:21:21:64:546:263:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:firms and banks.  Loan loss rates spike in financial recessions and take several more years to
34:1118:77576:21:21:64:546:242:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:return to normal.  The high loan losses cause a spike in intermediary failures.  Both the asset
34:1119:77671:21:21:64:546:221:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:and liability side of corporate and intermediary balance sheet shrinks.  The credit spread also
34:1120:77766:21:21:64:546:200:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:spikes in the first period of a financial crisis.  The increased cost of credit is consistent with a
34:1121:77866:21:21:64:546:179:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:reduced loan demand from firms.  Credit declines persistently.  In contrast, asset prices recover
34:1122:77963:21:21:64:546:158:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:quickly.   This  pattern  is  consistent  with  the  data,  where  the  credit  spread  normalizes  fairly
34:1123:78069:21:21:64:546:137:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:quickly  after  the  initial  spike,  but  the  quantity  of  credit  takes  a  long  time  to  recover.   The
34:1124:78179:21:21:64:546:116:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:behavior  of  quantities  and  prices  in  financial  crises  is  in  sharp  contrast  to  the  much  milder
34:1125:78287:21:0:64:305:95:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:changes in non-financial recessions (blue lines).
35:1126:78338:0:142:116:494:717:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Figure 3:  Financial vs.  Non-financial Recessions:  Balance Sheet Variables

35:1169:78741:0:142:420:516:540:2:Helvetica:2:Helvetica:0.1Loan spread
35:1170:78755:142:36:110:502:398:10:g_d0_f20:10:g_d0_f6:Blue line:non-financial recession,Red line:financial recession,Black line:no shocks.
35:1171:78839:36:20:64:546:362:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f3:SaversRisk averse savers only hold safe debt, provided both by the intermediaries and the
35:1172:78928:20:21:64:546:342:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:government.  On average, these two sources of safe assets account for 77% (row 15) and 60%
35:1173:79018:21:21:64:546:321:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:of  GDP  (row  16).   In  financial  recessions,  intermediaries  have  to  delever  due  to  their  equity
35:1174:79125:21:21:64:546:300:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:losses.   An  increase  in  government  debt  due  to  counter-cyclical  fiscal  policy  partially  offsets
35:1175:79232:21:21:64:546:279:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:the reduction in the supply of safe assets from bank deleveraging.  A drop in the interest rate
35:1176:79327:21:21:64:546:258:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:is required to induce the savers to reduce their demand for safe assets and consume instead.
35:1177:79419:21:21:64:546:237:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:On average the real interest rate is close to 2 percentage points lower in a financial recession
35:1178:79515:21:21:64:547:216:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:compared to the unconditional average (row 18).23A substantial reduction in the real interest
35:1179:79608:21:21:64:546:195:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:rate is consistent with the experience in the Great Recession.  This reduction in interest rates
35:1180:79704:21:21:64:546:174:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:benefits banks and helps them to rebuild their net worth.  This in turn restores their ability to
35:1181:79801:21:15:64:132:153:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:lend to firms.
35:1182:79815:15:16:74:547:138:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:23The magnitude of the drop in real rates depends on the EIS of the saver.  For example, whenνS= 50>>1,
35:1183:79918:16:12:64:546:122:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:the risk-free interest rate volatility approaches zero.  Intermediaries no longer benefit from low, even negative
35:1184:80031:12:12:64:546:110:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:interest rates in crises.  The absence of cheap funding in crises makes them more reluctant to take on leverage
35:1185:80142:12:0:64:98:98:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:ex-ante.
36:1186:80152:0:33:64:364:715:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:4.3    Importance of Intermediary Frictions
36:1187:80195:33:21:64:546:682:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Intermediary  frictions  are  essential  to  generate  financial  crises.   To  see  this,  we  successively
36:1188:80303:21:21:64:546:661:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:relax two key intermediary frictions.  First, we turn off the equity adjustment cost by setting
36:1189:80398:21:21:64:547:640:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f3:σI= 0.  Then we turn off limited liability (deposit insurance) for intermediaries, so that they
36:1190:80493:21:21:64:546:619:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:cannot go bankrupt.  Figure 4 compares financial recessions in these economies to those in the
36:1191:80587:21:21:64:546:598:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:benchmark (black line).  The underlying shocks in all three economies are the same.  Clearly,
36:1192:80680:21:21:64:546:577:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:the disruption in credit is not nearly as severe, and the credit spread does not increase nearly
36:1193:80776:21:21:64:546:556:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:as much.  Macro-economic quantities are not nearly as adversely affected as in the benchmark
36:1194:80868:21:24:64:110:535:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:economy.
36:1195:80876:24:21:75:547:511:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Eliminating  the  equity  adjustment  cost  (σI=  0,  blue  line)  means  that  shareholders  can
36:1196:80973:21:21:64:546:490:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:quickly  recapitalize  intermediaries  in  crises,  which  results  in  less  shrinkage  of  the  financial
36:1197:81080:21:21:64:546:469:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:sector.  However, limited liability still causes a suboptimally slow recapitalization when inter-
36:1198:81177:21:21:64:546:448:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:mediaries are closer to default, as they have incentives to take on debt and shift the risk onto
36:1199:81273:21:21:64:546:427:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:the  taxpayer.   Turning  off  limited  liability  in  addition  (red  line)  eliminates  the  option  value
36:1200:81381:21:21:64:546:406:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:of bankruptcy and banks recapitalize more quickly.  The end result is an economy that allows
36:1201:81473:21:21:64:546:385:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:for more corporate debt and intermediary leverage, and suffers fewer DWL from bankruptcies.
36:1202:81564:21:21:64:546:364:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Consumption dynamics during financial recessions in this counterfactual economy look similar
36:1203:81656:21:25:64:201:343:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:to non-financial recessions.
36:1204:81684:25:21:75:547:318:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:This  special  case  without  equity  issuance  frictions  and  deposit  insurance  approaches  the
36:1205:81783:21:21:64:546:297:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:model of Brunnermeier and Sannikov (2014) where the balance sheets of firms and banks are
36:1206:81872:21:54:64:546:276:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:merged.  The results show substantial amplification from the decoupling of the balance sheets.
36:1207:81966:54:36:64:299:222:17:g_d0_f2:17:g_d0_f2:5    Macro-prudential Policy
36:1208:81994:36:21:64:546:186:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:We use our calibrated model to investigate the effects of macro-prudential policy choices.  Our
36:1209:82089:21:21:64:546:165:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:main experiment is a variation in the intermediaries’ leverage constraint.  In the benchmark
36:1210:82181:21:21:64:546:144:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:model, intermediaries can borrow 94 cents against every dollar in assets;  they must hold 6%
36:1211:82273:21:21:64:547:123:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:equity capital.  We explore tighter constraints (ξ < .94), as well as looser constraints (ξ > .94).
36:1212:82372:21:21:64:546:102:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:We also study a time-varying capital requirement conditional on the uncertainty state.  Our
36:1213:82463:21:0:64:546:81:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:third  macro-prudential  policy  experiment  is  to  charge  intermediariesκ=  1.0%  for  deposit

37:1262:83424:12:12:64:546:350:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:(σI= 0) and in the ability of intermediaries to default (no intermediary bankruptcy).  The underlying shock
37:1263:83531:12:35:64:251:338:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:sequences are identical across experiments.
37:1264:83574:35:21:64:546:303:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:insurance,  a  much  higher  tax  on  leverage  than  in  the  benchmark  (0.084%).   Tables  4  and  5
37:1265:83677:21:47:64:517:282:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:show the results.  Table 5 reports moments in percentage deviation from the benchmark.
37:1266:83763:47:33:64:401:235:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:5.1    Changing maximum intermediary leverage
37:1267:83808:33:21:64:547:202:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f3:Effect on lending and intermediationRows 10 and 11 of Table 4 show that a policy that
37:1268:83893:21:20:64:546:181:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:constrains bank leverage is indeed successful at bringing down that leverage.  Banks reduce the
37:1269:83988:20:21:64:546:161:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:size of their assets, both in book and market value terms (rows 2 and 3) and the size of their
37:1270:84082:21:21:64:547:140:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:liabilities (row 16).  On net, intermediary equity capital increases sharply asξis lowered (row
37:1271:84177:21:25:64:84:119:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:14).
37:1272:84181:25:21:75:547:94:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:With  intermediaries  better  capitalized,  financial  fragility  falls.   Intermediary  bankruptcies
37:1273:84282:21:0:64:547:73:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:(row 13) drop rapidly from 0.54% to 0.01% first (atξ=.90) and are eradicated for even tighter
38:1274:84377:0:21:64:546:715:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:capital requirements.  Interestingly, with tighter regulation, intermediaries’ leverage constraints
38:1275:84476:21:21:64:546:694:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:bindlessfrequently  (row  12).   Intermediaries  become  more  cautious  when  they  are  better
38:1276:84572:21:21:64:546:673:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:capitalized, since equity capital adjustments become effectively more costly (as explained below)
38:1277:84669:21:21:64:546:652:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:and the option to default (limited liability) is farther out-of-the-money.  Tighter regulation leads
38:1278:84769:21:25:64:352:631:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:to a safer intermediary sector, but also to a smaller one.
38:1279:84827:25:21:75:547:606:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:The  increased  safety  of  the  financial  sector  asξfalls  is  also  reflected  in  lower  corporate
38:1280:84930:21:21:64:546:585:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:default,  loss-given-default,  and  loss  rates  on  loans  to  non-financial  firms  (rows  6-8).   Firms
38:1281:85036:21:21:64:546:564:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:choose to reduce leverage (rows 4-5).  Firms’ reluctance to undertake more leverage despite the
38:1282:85131:21:21:64:546:543:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:safer environment may be understood from the higher interest rate they face on debt (row 19).
38:1283:85224:21:21:64:547:522:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:When intermediary capacity shrinks (with lowerξ),  the reward for providing intermediation
38:1284:85314:21:21:64:547:501:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:services increases.  The  modest 25bps increase in the credit spread atξ=  0.75 is the result
38:1285:85407:21:21:64:546:480:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:of large offsetting movements in the expected loss rate, which halves, and in the excess return
38:1286:85502:21:25:64:411:459:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:intermediaries earn on their asset holdings, which doubles (row 21).
38:1287:85570:25:20:75:547:434:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:To understand the effect of tighter regulation on intermediary profitability, we compute the
38:1288:85662:20:21:64:546:414:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:franchise value of intermediation, defined as the market value of banks to shareholders per dollar
38:1289:85760:21:21:64:547:393:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:of equity capitalVI/WI−1 (row 15).  If the value of banks were simply equal to the difference
38:1290:85853:21:21:64:547:372:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:between the market value of assets and liabilities, franchise value would be zero (VI=WI).
38:1291:85943:21:21:64:547:351:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:The franchise value declines from 34% in the benchmark to 4% atξ=.75.  The drop can be
38:1292:86029:21:21:64:546:330:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:understood from the additional measures of bank profitability reported in rows 15a-c.  First,
38:1293:86122:21:21:64:546:309:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:banks become less profitable for shareholders as measured by the return on bank equity (in an
38:1294:86215:21:38:64:436:288:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:accounting sense), reported in row 15a.  We compute accounting ROE as
38:1295:86284:38:39:89:521:250:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:AROE = Excess ret.  on loans (row 21)×book value of loans (row 3)/WI(row 14).
38:1296:86361:39:21:64:546:211:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Tighter regulation requires more bank equity (row 14) to operate a smaller banking sector (rows
38:1297:86456:21:21:64:546:190:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:3).  This shrinkage effect dominates the rise in profitability per dollar of loans issued reflected
38:1298:86555:21:25:64:547:169:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:in the greater excess return (row 21), causing a decline in accounting ROE by 55% atξ= 75%.
38:1299:86646:25:20:75:547:144:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:As Admati, DeMarzo, Hellwig, and Pfleiderer (2013) point out, this calculation may not tell
38:1300:86737:20:21:64:546:124:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:the whole story.  The required return on equity will decline as banks are forced to hold more
38:1301:86830:21:21:64:546:103:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:capital and shareholders are exposed to less risk.  This force is also present in our model, and
38:1302:86926:21:0:64:546:82:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:we can compute the equilibrium market return on equity for bank shareholders to measure its
39:1303:87019:0:21:64:546:715:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:magnitude.  The cum-dividend market value of intermediary equity to borrower-entrepreneurs
39:1304:87109:21:21:64:546:694:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:is given byVIt=VI(WIt,SIt) as defined in (12).  Using this market price, we can compute the
39:1305:87200:21:40:64:250:673:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:expected market return on equity as
39:1306:87235:40:0:211:263:633:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:MROEt=
39:1307:87241:0:0:268:279:642:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f8:Et
39:1308:87243:0:10:281:286:652:12:g_d0_f11:12:g_d0_f11:[
39:1309:87244:10:0:286:308:642:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:max
39:1310:87247:0:10:310:317:652:12:g_d0_f11:12:g_d0_f11:{
39:1311:87248:10:0:317:383:642:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f3:VIt+1−-It+1,0
39:1312:87261:0:27:383:395:652:12:g_d0_f11:12:g_d0_f11:}]
39:1313:87263:27:0:312:350:625:12:g_d0_f7:8:g_d0_f8:VIt−dIt
39:1314:87270:0:38:396:399:633:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f7:.
39:1315:87271:38:21:64:546:595:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Indeed we find that the market return on equity declines as we tighten regulation and banks
39:1316:87362:21:21:64:546:574:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:become less risky (row 15b).  However, we also compute the weighted average cost of capital
39:1317:87453:21:21:64:546:553:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:(WACC) for banks in row 15c, using the market ROE from row 15b as cost of equity. To compute
39:1318:87545:21:21:64:547:532:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:WACC, first calculate the effective cost of debt finance to banks asrdebtt= (qt+τΠrft−κ)−1−1.
39:1319:87638:21:38:64:427:511:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:The total firm value of the bank isVbankt=VIt+qt×Depositst.  Hence
39:1320:87704:38:0:187:239:473:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:WACCt=
39:1321:87710:0:16:250:260:481:12:g_d0_f7:8:g_d0_f8:VIt
39:1322:87713:16:0:244:253:465:12:g_d0_f7:8:g_d0_f8:Vbankt
39:1323:87719:0:0:273:324:473:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:MROEt+
39:1324:87725:0:16:328:398:481:12:g_d0_f7:8:g_d0_f8:qt×Depositst
39:1325:87737:16:0:349:359:465:12:g_d0_f7:8:g_d0_f8:Vbankt
39:1326:87743:0:38:400:424:473:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f7:rdebtt.
39:1327:87750:38:21:64:546:435:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:The decline in the cost of less-risky equity is not able to offset the large change in the composition
39:1328:87852:21:21:64:547:414:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:of funding, which shifts from deposits towards equity with lowerξ.  As a result, WACC rises
39:1329:87943:21:21:64:547:393:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:by almost 50% relative to the benchmark atξ= 75%.  The reduced franchise value is a direct
39:1330:88033:21:21:64:546:372:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:result of this sharp rise in WACC and consistent with bankers’ argument that tighter regulation
39:1331:88128:21:21:64:546:351:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:destroys shareholder value.  The main driver of this value in the benchmark economy is access
39:1332:88221:21:21:64:546:330:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:to cheap deposit funding from savers.  As intermediaries are forced to fund each dollar of loans
39:1333:88317:21:21:64:546:309:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:with a greater proportion of equity, the value created for bank shareholders per dollar of capital
39:1334:88415:21:21:64:546:288:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:invested declines.  Banks charge higher spreads in the loan market, but can only partially pass
39:1335:88510:21:42:64:414:267:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:through the higher funding cost to borrowers in general equilibrium.
39:1336:88578:42:21:64:547:225:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f3:Effect  on  production  and  macroeconomic  volatilityA  first  major  adverse  effect  of
39:1337:88668:21:21:64:546:204:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:tighter  macro-prudential  policy  is  that  the  economy’s  output  shrinks  (row  27  of  Table  5).
39:1338:88770:21:21:64:546:183:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:The capital stock shrinks sizeably (row 28).  The reduction in output arises because firms are
39:1339:88864:21:20:64:546:162:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:smaller and borrow less from a smaller intermediary sector,  since debt finance became more
39:1340:88955:20:21:64:546:142:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:costly.  Even though GDP shrinks, aggregate consumption increases slightly (row 29) thanks to
39:1341:89048:21:25:64:379:121:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:lower deadweight losses from firm and bank failures (row 26).
39:1342:89109:25:21:75:547:96:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A second adverse effect of tighter capital regulation is that it reduces the risk absorption ca-
39:1343:89205:21:0:64:546:75:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:pacity of the intermediary sector.  Maintaining a larger equity buffer means that intermediaries
41:1344:90884:0:21:64:546:715:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:need to incur larger deviations from the dividend target (in absolute value).  At lowerξ, the
41:1345:90977:21:21:64:546:694:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:dividend adjustment cost makes reacting to economic fluctuations by varying dividends more
41:1346:91067:21:21:64:546:673:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:expensive, relative to the benchmark.  Intermediaries adjust assets and debt instead of equity
41:1347:91161:21:21:64:547:652:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:(rows 32-34): lowerξincreases the volatility of asset and debt growth, but reduces the volatility
41:1348:91258:21:21:64:546:631:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:of dividend growth.  When going from the benchmark to modestly tighter regulation, the re-
41:1349:91348:21:21:64:546:610:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:duced ability of intermediaries to absorb aggregate risk spills over to higher investment growth
41:1350:91444:21:21:64:546:589:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:volatility (35) and consumption growth volatility (rows 36-38).  The reduced risk-sharing role of
41:1351:91541:21:21:64:546:568:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:the intermediary is reflected in a more volatile ratio of marginal utility of borrowers and savers,
41:1352:91640:21:25:64:344:547:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:a marker of increased market incompleteness (row 39).
41:1353:91693:25:21:75:547:522:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:The overall effect on macroeconomic volatility is non-monotonic:  tighter regulation makes
41:1354:91783:21:21:64:546:501:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:financial  recessions  less  severe,  but  also  diminishes  the  intermediary’s  willingness  to  absorb
41:1355:91888:21:21:64:547:480:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:aggregate risk.  Volatility of investment and consumption growth peak atξ=.85.  For capital
41:1356:91979:21:21:64:546:459:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:requirements higher than 15%,  volatility starts to decline as the difference between financial
41:1357:92074:21:20:64:547:438:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:and  non-financial  recessions  becomes  smaller.   At  a  capital  requirement  of  25%  (ξ=.75),
41:1358:92172:20:21:64:546:418:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:volatilities are lower than in the benchmark.  Interestingly, looser regulation than benchmark
41:1359:92266:21:21:64:547:397:12:g_d0_f17:12:g_d0_f3:alsoraises  macroeconomic  volatility.   The  economy  withξ=.97  experiences  more  severe
41:1360:92357:21:21:64:546:376:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:financial  recessions  as  the  indicated  by  the  higher  default  rates  of  firms  and  banks.   This
41:1361:92462:21:21:64:546:355:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:increased  fragility  raises  macro-economic  volatility.   The  subtle,  hard-to-predict,  pattern  in
41:1362:92565:21:25:64:449:334:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:macro-economic volatility underscores the need for a rich structural model.
41:1363:92640:25:21:75:547:309:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:In summary, tightening the capital requirement has two key effects: (1) it shrinks the economy
41:1364:92734:21:21:64:546:288:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:and  lowers  leverage  of  firms  and  banks,  reducing  macroeconomic  volatility  and  bankruptcy-
41:1365:92834:21:21:64:546:267:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:related losses; and (2), it effectively makes banks more risk averse, reducing their willingness to
41:1366:92933:21:21:64:546:246:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:absorb aggregate risk and causing higher macroeconomic volatility.  Figure 5 summarizes the
41:1367:93024:21:21:64:546:225:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:effects of macro-prudential policy on financial fragility (left panel) and the size of the economy
41:1368:93122:21:42:64:132:204:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:(right panel).
41:1369:93136:42:21:64:547:162:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f3:WelfarePopulation-weighted aggregate welfareWpop(row 24) is maximized atξ=.90; a 4
41:1370:93218:21:20:64:546:141:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:percentage point higher equity capital requirement than in the benchmark.  The policy change
41:1371:93310:20:21:64:546:121:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:leads to a modest aggregate welfare gain of 32 bps.  Higher equity requirements than 10% reduce
41:1372:93405:21:21:64:546:100:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:the gains.  Locally, they increase volatility and reduce risk sharing without additional benefits
41:1373:93502:21:0:64:546:79:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:from fewer defaults.  At a 25% capital requirement, ex-post welfare is back to the benchmark

43:1409:95325:171:12:64:546:503:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:The  left  panel  plots  the  loss  rate  on  the  loans  held  by  banks  and  the  failure  rate  of  banks  as  a  function  of
43:1410:95455:12:12:64:547:491:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:the  macro-prudential  policy  parameterξ.   The  right  panel  plots  output  and  the  ratio  of  deposits  to  output
43:1411:95575:12:12:64:547:479:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:as a function of the macro-prudential policy parameterξ.  Each dot represents a different economy where all
43:1412:95682:12:35:64:487:467:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:parameters are the same as in te benchmark, except forξ.  The benchmark economy hasξ=.94.
43:1413:95771:35:21:64:546:432:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:value.  The green line in the left panel of Figure 6 shows modest welfare gains for a large range
43:1414:95868:21:25:64:156:411:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:of tighter policies.
43:1415:95888:25:21:75:547:386:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:The  small  aggregate  gain  masks  large  heterogeneity  in  gains  and  losses  among  borrowers
43:1416:95986:21:21:64:546:365:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:savers.  Tighter regulation redistributes wealth from savers to borrowers.  It both reduces the
43:1417:96081:21:21:64:546:344:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:supply  of  safe  assets  and  makes  it  less  reliable.   As  debt  finance  becomes  more  expensive,
43:1418:96185:21:21:64:546:323:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:borrowers rely more on equity finance and a larger share of firm earnings accrues to them.  At
43:1419:96279:21:21:64:546:302:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f3:ξ=.90, borrower consumption is 3.4% higher than in the benchmark and saver consumption
43:1420:96365:21:21:64:546:281:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:is  2.7%  lower  (row  30  and  31),  leading  to  welfare  gains  and  losses  of  similar  size  (row  24
43:1421:96472:21:21:64:546:260:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:and 25);  see also the right panel of Figure 6.  Looser capital requirements have the opposite
43:1422:96566:21:21:64:546:239:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:distributional  effect  and  increase  saver  wealth  at  the  expense  of  borrowers.   However,  DWL
43:1423:96668:21:21:64:546:218:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:from firm and bank failures are so large atξ=.97 that consumption of both agents is lower
43:1424:96757:21:20:64:546:197:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:than in the benchmark.  The increased financial fragility makes both agents worse off.  Maybe
43:1425:96850:20:21:64:546:177:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:surprisingly at first, forcing banks to hold more equity ends up benefiting their shareholders.  In
43:1426:96949:21:21:64:546:156:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:sum, tighter capital requirements lead to small (population-weighted) aggregate welfare gains,
43:1427:97043:21:21:64:546:135:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:they increase consumption and wealth inequality.  Policy makers have signaled concern about
43:1428:97134:21:21:64:546:114:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:redistributive implications of monetary policies adopted after the Great Financial Crisis.  We
43:1429:97228:21:25:64:369:93:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:show that macro-prudential policy has similar implications.
43:1430:97287:25:0:75:547:68:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:While none of the variations ofξconsidered in Table 5 allow for a Pareto improving transfer
44:1431:97380:0:21:64:546:715:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:scheme (row 23), the red line in the left panel of Figure 6 makes clear that there is a Pareto
44:1432:97474:21:21:64:547:694:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:improvement possible atξ=.95 andξ=.96.  In those cases, the welfare gains to savers are
44:1433:97561:21:21:64:546:673:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:sufficient to compensate borrowers for their losses and still have about 12% of GDP left over.
44:1434:97655:21:21:64:546:652:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Intuitively, borrowers are less patient than savers and require lower compensation for the same
44:1435:97750:21:21:64:546:631:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:permanent reduction in consumption.  In theξ=.96 economy, the policy maker could levy a tax
44:1436:97841:21:21:64:547:610:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:on savers that reduces their utility to the level of the benchmark.  Thepresent valueof the tax
44:1437:97936:21:21:64:546:589:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:revenue stream would be 23% of benchmark GDP. The revenue could be used to pay a subsidy
44:1438:98024:21:21:64:546:568:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:to borrowers that makes them exactly as well of as in the benchmark; the present value of this
44:1439:98118:21:21:64:546:547:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:subsidy stream would be 11.2% of GDP. The remaining revenue has a present value of 11.8%
44:1440:98206:21:21:64:546:526:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:of GDP and measures the Pareto improvement.  By the same logic, a 25% capital requirement
44:1441:98295:21:21:64:546:505:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:would require a massive transfer to the savers, much more than the impatient borrowers are
44:1442:98385:21:25:64:156:484:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:willing to give up.
44:1443:98404:25:21:75:547:459:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:The two different ways of aggregating welfare lead to optimal capital requirements of 10%
44:1444:98493:21:20:64:546:438:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:and 4%, straddling the 6% in the benchmark.  The results suggest that the status quo capital
44:1445:98585:20:27:64:238:418:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:requirements are close to optimal.
44:1446:98619:27:197:143:468:391:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Figure 6:  Welfare Across Macro-Prudential Policy Experiments
44:1447:98680:197:12:64:547:194:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:The left panel plots the ex-post population-weighted aggregate welfare functionWpopin green and the ex-ante
44:1448:98787:12:12:64:546:182:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:consumption  equivalent  variation  welfare  functionWcevin  red  as  a  function  of  the  macro-prudential  policy
44:1449:98903:12:12:64:547:170:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:parameterξ.  The right panel plots the value function of Borrower (black) and Saver (orange) as a function of
44:1450:99012:12:12:64:547:158:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:the macro-prudential policy parameterξ.  Each dot represents a different economy where all parameters are the
44:1451:99121:12:0:64:402:146:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:same as in te benchmark, except forξ.  The benchmark economy hasξ=.94.
45:1452:99193:0:33:64:391:715:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:5.2    Other Macro-prudential Policy Measures
45:1453:99238:33:21:64:547:682:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f3:Time-varying capital requirementThe 7th column of tables 4 and 5 show an experiment
45:1454:99321:21:21:64:547:661:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:with a capital requirement that varies conditional on the uncertainty stateσω,t.  When uncer-
45:1455:99414:21:21:64:546:640:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:tainty is low, banks’ constraint is tightened (ξ=.93) compared to the benchmark, whereas it is
45:1456:99508:21:21:64:546:619:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:loosened (ξ=.95) when uncertainty is high.  This counter-cyclical capital requirement causes
45:1457:99600:21:21:64:546:598:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:a moderate expansion in corporate and financial leverage, leading to slightly higher loan losses
45:1458:99696:21:21:64:546:577:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:(1.06% vs .96%) and substantially more frequent bank defaults (1.13% vs.  .54%).  However, the
45:1459:99790:21:21:64:546:556:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:higher DWL are offset by a greater capital stock (+1.1%) and higher GDP (+.3%), such that
45:1460:99879:21:20:64:546:535:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:aggregate consumption remains unchanged.  Even though credit risk increases, the credit spread
45:1461:99973:20:21:64:546:515:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:shrinks due to a smaller credit risk premium (+.89% vs.  1.09%).  Since intermediaries are less
45:1462:100068:21:21:64:546:494:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:constrained in financial crises now, they require less compensation for carrying aggregate risk
45:1463:100163:21:21:64:546:473:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:and macroeconomic volatility decreases.  Risk sharing among borrowers and savers improves, as
45:1464:100256:21:21:64:546:452:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:indicated by the lower volatility of the MU ratio (row 41, -34.2%).  The larger financial sector
45:1465:100352:21:21:64:546:431:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:distributes wealth from borrowers to savers:  saver consumption increases by 2.2% and welfare
45:1466:100445:21:21:64:546:410:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:by 1.5%.  Borrower welfare declines by 2.4%, implying an ex-post aggregate welfare loss of 31
45:1467:100538:21:21:64:546:389:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:bps.  However, since the experiment makes the more patient savers significantly better off, it
45:1468:100632:21:21:64:546:368:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:allows for Pareto improving wealth transfers.  The compensating variation wealth residual (row
45:1469:100726:21:25:64:163:347:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:23) is 17% of GDP.
45:1470:100744:25:21:75:547:322:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Appendix Figure 13 compares financial recessions in the world with counter-cyclical capital
45:1471:100835:21:21:64:546:301:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:requirements  to  financial  recessions  in  the  benchmark  economy.   The  former  feature  much
45:1472:100933:21:21:64:546:280:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:smaller  reductions  in  credit  extension,  in  part  due  to  a  much  smaller  increase  in  the  credit
45:1473:101040:21:41:64:476:259:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:spread, as well as a shallower recession in terms of consumption and investment.
45:1474:101120:41:21:64:546:218:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f3:Increasing cost of deposit insuranceThe last column of tables 4 and 5 shows the result
45:1475:101206:21:21:64:547:197:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:of an experiment that increases the cost of deposit insuranceκfrom 0.08% to 1% per unit of
45:1476:101296:21:21:64:546:176:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:deposit.  While this is a direct tax on bank leverage, its incidence falls on non-financial firms
45:1477:101393:21:21:64:546:155:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:and savers in equilibrium.  Firms bear most of the cost through a significantly higher credit risk
45:1478:101491:21:21:64:546:134:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:premium, paying a 2.39% credit spread (vs.  2.05%), despite a reduction in the loan loss rate
45:1479:101584:21:21:64:546:113:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:from 0.96% to 0.50%.  As a result of the higher cost of debt, equilibrium firm leverage is much
45:1480:101679:21:21:64:546:92:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:lower.  Contrary to the presumed intention of the policy, banks lever up due to the high credit
45:1481:101774:21:0:64:546:71:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:spread they earn and become more fragile (1.13% bank failures,  twice the benchmark level).
46:1482:101867:0:21:64:546:715:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:The capital stock shrinks by 4.2% and GDP by 1.2%.  Since DWL from corporate defaults fall,
46:1483:101958:21:21:64:546:694:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:aggregate consumption is unaffected.  Overall,  the policy redistributes wealth from savers to
46:1484:102052:21:21:64:546:673:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:borrowers, as the overall supply of risk free debt shrinks.  While there is an ex-post aggregate
46:1485:102148:21:54:64:464:652:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:welfare gain of .49%, the policy does not allow for Pareto improving transfers.
46:1486:102227:54:37:64:189:598:17:g_d0_f2:17:g_d0_f2:6    Robustness
46:1487:102242:37:21:64:546:561:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Appendix D studies the robustness of the results.  Section D.5 shows transition dynamics from
46:1488:102335:21:21:64:546:540:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:the benchmark economy to one with tighter capital requirements.  Along the transition path,
46:1489:102426:21:20:64:546:519:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:there is a consumption boom as the economy gradually adjusts to a permanently lower capital
46:1490:102517:20:25:64:94:499:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:stock.
46:1491:102523:25:21:75:547:474:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Appendix D.6 studies a range of values for the equity issuance cost around the benchmark.
46:1492:102612:21:21:64:546:453:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:The effects of a greater adjustment cost are similar to those of tighter capital requirements.
46:1493:102706:21:21:64:547:432:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:HigherσIlimits banks’ ability to absorb aggregate risk and increases the cost of debt finance
46:1494:102799:21:21:64:546:411:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:to firms.  In equilibrium, this leads to substantially lower corporate leverage and hence reduces
46:1495:102896:21:21:64:546:390:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:financial fragility for both producers and intermediaries.  At the same time, it causes a smaller
46:1496:102993:21:21:64:546:369:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:capital stock and lower output.  The exercise highlights the importance of the equity adjustment
46:1497:103089:21:21:64:547:348:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:cost for generating a large credit risk premium. When we raiseσIto 7 from a benchmark value of
46:1498:103183:21:21:64:546:327:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:5, the loss rate on corporate loans is cut in half, while the risk premium earned by intermediaries
46:1499:103282:21:25:64:525:306:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:doubles.  This implies that the price of risk earned by intermediaries increases by factor 4.
46:1500:103375:25:21:75:547:281:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Appendix D.7 finds that the conclusions of our main macro-prudential policy experiment are
46:1501:103465:21:21:64:546:260:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:robust to changes in key model parameters.  Neither the presence of the bankruptcy option,
46:1502:103555:21:21:64:546:239:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:nor  the  equity  adjustment  costs,  nor  the  tax  shield  for  banks  are  crucial  for  the  qualitative
46:1503:103663:21:21:64:546:218:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:macro-pru  implications  of  the  model.   In  every  case,  borrowers  gain  from  tighter  policy  and
46:1504:103767:21:21:64:546:197:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:savers loose.  The trade-off between less financial fragility and a smaller economy is present in
46:1505:103864:21:53:64:169:176:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:every model variant.
46:1506:103884:53:37:64:186:123:17:g_d0_f2:17:g_d0_f2:7    Conclusion
46:1507:103899:37:21:64:546:86:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:We provide the first calibrated macro-economic model which features intermediaries who extend
46:1508:103992:21:0:64:546:65:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:long-term defaultable loans to firms producing output and raise deposits from risk averse savers,
47:1509:104091:0:21:64:546:715:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:and in which both banks and firms can default. The model incorporates a rich set of fiscal policy
47:1510:104188:21:25:64:459:694:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:rules, including deposit insurance, and endogenizes the risk-free interest rate.
47:1511:104268:25:21:75:547:669:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Like  in  the  standard  accelerator  model,  shocks  to  the  economy  affect  entrepreneurial  net
47:1512:104368:21:21:64:546:648:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:worth.  Since firm borrowing is constrained by net worth, macroeconomic shocks are potentially
47:1513:104462:21:21:64:546:627:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:amplified by tighter borrowing constraints.  For realistic firm leverage ratios,  this traditional
47:1514:104560:21:21:64:546:606:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:accelerator is not very powerful.  A second, much more powerful financial accelerator arises from
47:1515:104657:21:21:64:546:585:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:explicitly modeling the financial intermediaries’ net worth dynamics.  Intermediaries are subject
47:1516:104754:21:21:64:546:564:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:to  regulatory  capital  constraints.   Macroeconomic  shocks  that  lead  to  binding  intermediary
47:1517:104854:21:21:64:546:543:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:borrowing  constraints  amplify  the  shocks  through  their  direct  effect  on  intermediaries’  net
47:1518:104956:21:25:64:454:522:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:worth and the indirect effect on borrowers to whom the intermediaries lend.
47:1519:105031:25:21:75:547:497:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:We find that tighter restrictions on bank leverage reduce financial fragility, but also shrinks
47:1520:105126:21:21:64:546:476:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:the  size  of  the  intermediation  sector  and  its  risk  absorption  capacity.   The  size  of  the  econ-
47:1521:105235:21:21:64:546:455:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:omy shrinks and macro-economic volatility may increase.  Counter-cyclical capital equity re-
47:1522:105327:21:20:64:546:434:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:quirements centered around the current level generate a Pareto improvement.  Tighter macro-
47:1523:105418:20:21:64:546:414:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:prudential policy has sizeable effects on inequality; the incidence of policies designed to limit
47:1524:105515:21:25:64:456:393:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:the riskiness of the financial sector may fall on other sectors of the economy.
47:1525:105594:25:21:75:547:368:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Several  extensions  are  fruitful  directions  for  future  research.   One  could  study  monetary
47:1526:105694:21:21:64:546:347:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:policy in a model that has endogenous labor supply and New-Keynesian ingredients.  Modeling
47:1527:105785:21:21:64:546:326:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:heterogeneity within the financial sector would be interesting, splitting institutions into levered
47:1528:105884:21:21:64:546:305:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:and unlevered for example.  One can add mortgage borrowers and study interactions between
47:1529:105973:21:21:64:546:284:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:stress in mortgage and corporate loans and their implications for the real economy.  Finally,
47:1530:106066:21:21:64:546:263:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:our model assumed perfect alignment between management and shareholders.  The presence of
47:1531:106155:21:21:64:546:242:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:management’s incentives to gamble arising from compensation structures may affect optimal
47:1532:106244:21:65:64:207:221:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:equity capital requirements.
47:1533:106272:65:29:64:155:156:17:g_d0_f2:17:g_d0_f2:References

61:2373:129256:24:26:117:546:666:11:g_d0_f18:11:g_d0_f6:qft(CSt)−1/ν(1−βS)(VSt)1/ν=λSt+βSEt[(VSt+1)−σSVSW,t+1](CESt)σS−1/ν(VSt)1/ν(56)
61:2374:129334:26:34:64:414:640:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:whereλStis the Lagrange multiplier on the no-borrowing constraint (54).
61:2375:129405:34:24:64:370:606:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A.3.3    Marginal Values of State Variables and SDF
61:2376:129456:24:25:64:245:582:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:The marginal value of saver wealth is:
61:2377:129494:25:28:224:546:557:11:g_d0_f18:11:g_d0_f6:VSW,t= (CSt)−1/ν(1−βS)(VSt)1/ν,.(57)
61:2378:129530:28:36:75:410:529:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:Defining the SDF in the same fashion as we did for borrowers, we get:
61:2379:129599:36:0:199:257:493:11:g_d0_f9:8:g_d0_f8:MSt,t+1=βS
61:2380:129609:0:10:260:269:511:11:g_d0_f11:11:g_d0_f11:(

61:2382:129615:16:0:270:290:485:11:g_d0_f18:8:g_d0_f8:CESt
61:2383:129619:0:10:295:349:511:11:g_d0_f11:11:g_d0_f11:)1/νS−σS(
61:2384:129628:10:16:350:372:501:11:g_d0_f18:8:g_d0_f4:CSt+1
61:2385:129633:16:0:354:365:485:11:g_d0_f18:8:g_d0_f8:CSt

61:2387:129642:18:42:409:412:493:11:g_d0_f18:11:g_d0_f18:.
61:2388:129643:42:25:64:203:451:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A.3.4    Euler Equations
61:2389:129667:25:14:64:546:426:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:Combining the first-order condition for short-term bonds (56) with the marginal value of wealth, and
61:2390:129767:14:24:64:354:412:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:the SDF, we get the Euler equation for the short-term bond:
61:2391:129826:24:0:253:314:388:11:g_d0_f18:8:g_d0_f8:qft= ̃λSt+ Et

61:2397:129931:38:24:64:189:324:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:A.4    Equilibrium
61:2398:129949:24:14:64:546:300:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:The optimality conditions describing the problem are (26), (30), (35), (36), and (31) for borrowers,
61:2399:130049:14:13:64:546:286:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:(41),  (50),  and  (51)  for  intermediaries,  and  (52)  and  (58)  for  depositors.   We  add  complementary
61:2400:130159:13:14:64:546:273:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:slackness conditions for the constraints (27) for borrowers, (43) and (44) for intermediaries, and (54)
61:2401:130262:14:13:64:546:259:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:for depositors.  Together with the market clearing conditions (18), (19), (20), and (21) these equations
61:2402:130366:13:0:64:211:246:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:fully characterize the economy.
62:2403:130399:0:29:64:296:715:17:g_d0_f2:17:g_d0_f2:B    Computational Method
62:2404:130424:29:13:64:546:686:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:The equilibrium of dynamic stochastic general equilibrium models is usually characterized recursively.
62:2405:130526:13:14:64:546:673:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:If a stationary Markov equilibrium exists, there is a minimal set of state variables that summarizes
62:2406:130626:14:13:64:546:659:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:the economy at any given point in time.  Equilibrium can then be characterized using two types of
62:2407:130723:13:14:64:546:646:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:functions:  transition functions map today’s state into probability distributions of tomorrow’s state,
62:2408:130825:14:13:64:546:632:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:and policy functions determine agents’ decisions and prices given the current state.  Brumm, Kryczka,
62:2409:130926:13:14:64:546:619:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:and  Kubler  (2018)  analyze  theoretical  existence  properties  in  this  class  of  models  and  discuss  the
62:2410:131038:14:13:64:546:605:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:literature.  Perturbation-based solution methods find local approximations to these functions around
62:2411:131138:13:14:64:546:592:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:the “deterministic steady-state”.  For applications in finance, there are often two problems with local
62:2412:131241:14:14:64:546:578:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:solution methods.  First, portfolio restrictions such as leverage constraints may be occasionally binding
62:2413:131346:14:13:64:546:564:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:in the true stochastic equilibrium.  Generally, a local approximation around the steady state (with a
62:2414:131447:13:14:64:546:551:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:binding or slack constraint) will therefore inaccurately capture nonlinear dynamics when constraints go
62:2415:131550:14:13:64:546:537:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:from slack to binding. Guerrieri and Iacoviello (2015) propose a solution using local methods. Secondly,
62:2416:131654:13:14:64:546:524:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:the portfolio allocation of agents across assets with different risk profiles is generally indeterminate
62:2417:131758:14:13:64:546:510:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:at the non-stochastic steady state.  This means that it is generally impossible to solve for equilibrium
62:2418:131862:13:18:64:525:497:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:dynamics using local methods since the point around which to perturb the system is not known.
62:2419:131955:18:13:75:547:479:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:Global projection methods (Judd (1998)) avoid these problems by not relying on the deterministic
62:2420:132051:13:14:64:546:466:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:steady state.  Rather,  they directly approximate the transition and policy functions in the relevant
62:2421:132152:14:13:64:546:452:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:area of the state space.  Additional advantages of global nonlinear methods are greater flexibility in
62:2422:132254:13:14:64:546:439:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:dealing with highly nonlinear functions within the model such as probability distributions or option-like
62:2423:132359:14:37:64:100:425:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:payoffs.
62:2424:132367:37:25:64:240:388:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:B.1    Solution Procedure
62:2425:132392:25:26:64:448:363:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:The projection-based solution approach used in this paper has three main steps:
62:2426:132471:26:14:54:547:337:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:Step 1.Define approximating basis for the policy and transition functions.To approximate
62:2427:132559:14:13:94:547:323:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:these  unknown  functions,  we  discretize  the  state  space  and  use  multivariate  linear  interpola-
62:2428:132664:13:14:94:547:310:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:tion.  Our general solution framework provides an object-oriented MATLAB library that allows
62:2429:132756:14:13:94:547:296:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:approximation of arbitrary multivariate functions using linear interpolation, splines, or polyno-
62:2430:132853:13:14:94:547:283:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:mials.  For the model in this paper, splines or polynomials of various orders achieved inferior
62:2431:132948:14:23:94:347:269:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:results due to their lack of global shape preservation.
62:2432:133003:23:13:54:547:246:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:Step 2.Iteratively solve for the unknown functions.Given an initial guess for policy and transi-
62:2433:133099:13:14:94:547:233:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:tion functions, at each point in the discretized state space compute the current-period optimal
62:2434:133194:14:13:94:547:219:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:policies.  Using the solutions, compute the next iterate of the transition functions.  Repeat until
62:2435:133293:13:14:94:547:206:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:convergence.  The system of nonlinear equations at each point in the state space is solved us-
62:2436:133387:14:13:94:547:192:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:ing a standard nonlinear equation solver.  Kuhn-Tucker conditions can be rewritten as equality
62:2437:133481:13:14:94:547:179:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:constraints for this purpose.  This step is completely parallelized across points in the state space
62:2438:133581:14:22:94:186:165:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:within each iterate.
62:2439:133601:22:14:54:546:143:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:Step 3.Simulate the model for many periods using approximated functions.Verify that the
62:2440:133688:14:13:94:547:129:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:simulated time path stays within the bounds of the state space for which policy and transition
62:2441:133782:13:14:94:547:116:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:functions were computed.  Calculate relative Euler equation errors to assess the computational
62:2442:133876:14:14:94:547:102:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:accuracy of the solution.  If the simulated time path leaves the state space boundaries or errors
62:2443:133973:14:13:94:547:88:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:are too large, the solution procedure may have to be repeated with optimized grid bounds or
62:2444:134064:13:0:94:217:75:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:positioning of grid points.
63:2445:134093:0:33:75:373:715:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:We will now provide a more detailed description for each step.
63:2446:134155:33:25:64:240:682:12:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f6:Step 1The state space consists of
63:2447:134188:25:22:84:306:657:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:-  two exogenous state variables [ZAt,σω,t], and
63:2448:134236:22:25:84:355:635:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:-  five endogenous state variables [KBt,ABt,WIt,WSt,BGt].
63:2449:134293:25:14:64:546:610:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:We first discretizeZAtinto aNZA-state Markov chain using the Rouwenhorst (1995) method.  The
63:2450:134385:14:14:64:546:596:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:procedure chooses the productivity grid points{ZAj}NZAj=1and theNZA×NZAMarkov transition matrix
63:2451:134480:14:14:64:546:582:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:ΠZAbetween them to match the volatility and persistence of HP-detrended GDP. The dispersion of
63:2452:134574:14:13:64:546:568:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:idiosyncratic productivity shocksσω,tcan take on two realizations{σω,L,σω,H}as described in the
63:2453:134669:13:14:64:546:555:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:calibration section.  The 2 x 2 Markov transition matrix between these states is given by Πσω.  We
63:2454:134767:14:13:64:547:541:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:assume independence between both exogenous shocks.  Denote the set of theNx= 2NZAvalues the
63:2455:134858:13:0:64:325:528:11:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f8:exogenous state variables can take on asSx={ZAj}N
63:2456:134907:0:10:325:336:535:6:g_d0_f12:6:g_d0_f12:ZA
63:2457:134909:10:11:318:547:525:8:g_d0_f8:11:g_d0_f6:j=1×{σω,L,σω,H}, and the associated Markov
63:2458:134951:11:17:64:234:514:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:transition matrix Πx= ΠZA⊗Πσω.
63:2459:134981:17:14:75:547:497:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:One endogenous state variable can be eliminated for computational purposes since its value is implied
63:2460:135082:14:13:64:546:483:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:by the agents’ budget constraints, conditional on any four other state variables.  We eliminate saver
63:2461:135183:13:25:64:250:470:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:wealthWSt, which can be computed as
63:2462:135218:25:24:196:415:445:11:g_d0_f18:11:g_d0_f18:WSt= ΩA(ω∗t)(1 +δqmt)ABt+Mt−WIt+BGt.
63:2463:135254:24:14:64:546:421:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:Our solution algorithm requires approximation of continuous functions of the endogenous state vari-
63:2464:135353:14:14:64:546:407:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:ables.   Define  the  “true”  endogenous  state  space  of  the  model  as  follows:  if  each  endogenous  state
63:2465:135466:14:13:64:547:393:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:variableSt∈ {KBt,ABt,WIt,BGt}can  take  on  values  in  a  continuous  and  convex  subset  of  the  re-
63:2466:135570:13:14:64:546:380:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:als,  characterized  by  constant  state  boundaries,  [ ̄Sl, ̄Su],  then  the  endogenous  state  spaceSn=
63:2467:135677:14:17:64:500:366:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:[ ̄KBl, ̄KBu]×[ ̄ABl, ̄ABu]×[ ̄WIl, ̄WIu]×[ ̄BGl, ̄BGu].  The total state space is the setS=Sx×Sn.
63:2468:135775:17:14:75:546:349:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:To approximate any functionf:S →R, we form an univariate grid of (not necessarily equidistant)
63:2469:135869:14:16:64:547:335:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:strictly  increasing  points  for  each  endogenous  state  variables,  i.e.,  we  choose{KBj}NKj=1,{ABk}NAk=1,
63:2470:135980:16:14:64:547:319:11:g_d0_f9:11:g_d0_f6:{WIm}NWm=1, and{BGn}NGn=1.  These grid points are chosen to ensure that each grid covers the ergodic
63:2471:136080:14:13:64:546:305:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:distribution of the economy in its dimension, and to minimize computational errors, with more details
63:2472:136181:13:16:64:546:292:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f9:on the choice provided below.  Denote the set of all endogenous-state grid points asˆSn={KBj}NKj=1×
63:2473:136280:16:14:64:547:276:11:g_d0_f9:11:g_d0_f6:{ABk}NAk=1×{WIm}NWm=1×{BGn}NGn=1, and the total discretized state space asˆS=Sx×ˆSn.  This discretized
63:2474:136382:14:14:64:547:262:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:state space hasNS=Nx·NK·NA·NW·NGtotal points, where each point is a 5 x 1 vector as there
63:2475:136471:14:13:64:547:248:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:are 5 distinct state variables.  We can now approximate the smooth functionfif we know its values
63:2476:136568:13:0:64:92:235:11:g_d0_f9:8:g_d0_f8:{fj}N
63:2477:136573:0:10:93:98:242:6:g_d0_f12:6:g_d0_f12:S
63:2478:136574:10:15:85:445:232:8:g_d0_f8:11:g_d0_f6:j=1at each point ˆs∈ˆS, i.e.fj=f(ˆsj) by multivariate linear interpolation.
63:2479:136649:15:13:75:547:217:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:Our  solution  method  requires  approximation  of  of  three  sets  of  functions  defined  on  the  domain
63:2480:136757:13:0:64:440:204:11:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f8:of the state variables.  The first set of unknown functionsCP:S → P ⊆ RN
63:2481:136829:0:7:440:445:211:6:g_d0_f12:6:g_d0_f12:C
63:2482:136830:7:14:447:546:204:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:, withNCbeing the
63:2483:136847:14:13:64:546:190:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:number of policy variables, determines the values of endogenous objects specified in the equilibrium
63:2484:136947:13:14:64:546:177:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:definition at every point in the state space.  These are the prices,  agents’ choice variables,  and the
63:2485:137051:14:13:64:546:163:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:Lagrange multipliers on the portfolio constraints.  Specifically, the 12 policy functions are bond prices
63:2486:137156:13:14:64:546:150:11:g_d0_f18:11:g_d0_f6:qm(S),q(S),  investmentX(S),  consumptioncB(S),cS(S),  the bank dividenddI(S),  wageswB(S),
63:2487:137247:14:14:64:546:136:11:g_d0_f18:11:g_d0_f6:wS(S),  the  Lagrange  multipliers  for  the  bank  leverage  constraintλI(S)  and  no-shorting  constraint
63:2488:137354:14:13:64:546:122:11:g_d0_f18:11:g_d0_f6:μI(S), the multiplier for borrowers’ leverage constraintλB(S), and finally the multiplier on the savers’
63:2489:137458:13:14:64:547:109:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:no-shorting constraintμS(S).  There is an equal number of these unknown functions and nonlinear
63:2490:137553:14:17:64:318:95:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:functional equations, to be listed under step 2 below.
63:2491:137607:17:14:75:547:78:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:The second set of functionsCT:S×Sx→Sndetermine the next-period endogenous state variable
63:2492:137695:14:0:64:546:64:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:realizations as a function of the state in the current period and the next-period realization of exogenous
64:2493:137803:0:14:64:546:715:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:shocks.   There  is  one  transition  function  for  each  endogenous  state  variable,  corresponding  to  the
64:2494:137914:14:17:64:400:701:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:transition law for each state variable, also to be listed below in step 2.
64:2495:137988:17:14:75:547:684:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:The third set are forecasting functionsCF:S →F ⊆RNF, whereNFis the number of forecasting
64:2496:138076:14:13:64:546:670:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:variables.  They map the state into the set of variables sufficient to compute expectations terms in the
64:2497:138180:13:14:64:546:657:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:nonlinear functional equations that characterize equilibrium.  They partially coincide with the policy
64:2498:138282:14:14:64:546:643:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:functions, but include additional functions.  In particular, the forecasting functions for our model are
64:2499:138386:14:13:64:546:629:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:the  bond  priceqm(S),  investmentX(S),  consumptioncB(S),cS(S),  the  bank  dividenddI(S),  the
64:2500:138482:13:14:64:546:616:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:value functions of householdsVS(S),VB(S), and banksVI(S), the wage billw(S) =wB(S) +wS(S),
64:2501:138572:14:32:64:414:602:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:and the Lagrange multiplier on the borrowers’ leverage constraintλB(S).
64:2502:138643:32:14:64:547:570:12:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f6:Step 2Given an initial guessC0={C0P,C0T,C0F}, the algorithm to compute the equilibrium takes
64:2503:138735:14:26:64:156:556:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:the following steps.
64:2504:138755:26:24:76:525:530:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:A.Initializethe algorithm by setting the current iterateCm={CmP,CmT,CmF}={C0P,C0T,C0F}.

68:2819:146983:14:33:94:489:674:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:to reduce oscillation in function values in successive iterations.  Next, go to step B.
