68:2821:147166:13:14:64:547:628:11:g_d0_f18:11:g_d0_f6:Tini+Tperiod.  Since the exogenous shocks follow a discrete-time Markov chain with transition matrix
68:2822:147266:14:13:64:547:614:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:Πx, we can simulate the chain given any initial statex0using ̄T−1 uniform random numbers based on
68:2823:147363:13:14:64:546:601:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:standard techniques (we fix the seed of the random number generator to preserve comparability across
68:2824:147463:14:13:64:546:587:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:experiments). Using the simulated path{xt} ̄Tt=1, we can simulate the associated path of the endogenous
68:2825:147566:13:25:64:547:574:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:state variables given initial states0= [x0,KB0,AB0,WI0,WS0,BG0] by evaluating the transition functions
68:2826:147668:25:26:197:414:549:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f18:[KBt+1,ABt+1,WIt+1,WSt+1,BGt+1] =C∗T(st,xt+1),
68:2827:147714:26:14:64:546:523:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:to obtain a complete simulated path of model state variables{st} ̄Tt=1.  To remove any effect of the
68:2828:147814:14:13:64:547:509:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:initial conditions, we discard the firstTinipoints.  We then also evaluate the policy and forecasting
68:2829:147915:13:18:64:501:496:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:functions along the simulated sample path to obtain a complete sample path{st,Pt,ft} ̄Tt=1.
68:2830:148006:18:13:75:547:478:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:To assess the quality and accuracy of the solution, we perform two types of checks.  First, we verify
68:2831:148107:13:14:64:546:465:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:that all state variable realizations along the simulated path are within the bounds of the state variable
68:2832:148212:14:13:64:546:451:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:grids defined in step 1.  If the simulation exceeds the grid boundaries, we expand the grid bounds in
68:2833:148313:13:14:64:546:438:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:the violated dimensions, and restart the procedure at step 1.  Secondly, we compute relative errors for
68:2834:148416:14:13:64:546:424:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:all equations of the system (E1) – E(12) and the transition functions (T1) – (T4) along the simulated
68:2835:148517:13:14:64:546:411:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:path.  For equations involving expectations (such as (E1)), this requires evaluating the transition and
68:2836:148620:14:13:64:546:397:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:forecasting function as in step 2B at the current statest.  For each equation, we divide both sides by
68:2837:148722:13:30:64:496:384:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:a sensibly chosen endogenous quantity to yield “relative” errors; e.g., for (E1) we compute
68:2838:148813:30:0:113:129:354:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f9:1−
68:2839:148815:0:15:137:142:362:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:1
68:2840:148816:15:0:134:141:347:11:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f8:ˆqmj
68:2841:148820:0:10:149:156:367:11:g_d0_f11:11:g_d0_f11:(
68:2842:148821:10:7:156:198:357:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:ˆλBjF+ E
68:2843:148829:7:0:199:221:350:8:g_d0_f8:6:g_d0_f12:s′i,j|sj
68:2844:148837:0:10:224:231:367:11:g_d0_f11:11:g_d0_f11:{
68:2845:148838:10:0:236:480:357:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f11:ˆMBi,j[ΩA(ω∗i,j)(1−(1−θ)τΠ+δqmi,j)+fω(ω∗i,j)Fi,j]
68:2846:148887:0:13:479:493:367:11:g_d0_f11:11:g_d0_f11:})
68:2847:148889:13:31:495:498:354:11:g_d0_f18:11:g_d0_f18:,
68:2848:148890:31:14:64:546:323:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:using the same notation as in step 2B. These errors are small by construction when calculated at the
68:2849:148990:14:13:64:547:309:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:points of the discretized state gridˆS, since the algorithm under step 2 solved the system exactly at
68:2850:149091:13:14:64:546:296:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:those points.  However, the simulated path will likely visit many points that are between grid points,
68:2851:149193:14:14:64:547:282:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:at which the functionsC∗are approximated by interpolation.  Therefore, the relative errors indicate
68:2852:149292:14:13:64:546:268:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:the quality of the approximation in the relevant area of the state space.  We report average, median,
68:2853:149393:13:14:64:546:255:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:and tail errors for all equations.  If errors are too large during simulation, we investigate in which part
68:2854:149500:14:13:64:546:241:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:of the state space these high errors occur.  We then add additional points to the state variable grids
68:2855:149602:13:37:64:257:228:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:in those areas and repeat the procedure.
68:2856:149642:37:25:64:216:191:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:B.2    Implementation
68:2857:149663:25:14:64:546:166:12:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f6:Solving the system of equations.We solve system of nonlinear equations at each point in the
68:2858:149754:14:13:64:546:152:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:state space using a standard nonlinear equation solver (MATLAB’s fsolve).  This nonlinear equation
68:2859:149852:13:14:64:546:139:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:solver uses a variant of Newton’s method to find a “zero” of the system.  We employ several simple
68:2860:149950:14:13:64:546:125:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:modifications of the system (E1) – E(12) to avoid common pitfalls at this step of the solution procedure.
68:2861:150055:13:14:64:546:112:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:Nonlinear  equation  solver  are  notoriously  bad  at  dealing  with  complementary  slackness  conditions
68:2862:150162:14:13:64:546:98:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:associated with constraint, such as (E8) – E(11).  Judd, Kubler, and Schmedders (2002) discuss the
68:2863:150260:13:14:64:546:85:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:reasons for this and also show how Kuhn-Tucker conditions can be rewritten as additive equations for
68:2864:150360:14:0:64:546:71:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:this purpose. For example, consider the bank’s Euler Equation for risk-free bonds and the Kuhn-Tucker
69:2865:150463:0:27:64:236:715:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:condition for its leverage constraint:
69:2866:150501:27:7:213:346:688:11:g_d0_f6:6:g_d0_f14:ˆqfj(1−ˆλIj) +τΠˆrfj−κ= Es′
69:2867:150528:7:0:344:362:681:6:g_d0_f12:6:g_d0_f12:i,j|sj
69:2868:150534:0:9:365:370:700:11:g_d0_f11:11:g_d0_f11:[
69:2869:150535:9:0:376:393:691:11:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f8:ˆMIi,j
69:2870:150541:0:24:393:398:700:11:g_d0_f11:11:g_d0_f11:]
69:2871:150542:24:12:223:230:676:11:g_d0_f11:11:g_d0_f11:(
69:2872:150543:12:0:230:296:664:11:g_d0_f18:8:g_d0_f8:ξˆqmjˆAIj+ ˆqfjˆBIj
69:2873:150562:0:9:299:306:676:11:g_d0_f11:11:g_d0_f11:)
69:2874:150563:9:33:307:338:667:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:ˆλIj= 0
69:2875:150570:33:17:64:546:634:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:Now  define  an  auxiliary  variablehj∈ Rand  two  functions  of  this  variable,  such  thatˆλI,+j=
69:2876:150670:17:13:64:546:617:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:max{0,hj}3andˆλI,−j=  max{0,−hj}3.   Clearly,  ifhj<0,  thenˆλI,+j=  0  andˆλI,−j>0,  and  vice
69:2877:150765:13:28:64:490:604:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:versa forhj>0.  Using these definitions, the two equations above can be transformed to:
69:2878:150852:28:7:209:351:576:11:g_d0_f6:6:g_d0_f14:ˆqfj(1−ˆλI,+j) +τΠˆrfj−κ= Es′
69:2879:150881:7:0:349:367:569:6:g_d0_f12:6:g_d0_f12:i,j|sj
69:2880:150887:0:9:370:375:588:11:g_d0_f11:11:g_d0_f11:[
69:2881:150888:9:0:380:397:579:11:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f8:ˆMIi,j
69:2882:150894:0:12:398:403:588:11:g_d0_f11:11:g_d0_f11:]
69:2883:150895:12:22:524:546:576:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:(K1)
69:2884:150899:22:25:220:546:554:11:g_d0_f18:11:g_d0_f6:ξˆqmjˆAIj+ ˆqfjˆBIj−ˆλI,−j= 0(K2)
69:2885:150932:25:15:64:547:529:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:The  solution  variable  for  the  nonlinear  equation  solver  corresponding  to  the  multiplier  ishj.   The
69:2886:151043:15:13:64:547:514:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:solver can choose positivehjto make the constraint binding (ˆλI,−j= 0), in which caseˆλI,+jtakes on
69:2887:151142:13:15:64:547:501:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:the value of the Lagrange multiplier.  Or the solver can choose negativehjto make the constraint
69:2888:151238:15:18:64:485:486:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:non-binding (ˆλI,+j= 0), in which caseˆλI,−jcan take on any value that makes (K2) hold.
69:2889:151325:18:14:75:547:468:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:Similarly, certain solution variables are restricted to positive values due to the economic structure of
69:2890:151429:14:13:64:546:454:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:the problem.  For example, with power utility consumption must be positive.  To avoid that the solver
69:2891:151530:13:14:64:547:441:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:tries out negative consumption values (and thus utility becomes ill-defined), we use log(ˆcnj),n=B,S,
69:2892:151631:14:13:64:546:427:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:as solution variable for the solver.  This means the solver can make consumption arbitrarily small, but
69:2893:151734:13:18:64:126:414:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:not negative.
69:2894:151747:18:13:75:547:396:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:The nonlinear equation solver needs to compute the Jacobian of the system at each step.  Numerical
69:2895:151845:13:14:64:546:383:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:central-difference (forward-difference) approximation of the Jacobian can be inaccurate and is compu-
69:2896:151946:14:13:64:547:369:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:tationally costly because it requires 2N+1 (N+1) evaluations of the system, withNbeing the number
69:2897:152043:13:14:64:546:356:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:of variables, whereas analytically computed Jacobians are exact and require only one evaluation.  We
69:2898:152143:14:13:64:546:342:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:follow Elenev (2016) in “pre-computing” all forecasting functions in step 2B of the algorithm, so that
69:2899:152245:13:14:64:546:329:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:we can calculate the Jacobian of the system analytically.  To do so,  we employ the Symbolic Math
69:2900:152342:14:14:64:546:315:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:Toolbox in MATLAB, passing the analytic Jacobian to fsolve at the beginning of step 2C. This greatly
69:2901:152442:14:32:64:173:301:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:speeds up calculations.
69:2902:152465:32:13:64:547:269:12:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f6:Grid configuration.We choose to include borrower wealthWBtas state variable instead of bor-
69:2903:152556:13:14:64:188:256:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:rower debtABt, defined as
69:2904:152581:14:20:253:358:242:11:g_d0_f18:11:g_d0_f18:WBt=ptKBt−qmtABt,
69:2905:152598:20:13:64:546:222:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:such that the total set of endogenous state variables is [KBt,WBt,WIt,WSt,BGt].  Keeping track of bor-
69:2906:152700:13:14:64:546:209:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:rower wealthWBtinstead of debtABtturns out to have better properties for numerical approximation
69:2907:152796:14:13:64:546:195:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:and the same information content.  The reason is that borrower wealth is much more stable in the
69:2908:152892:13:14:64:546:182:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:dynamics of the model than borrower debt, since borrower debt and capital are strongly correlated
69:2909:152989:14:13:64:546:168:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:reflecting borrowers’ optimal investment and leverage choices.  Recall that one endogenous state vari-
69:2910:153091:13:14:64:546:155:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:able can be eliminated because of the adding-up property of budget constraints in combination with
69:2911:153189:14:14:64:547:141:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:market clearing.  We choose to eliminate saver wealthWS.  The grid points in each state dimension
69:2912:153286:14:22:64:128:127:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:are as follows
69:2913:153300:22:14:82:547:105:11:g_d0_f9:11:g_d0_f6:•ZA:We discretizeZAtinto a 5-state Markov chain using the Rouwenhorst (1995) method.  The
69:2914:153389:14:13:94:547:91:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:procedure chooses the productivity grid points{ZAj}5j=1and the 5×5 Markov transition matrix
69:2915:153480:13:14:94:547:78:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:ΠZAbetween them to match the volatility and persistence of HP-detrended GDP. This yields
69:2916:153568:14:0:94:368:64:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:the possible realizations:  [0.957,0.978,1.000,1.022,1.045].
70:2917:153630:0:23:82:255:715:11:g_d0_f9:11:g_d0_f6:•σω:[0.095,0.175] (see calibration)
70:2918:153665:23:22:82:290:692:11:g_d0_f9:11:g_d0_f6:•KB:[1.84,1.98,2.05,2.10,2.26,2.45,2.70]
70:2919:153705:22:23:82:448:670:11:g_d0_f9:11:g_d0_f6:•WB:[1.00,1.16,1.20,1.23,1.24,1.285,1.33,1.35,1.375,1.41,1.50,1.60,1.70]
70:2920:153777:23:27:82:113:647:11:g_d0_f9:11:g_d0_f20:•WI:
70:2921:153781:27:17:104:549:620:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f18:[−0.02,−0.01,0,0.005,0.01,0.015,0.02,0.025,0.03,0.035,0.04,0.045,0.05,0.055,0.06,0.065,...
70:2922:153871:17:29:296:537:603:11:g_d0_f18:11:g_d0_f6:...,0.07,0.075,0.08,0.10,0.125,0.15,0.25,0.3,0.38]
70:2923:153921:29:26:82:417:574:11:g_d0_f9:11:g_d0_f6:•BG:[−0.2000,−0.02,0,0.1833,0.4667,0.7500,1.0333,1.3167,1.4000]
70:2924:153984:26:14:75:547:548:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:The  total  state  space  grid  has  204,750  points.   As  pointed  out  by  several  previous  studies  such
70:2925:154094:14:13:64:546:534:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:as Kubler and Schmedders (2003), portfolio constraints lead to additional computational challenges
70:2926:154192:13:14:64:546:521:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:since  portfolio  policies  may  not  be  smooth  functions  of  state  variables  due  to  occasionally  binding
70:2927:154305:14:14:64:546:507:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:constraints.  Hence we cluster grid points in areas of the state space where constraints transition from
70:2928:154409:14:13:64:547:493:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:slack to binding. Our policy functions are particularly nonlinear in bank net worthWIt, since the status
70:2929:154513:13:14:64:546:480:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:of the bank leverage constraint (binding or not binding) depends predominantly on this state variable.
70:2930:154615:14:13:64:547:466:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:To achieve acceptable accuracy, we have to specify a very dense grid forWI, as can be seen above.
70:2931:154712:13:14:64:546:453:11:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f8:Also note that the lower end of theWIgrid includes some negative values.  Negative realizations ofWI
70:2932:154812:14:13:64:546:439:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:can occur in severe financial crisis episodes.  Recall thatWIis the beginning-of-period net worth of all
70:2933:154916:13:14:64:546:426:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:banks.  Depending on the realization of their idiosyncratic payout shock, banks decide whether or not
70:2934:155017:14:13:64:546:412:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:to default.  Thus the model contains two reasons why banks may not default despite initial negative
70:2935:155116:13:14:64:546:399:11:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f8:net worth:  (i) positive idiosyncratic shocks, and (ii) positive franchise value.  The lower bound ofWI
70:2936:155219:14:13:64:546:385:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:needs  to  be  low  enough  such  that  bank  net  worth  is  not  artificially  truncated  during  crises,  but  it
70:2937:155335:13:14:64:546:372:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:must not be so low that, given such low initial net worth, banks cannot be recapitalized to get back to
70:2938:155438:14:14:64:546:358:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:positive net worth.  Thus the “right” lower bound depends on the strength of the equity issuance cost
70:2939:155539:14:32:64:535:344:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:and other parameters.  Finding the right value for the lower bound is a matter of experimentation.
70:2940:155637:32:14:64:547:312:12:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f6:Generating an initial guess and iteration scheme.To find a good initial guess for the policy,
70:2941:155730:14:13:64:546:298:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:forecasting, and transition functions, we solve the deterministic “steady-state” of the model under the
70:2942:155833:13:14:64:546:285:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:assumption that the bank leverage constraint is binding and government debt/GDP is 40%.  We then
70:2943:155929:14:14:64:546:271:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:initialize all functions to their steady-state values, for all points in the state space.  Note that the only
70:2944:156038:14:13:64:546:257:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:role of the steady-state calculation is to generate an initial guess that enables the nonlinear equation
70:2945:156142:13:14:64:546:244:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:solver to find solutions at (almost) all points during the first iteration of the solution algorithm.  In
70:2946:156247:14:17:64:392:230:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:our experience, the steady state delivers a good enough initial guess.
70:2947:156317:17:14:75:547:213:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:In case the solver cannot find solutions for some points during the initial iterations, we revisit such
70:2948:156420:14:13:64:546:199:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:points at the end of each iteration.  We try to solve the system at these “failed” points using as initial
70:2949:156526:13:14:64:546:186:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:guess the solution of the closest neighboring point at which the solver was successful.  This method
70:2950:156626:14:17:64:438:172:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:works well to speed up convergence and eventually find solutions at all points.
70:2951:156705:17:14:75:547:155:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:To further speed up computation time, we run the initial 100 iterations with a coarser state space
70:2952:156803:14:13:64:546:141:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:grid (19,500 points total). After these iterations, the algorithm is usually close to convergence; however,
70:2953:156910:13:14:64:546:128:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:the accuracy during simulation would be too low.  Therefore,  we initialize the finer (final) solution
70:2954:157012:14:14:64:546:114:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:grid using the policy, forecasting, and transition function obtained after 100 coarse grid iterations.  We
70:2955:157118:14:17:64:401:100:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:then run the algorithm for at most 40 more iterations on the fine grid.
70:2956:157189:17:14:75:547:83:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:To determine convergence, we check absolute errors in the value functions of households and banks,
70:2957:157287:14:0:64:546:69:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:(V1) – V(3).  Out of all functions we approximate during the solution procedure,  these exhibit the
71:2958:157388:0:14:64:546:715:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:slowest convergence.  We stop the solution algorithm when the maximum absolute difference between
71:2959:157485:14:13:64:546:701:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:two iterations, and for all three functions and all points in the state space, falls below 1e-3 and the
71:2960:157588:13:14:64:546:688:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:mean distance falls below 1e-4.  For appropriately chosen grid boundaries, the algorithm will converge
71:2961:157690:14:17:64:203:674:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:within the final 40 iterations.
71:2962:157721:17:14:75:547:657:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:In some cases, our grid boundaries are wider than necessary, in the sense that the simulated economy
71:2963:157821:14:14:64:546:643:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:never visits the areas near the boundary on its equilibrium path.  Local convergence in those areas
71:2964:157920:14:13:64:546:629:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:is usually very slow, but not relevant for the equilibrium path of the economy.  If the algorithm has
71:2965:158021:13:14:64:546:616:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:not achieved convergence after the 40 additional iterations on the fine grid, we nonetheless stop the
71:2966:158122:14:13:64:546:602:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:procedure and simulate the economy.  If the resulting simulation produces low relative errors (see step
71:2967:158225:13:14:64:546:589:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:3 of the solution procedure),  we accept the solution.  After the 140 iterations described above,  our
71:2968:158327:14:13:64:546:575:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:simulated model economies either achieve acceptable accuracy in relative errors, or if not, the cause is
71:2969:158431:13:14:64:546:562:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:a badly configured state grid.  In the latter case, we need to improve the grid and restart the solution
71:2970:158535:14:13:64:546:548:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:procedure.  Additional iterations, beyond 100 on the coarse and 40 on the fine grid, do not change any
71:2971:158637:13:18:64:448:535:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:statistics of the simulated equilibrium path for any of the simulations we report.
71:2972:158719:18:13:75:547:517:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:We  implement  the  algorithm  in  MATLAB  and  run  the  code  on  a  high-performance  computing
71:2973:158817:13:14:64:546:504:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:(HPC) cluster.  As mentioned above, the nonlinear system of equations can be solved in parallel at
71:2974:158915:14:14:64:546:490:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:each point.  We parallelize across 28 CPU cores of a single HPC node.  From computing the initial
71:2975:159012:14:13:64:546:476:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:guess and analytic Jacobian to simulating the solved model, the total running time for the benchmark
71:2976:159112:13:14:64:546:463:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:calibration is about 2 hours and 40 minutes.  Calibrations that exhibit more financial fragility and/or
71:2977:159215:14:32:64:272:449:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:macro volatility converge up to 15% slower.
71:2978:159258:32:14:64:547:417:12:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f6:Simulation.To  obtain  the  quantitative  results,  we  simulate  the  model  for  10,000  periods  after
71:2979:159363:14:14:64:546:403:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:a  “burn-in”  phase  of  500  periods.   The  starting  point  of  the  simulation  is  the  ergodic  mean  of  the
71:2980:159478:14:13:64:546:389:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:state  variables.   As  described  in  detail  above,  we  verify  that  the  simulated  time  path  stays  within
71:2981:159592:13:14:64:546:376:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:the bounds of the state space for which the policy functions were computed.  We fix the seed of the
71:2982:159691:14:13:64:546:362:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:random number generator so that we use the same sequence of exogenous shock realizations for each
71:2983:159788:13:18:64:178:349:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:parameter combination.
71:2984:159810:18:13:75:547:331:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:To produce impulse response function (IRF) graphs, we simulate 10,000 different paths of 25 periods
71:2985:159909:13:14:64:546:318:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:each.   In  the  initial  period,  we  set  the  endogenous  state  variables  to  several  different  values  that
71:2986:160024:14:13:64:546:304:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:reflect the ergodic distribution of the states.  We use a clustering algorithm to represent the ergodic
71:2987:160127:13:14:64:546:291:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:distribution non-parametrically.  We fix the initial exogenous shock realization to mean productivity
71:2988:160228:14:13:64:546:277:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:(ZA=  1)  and  low  uncertainty  (σω,low).   The  “impulse”  in  the  second  period  is  either  only  a  bad
71:2989:160338:13:14:64:546:264:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:productivity shock (ZA= 0.978) for non-financial recessions, or both lowZAand a high uncertainty
71:2990:160434:14:14:64:546:250:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:shock (σω,hi) for financial recessions.  For the remaining 23 periods, the simulation evolves according
71:2991:160537:14:13:64:546:236:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:to the stochastic law of motion of the shocks.  In the IRF graphs, we plot the median path across the
71:2992:160638:13:37:64:254:223:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:10,000 paths given the initial condition.
71:2993:160679:37:25:64:268:186:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:B.3    Evaluating the solution
71:2994:160709:25:13:64:547:161:12:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f6:Equation errors.Our main measure to assess the accuracy of the solution are relative equation
71:2995:160802:13:14:64:546:148:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:errors calculated as described in step 3 of the solution procedure.  Table 6 reports the median error,
71:2996:160904:14:14:64:547:134:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:the 95thpercentile of the error distribution, the 99th, and 100thpercentiles during the 10,000 period
71:2997:161005:14:13:64:546:120:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:simulation of the model.  Median and 75th percentile errors are small for all equations.  Equations
71:2998:161104:13:14:64:546:107:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:(E5) – (E6) and (E9) have elevated maximum errors.  These errors are caused by a bad approximation
71:2999:161202:14:13:64:547:93:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:of the bank’s Lagrange multiplierλIin rarely occurring states.  It is possible to reduce these errors by
71:3000:161306:13:14:64:546:80:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:placing more grid points in those areas of the state space.  In our experience, adding points to eliminate
71:3001:161412:14:0:64:546:66:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:the tail errors has little to no effect on any of the results we report.  Since it increases computation

72:3023:162433:12:37:165:259:406:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:text and appendix A.
72:3024:162453:37:33:64:343:369:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:times nonetheless, we chose the current grid configuration.
72:3025:162512:33:13:64:546:336:12:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f6:Policy function plots.We further visually inspect policy functions to gauge whether the approx-
72:3026:162607:13:14:64:546:323:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:imated functions have the smoothness and monotonicity properties implied by our choices of utility
72:3027:162705:14:13:64:546:309:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:and adjustment cost functions.  Such plots also allow us to see the effect of binding constraints on
72:3028:162805:13:14:64:546:296:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:prices and quantities.  For example, figure 7 shows investment by firms and the Lagrange multiplier on
72:3029:162907:14:14:64:546:282:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:the bank’s leverage constraint.  It is obvious from the graphs that a binding intermediary constraint
72:3030:163008:14:13:64:546:268:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:restricts investment.  The intermediary constraint becomes binding for low values of intermediary net
72:3031:163109:13:14:64:546:255:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:worth.  Further note the interaction with borrower-entrepreneur net worth:  holding fixed intermediary
72:3032:163211:14:32:64:456:241:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:net worth, the constraint is more likely to become biding for low borrower wealth.
72:3033:163293:32:14:64:546:209:12:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f6:State space histogram plots.We also create histogram plots for the endogenous state variables,
72:3034:163387:14:14:64:546:195:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:overlaid with the placement of grid points.  These types of plots allow us to check that the simulated
72:3035:163489:14:13:64:546:181:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:path of the economy does not violate the state grid boundaries.  It further helps us to determine where
72:3036:163592:13:0:64:451:168:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:to place grid points.  Histogram plots for the benchmark economy are in figure 8.

73:3065:164218:35:33:64:282:412:17:g_d0_f2:17:g_d0_f2:C    Calibration Appendix
73:3066:164243:33:25:64:322:379:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:C.1    Parameter Sensitivity Analysis
73:3067:164280:25:13:64:546:354:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:In  a  complex,  non-linear  structural  general  equilibrium  model  like  ours,  it  is  often  difficult  to  see
73:3068:164396:13:14:64:546:341:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:precisely which features of the data drive the ultimate results.  This appendix follows the approach
73:3069:164496:14:13:64:546:327:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:advocated  by  Andrews,  Gentzkow,  and  Shapiro  (2017)  to  report  how  key  moments  are  affected  by
73:3070:164602:13:14:64:546:314:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:changes  in  the  model’s  key  parameters,  in  the  hope  of  improving  the  transparency  of  the  results.
73:3071:164713:14:17:64:517:300:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:Structural identification of parameters and sensitivity of results are two sides of the same coin.
73:3072:164811:17:14:75:546:283:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:Consider a generic vector of momentsmwhich depends on a generic parameter vectorθ.  Letιibe
73:3073:164902:14:13:64:546:269:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:a selector vector of the same length asθtaking a value of 1 in thei’th position and zero elsewhere.
73:3074:165001:13:14:64:546:256:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:Denote the parameter choices in the benchmark calibration by a superscriptb.  For each parameter
73:3075:165097:14:14:64:546:242:11:g_d0_f18:11:g_d0_f6:θi, we solve the model once forθb◦eιiεand once forθb◦e−ιiε.  We then report the symmetric finite
73:3076:165193:14:10:64:112:228:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:difference:
73:3077:165204:10:0:216:230:218:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:log
73:3078:165207:0:9:232:237:227:11:g_d0_f11:11:g_d0_f11:(
73:3079:165208:9:0:237:294:218:11:g_d0_f20:11:g_d0_f6:m(θb◦eιiε)
73:3080:165218:0:9:294:299:227:11:g_d0_f11:11:g_d0_f11:)
73:3081:165219:9:0:301:326:218:11:g_d0_f9:11:g_d0_f6:−log
73:3082:165223:0:9:328:333:227:11:g_d0_f11:11:g_d0_f11:(
73:3083:165224:9:0:333:389:218:11:g_d0_f20:11:g_d0_f6:m(θb◦eιiε)
73:3084:165234:0:25:390:395:227:11:g_d0_f11:11:g_d0_f11:)
73:3085:165235:25:15:300:311:202:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f18:2ε
73:3086:165237:15:14:64:547:187:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:We setε=.01, or 1% of the benchmark parameter value.  The resulting quantities are elasticities of
73:3087:165335:14:17:64:230:173:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:moments to structural parameters.
73:3088:165368:17:14:75:547:156:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:To avoid excessive reporting, we focus on 8 key parameters and 13 key moments.  The parameters
73:3089:165462:14:13:64:546:142:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:are: (1) the equity adjustment cost parameterσI, (2) the cost of default parameterζ, (3) the mortgage
73:3090:165563:13:14:64:546:129:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:duration parameterδ, (4) the capital adjustment cost parameterφ, (5) the idiosyncratic bank profit
73:3091:165661:14:14:64:546:115:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:riskσε,  (6)  the  dispersion  of  TFP  shocks  in  the  normal  stateσω,L,  and  (7)  the  dispersion  of  TFP
73:3092:165772:14:13:64:547:101:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:shocks  in  the  crisis  stateσω,H,  and  (8)  the  risk  aversion  coefficient  (of  both  borrowers  and  savers,
73:3093:165887:13:14:64:547:88:11:g_d0_f18:11:g_d0_f6:σB=σS).  Each panel of Figure 9 lists the same 14 moments and shows the elasticity of the moments
73:3094:165984:14:0:64:546:74:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:to one of the eight parameters.  As an aside, the movements in the excess bond return in response to

74:3121:166507:35:14:64:546:424:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:multiple parameters appear to be large but they are only large relative to a fairly small baseline level
74:3122:166611:14:13:64:546:410:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:of excess returns of 30 basis points per year.  For consistency, we report percentage changes, which are
74:3123:166715:13:18:64:194:397:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:unit-free, in every moment.
74:3124:166742:18:14:75:547:379:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:A higher equity adjustment cost in the first panel, strongly increases the excess return on corporate
74:3125:166843:14:13:64:546:365:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:bonds, the moment chosen to pin down this parameter.  It also strongly decreases bank bankruptcies.
74:3126:166942:13:14:64:547:352:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:IncreasingσIis akin to an increase in the risk aversion of banks,  consistent with the discussion in
74:3127:167042:14:13:64:546:338:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:Section  D.6  below.   Higher  risk  aversion  naturally  results  in  a  larger  equilibrium  compensation  for
74:3128:167154:13:18:64:534:325:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:bearing credit risk and a tendency for banks to stay farther away from their borrowing constraint.
74:3129:167252:18:13:75:547:307:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:A higher value for the bankruptcy cost parameterζnaturally results in higher losses given default,
74:3130:167350:13:14:64:546:294:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:the moment chosen to pin down this parameter.  While there is a modest decline in the default rate,
74:3131:167449:14:13:64:546:280:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:the overall loss rate still goes up.  There are more bank bankruptcies and a higher excess return on
74:3132:167549:13:14:64:546:267:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:corporate bonds, given the increased quantity of credit risk.  Corporate leverage declines in the wake
74:3133:167651:14:13:64:546:253:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:of costlier credit.  With less corporate debt and unchanged financial sector leverage, the banking sector
74:3134:167756:13:14:64:546:240:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:shrinks (Deposits/Y). Lower corporate debt also results in a lower capital stock and a less volatile
74:3135:167856:14:18:64:347:226:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:economy, which improves risk sharing (MU vol goes down).
74:3136:167912:18:13:75:547:208:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:An increase in the corporate debt maturity parameterδmost directly affects bond duration,  the
74:3137:168006:13:14:64:546:195:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:elasticity  of  corporate  bond  prices  to  interest  rates  (not  reported).   An  increase  in  bond  duration
74:3138:168119:14:13:64:546:181:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:increases the excess return on bonds.  With increased duration, firms become better duration-matched
74:3139:168219:13:14:64:546:168:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:since the duration of their capital assets is high.  As a result, firm leverage slightly increases despite
74:3140:168325:14:17:64:175:154:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:the higher cost of debt.
74:3141:168349:17:14:75:546:137:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:The fourth panel explores changes in the capital adjustment cost parameterψ.  Higher capital ad-
74:3142:168445:14:13:64:546:123:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:justment costs naturally reduce investment volatility.  They raise consumption volatility.  The increase
74:3143:168549:13:14:64:546:110:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:in capital adjustment costs increases the volatility in the price of capital (not reported), which causes
74:3144:168654:14:13:64:546:96:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:risk-averse firms to de-lever.  Lower leverage reduces the quantity of default risk as well as the credit
74:3145:168759:13:14:64:546:83:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:spread  unconditionally,  but  makes  realized  excess  returns  lower  in  crises,  eroding  bank  capital  and
74:3146:168871:14:0:64:546:69:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:increasing expected excess returns enough to increase them unconditionally as well.  With more risk

75:3179:169637:18:13:75:546:288:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:Panel five increases the volatility of idiosyncratic bank profit shocksσ-.  That most directly affects
75:3180:169739:13:14:64:546:275:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:bank bankruptcies, which is how the parameter is calibrated.  The banks’ leverage constraint binds

75:3185:170170:14:14:64:546:203:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:between  the  low  and  the  high  state  thereby  reducing  the  aggregate  risk  in  the  economy,  while  the
75:3186:170282:14:13:64:546:189:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:latter  change  increases  the  gap.   The  reduction  in  aggregate  risk  is  consistent  with  a  reduction  in
75:3187:170396:13:14:64:546:176:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:macroeconomic volatility and an improvement in risk sharing (a reduction in MU vol).  Financial firms
75:3188:170497:14:13:64:546:162:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:respond to the safer macro-economic environment and the higher excess bond returns by increasing
75:3189:170593:13:18:64:462:149:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:their risk taking, which results in higher financial sector leverage and bankruptcies.
75:3190:170679:18:13:75:547:131:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:Panel  eight  studies  an  increase  in  the  risk  aversion  of  both  types  of  households  in  the  economy,
75:3191:170791:13:14:64:546:118:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:from the benchmark value of one.  The intertemporal elasticity of substitution stays unchanged at one.
75:3192:170893:14:13:64:546:104:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:The effect of this change is orders of magnitude smaller than the effect of other parameter changes.
75:3193:170993:13:14:64:546:91:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:Corporate  leverage  and  defaults  go  down.   The  financial  leverage  constraint  becomes  binding  more
75:3194:171101:14:0:64:546:77:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:frequently, as intermediating has become more profitable as witnessed by the increase in the excess
76:3195:171202:0:37:64:124:715:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:bond return.
76:3196:171214:37:25:64:305:678:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:C.2    Long-term Corporate Bonds
76:3197:171246:25:14:64:546:653:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:Our model’s corporate bonds are geometrically declining perpetuities, and as such have no principal.
76:3198:171346:14:13:64:546:639:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:The issuer of one unit of the bond at timetpromises to pay the holder 1 at timet+ 1,δat time
76:3199:171438:13:14:64:547:626:11:g_d0_f18:11:g_d0_f6:t+ 2,δ2at timet+ 3, and so on.  Issuers must hold enough capital to collateralize the face value of
76:3200:171537:14:13:64:547:612:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:the bond, given byF=θ1−δ, a constant parameter that does not depend on any state variable of the
76:3201:171633:13:14:64:546:599:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:economy.  Real life bonds have a finite maturity and a principal payment.  They also have a vintage
76:3202:171732:14:13:64:546:585:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:(year of issuance), whereas our bonds combine all vintages in one variable.  This appendix explains
76:3203:171831:13:18:64:542:572:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:how to map the geometric bonds in our model into real-world bonds by choosing values forδandθ.
76:3204:171925:18:13:75:547:554:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:Our model’s corporate loan/bond refers to the entire pool of all outstanding corporate loans/bonds.
76:3205:172024:13:14:64:546:541:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:To proxy for this pool, we use investment-grade and high-yield indices constructed by Bank of Amer-
76:3206:172123:14:13:64:546:527:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:ica Merill Lynch (BofAML) and Barclays Capital (BarCap).  For the BofAML indices (Datastream
76:3207:172215:13:14:64:546:514:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:Codes LHYIELD and LHCCORP for investment grade and high-yield corporate bonds, respectively)
76:3208:172307:14:14:64:546:500:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:we obtain a time series of monthly market values, durations (the sensitivity of prices to interest rates),
76:3209:172413:14:13:64:546:486:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:weighted-average maturity (WAM), and weighted average coupons (WAC) for January 1997 until De-
76:3210:172507:13:14:64:546:473:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:cember 2015.  For the BarCap indices (C0A0 and H0A0 for investment grade and high-yield corporate
76:3211:172604:14:17:64:546:459:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:bonds, respectively), we obtain a time series of option-adjusted spreads over the Treasury yield curve.
76:3212:172707:17:14:75:547:442:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:First,  we  use  market  values  of  the  BofAML  investment  grade  and  high-yield  portfolios  to  create

77:3253:173971:14:13:64:547:701:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:zero-coupon bond i.e.  borrowing some amount today (the principal) and repaying itDtyears from
77:3254:174065:13:10:64:547:688:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:now.  The principal of this loan is just the price of the correspondingDtmaturity zero-coupon bond
77:3255:174163:10:8:81:85:678:8:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f4:1
77:3256:174164:8:15:65:99:670:8:g_d0_f4:6:g_d0_f12:(1+rt)Dt
77:3257:174172:15:13:75:546:655:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:We set the “principal”Fof one unit of the geometric bond to be some fractionθof the undiscounted
77:3258:174268:13:37:64:234:642:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:sum of all its cash flowsθ1−δ, where
77:3259:174304:37:0:246:263:605:11:g_d0_f18:11:g_d0_f6:θ=
77:3260:174306:0:14:270:275:612:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:1
77:3261:174307:14:0:268:277:598:11:g_d0_f18:11:g_d0_f18:N
77:3262:174308:0:27:283:305:619:8:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f11:2015.12∑
77:3263:174316:27:0:281:314:592:8:g_d0_f8:8:g_d0_f4:t=1997.1
77:3264:174324:0:14:337:342:612:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:1
77:3265:174325:14:30:317:362:598:11:g_d0_f6:6:g_d0_f12:(1 +rt)Dt
77:3266:174334:30:38:75:227:568:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:We getθ= 0.582 andF= 9.18.
77:3267:174360:38:24:64:212:530:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:C.3    LTV constraint
77:3268:174381:24:14:64:546:506:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:The cost of bankruptcy induces banks to limit leverage.  In the computation of the model solution, we
77:3269:174482:14:24:64:491:492:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:additionally impose a hard constraint on leverage.  This is a standard leverage constraint:
77:3270:174573:24:25:206:546:468:11:g_d0_f18:11:g_d0_f6:FABt+1≤Φpt(1−(1−τBΠ)δK)ΩA(ω∗t)KBt.(59)
77:3271:174611:25:13:64:547:443:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:The borrowing constraint in (59) caps the face value of debt at the end of the period,FABt+1, to a
77:3272:174709:13:14:64:546:430:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f9:fraction of the market value of the available capital units after default and depreciation,pt(1−(1−
77:3273:174808:14:13:64:547:416:11:g_d0_f18:11:g_d0_f6:τBΠ)δK)ΩA(ω∗t)KBt, where Φ is the maximum leverage ratio.  With such a constraint, declines in capital
77:3274:174910:13:14:64:546:403:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:prices (in bad times) tighten borrowing constraints, as in Kiyotaki and Moore (1997).  The constraint
77:3275:175011:14:18:64:330:389:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:(59) imposes a hard upper bound on borrower leverage.
77:3276:175064:18:13:75:546:371:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:We  set  the  maximum  LTV  ratio  parameter  Φ  =  0.45.   This  value  is  just  large  enough  so  that
77:3277:175170:13:14:64:546:358:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:the LTV constraint never binds during expansions and non-financial recessions.  In the simulation of
77:3278:175270:14:13:64:546:344:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:the benchmark model, the borrower’s LTV constraint binds in 3% of financial recessions.  The LTV
77:3279:175366:13:14:64:546:331:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:constraint limits corporate borrowing as a fraction of the market value of capital.  We set Φ to match
77:3280:175468:14:13:64:546:317:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:the volatility of corporate debt-to-GDP of the non-financial sector, which is 5.2% in the data and 4.3%
77:3281:175571:13:18:64:127:304:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:in the model.
77:3282:175584:18:13:75:547:286:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:We have verified that relaxing this constraint to the extent that it is never binding does not signif-
77:3283:175686:13:14:64:546:273:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:icantly affect the results.  For example, setting the maximum leverage ratio to Φ =.55 yields almost
77:3284:175786:14:13:64:546:259:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:identical  results.   We  include  the  constraint  for  comparability  with  the  existing  literature  that  has
77:3285:175900:13:14:64:546:246:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:emphasized  the  financial  accelerator  operating  through  capital  prices.   In  our  setup  the  main  force
77:3286:176012:14:37:64:528:232:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:limiting corporate leverage is a standard trade-off between the benefits and costs of debt finance.
77:3287:176111:37:25:64:378:195:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:C.4    Measuring Labor Income Tax Revenue
77:3288:176152:25:13:64:546:170:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:We define income tax revenue as current personal tax receipts (line 3) plus current taxes on production
77:3289:176255:13:14:64:546:157:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:and imports (line 4) minus the net subsidies to government sponsored enterprises (line 30 minus line
77:3290:176355:14:13:64:546:143:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:19) minus the net government spending to the rest of the world (line 25 + line 26 + line 29 - line 6 - line
77:3291:176462:13:14:64:546:130:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:9 - line 18).  Our logic for adding the last three items to personal tax receipts is as follows.  Taxes on
77:3292:176568:14:14:64:546:116:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:production and export mostly consist of federal excise and state and local sales taxes, which are mostly
77:3293:176672:14:13:64:546:102:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:paid by consumers.  Net government spending on GSEs consists mostly of housing subsidies received
77:3294:176769:13:14:64:546:89:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:by households which can be treated equivalently as lowering the taxes that households pay.  Finally,
77:3295:176869:14:0:64:546:75:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:in the data,  some of the domestic GDP is sent abroad in the form of net government expenditures
78:3296:176967:0:14:64:546:715:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:to the rest of the world rather than being consumed domestically.  Since the model has no foreigners,
78:3297:177068:14:13:64:546:701:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:we reduce personal taxes for this amount, essentially rebating this lost consumption back to domestic
78:3298:177169:13:38:64:97:688:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:agents.
78:3299:177176:38:24:64:365:650:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:C.5    Taxation of Savers’ Financial Income
78:3300:177219:24:14:64:546:626:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:Savers earn financial income from two sources.  First, they earn interest on their private lending i.e.
78:3301:177322:14:13:64:546:612:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:deposits in the financial intermediaries.  This income is ultimately a claim on the capital rents in the
78:3302:177426:13:18:64:525:599:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:economy and should be taxed at the same rateτKas borrowers’ and intermediaries’ net income.
78:3303:177517:18:13:75:547:581:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:Second,  they earn interest on their public lending i.e.  government bonds.  In the data,  Treasury
78:3304:177616:13:14:64:547:568:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:coupons are taxed at the household’s marginal tax rate,τin the model.  However, the tax revenue
78:3305:177711:14:13:64:542:554:11:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f8:collected by the government from interest income on its own bonds is substantially lower thanτBGt
78:3306:177808:13:14:64:546:541:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:because  (a)  Treasury  coupons  are  exempt  from  state  and  local  taxes,  and  (b)  more  than  half  of
78:3307:177917:14:17:64:516:527:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:privately owned Treasury debt is held by foreigners, who also do not pay federal income taxes.
78:3308:178011:17:14:75:547:510:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:In the model, there is one tax rateτDat which all of the saver’s interest income is taxed.  We choose
78:3309:178112:14:31:64:124:496:11:g_d0_f18:11:g_d0_f6:τDto satisfy
78:3310:178124:31:0:136:319:465:11:g_d0_f18:11:g_d0_f18:τD(ˆBI+ˆBG) =τK(ˆBI−ˆBIpension) +τ
78:3311:178158:0:14:322:352:472:11:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f4:ˆτfederal
78:3312:178167:14:0:325:348:458:11:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f4:ˆτtotal
78:3313:178174:0:27:353:475:465:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:(ˆBG−ˆBGforeign−ˆBIpension)
78:3314:178201:27:14:64:547:438:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:where hats denote quantities in the data.  Specifically, the revenue from taxes collected at rateτDon
78:3315:178302:14:13:64:546:424:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:all private safe debt and government debt must equal the sum of tax revenues collected on taxable
78:3316:178399:13:14:64:546:411:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:private safe debt (private safe debt not held in tax-advantaged pension funds) at rateτK,  and tax
78:3317:178497:14:15:64:546:397:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:revenues collected on taxable public debt (Treasury debt not held by foreigners, the Fed, or pension
78:3318:178597:15:0:64:175:382:11:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f8:funds) taxed at rateτˆτ
78:3319:178620:0:11:176:198:389:6:g_d0_f13:6:g_d0_f13:federal
78:3320:178627:11:13:175:202:378:8:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f6:ˆτtotal.
78:3321:178635:13:14:75:547:365:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:We measure all quantities at December 31, 2014.  Private debt stocks are taken from the Financial
78:3322:178732:14:13:64:546:351:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:Accounts of the United States.  Treasury debt stocks are taken from the Treasury Bulletin.  Federal
78:3323:178831:13:14:64:546:338:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:and total personal tax revenues are taken from the BEA’s National Income and Product Accounts.
78:3324:178925:14:13:64:546:324:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:There is approximately $13 trillion each outstanding of private and public debt.  Almost all private
78:3325:179025:13:14:64:546:311:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:debt is taxable, but only $4 trillion of public debt is.  Federal taxes constitute approximately 80% of
78:3326:179128:14:45:64:424:297:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:all personal income tax revenue.  Using the calibration forτKandτ, we get
78:3327:179201:45:0:211:235:252:11:g_d0_f18:11:g_d0_f9:τD≈
78:3328:179204:0:14:240:397:259:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f18:20%×$13T+ 29.5%×0.8×$4T
78:3329:179227:14:21:288:348:245:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f18:$13T+ $13T
78:3330:179237:21:38:64:180:224:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:orτD= 13.4% precisely.
78:3331:179259:38:24:64:340:186:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:C.6    Stationarity of Government Debt
78:3332:179297:24:14:64:546:162:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:In  our  numerical  work,  we  guarantee  the  stationarity  of  the  ratio  of  government  debt  to  GDP  by
78:3333:179407:14:13:64:547:148:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:gradually  decreasing  personal  tax  ratesτtwhen  debt-to-GDP  falls  belowbG=  0.1  –the  profligacy
78:3334:179509:13:14:64:546:135:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:region–  and  by  gradually  increasing  personal  tax  rates  when  debt-to-GDP  exceedbG=  1.2  –the
78:3335:179611:14:13:64:546:121:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:austerity region.  Specifically, taxes are gradually and smoothly lowered with a convex function until
78:3336:179713:13:14:64:546:108:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:they hit zero at debt to GDP of -0.1.  Tax rates are gradually and convexly increased until they hit 60%
78:3337:179817:14:14:64:546:94:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:at a debt-to-GDP ratio of 150%.  Our simulations never reach the -10% and +150% debt/GDP states.
78:3338:179913:14:13:64:546:80:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:The simulation spends 24% of the time in the profligacy and 15% of the time in the austerity region.
78:3339:180013:13:0:64:546:67:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:The  fraction  of  time  spent  in  these  regions  has  no  effect  on  the  overall  resources  of  the  economy.
79:3340:180130:0:14:64:546:715:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:Achieving  stationarity  of  government  debt  requires  primary  surpluses,  since  the  government  must
79:3341:180236:14:13:64:546:701:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:also  service  the  debt.   Generating  primary  surpluses  requires  slightly  overshooting  on  personal  and
79:3342:180347:13:14:64:546:688:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:corporate tax revenue relative to the data, since the U.S. government has historically had an average
79:3343:180448:14:13:64:546:674:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:primary surplus of (just about) zero.  Put differently, the actual U.S. fiscal path is unsustainable, i.e.,
79:3344:180555:13:38:64:247:661:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:incompatible with a stationary model.
79:3345:180592:38:24:64:393:623:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:C.7    Measuring Intermediary Sector Leverage
79:3346:180637:24:14:64:546:599:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:Our notion of the intermediary sector is the levered financial sector.  We take book values of assets and
79:3347:180742:14:13:64:546:585:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:liabilities of these sectors from the Financial Accounts of the United States (formerly Flow of Funds).
79:3348:180845:13:14:64:546:572:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:We subtract holding and funding company equity investments in subsidiaries from those subsidiaries’
79:3349:180944:14:13:64:546:558:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:liabilities.  Table 7 reports the assets, liabilities, and leverage of each sector as of 2014, as well as the
79:3350:181053:13:14:64:546:545:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:average leverage from 1953 to 2014.  We find that the average leverage ratio of the levered financial
79:3351:181154:14:17:64:294:531:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:sector was 91.5%.  This is our calibration target.
79:3352:181204:17:14:75:547:514:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:Krishnamurthy and Vissing-Jorgensen (2015) identify a similar group of financial institutions as net
79:3353:181304:14:14:64:546:500:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:suppliers of safe, liquid assets.  Their financial sector includes money market mutual funds (who do not
79:3354:181408:14:13:64:546:486:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:perform maturity transformation) and equity REITS (who operate physical assets) but excludes life
79:3355:181505:13:14:64:546:473:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:insurance companies (which are highly levered).  The financial sector definition of Krishnamurthy and
79:3356:181606:14:13:64:546:459:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:Vissing-Jorgensen (2015) suggests a similar ratio of 90.9%.  As an aside, we note that Krishnamurthy
79:3357:181706:13:14:64:546:446:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:and  Vissing-Jorgensen  (2015)  report  lower  total  assets  and  liabilities  than  in  our  reconstruction  of
79:3358:181819:14:13:64:546:432:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:their procedure because they net out positions within the financial sector by instrument while we do
79:3359:181919:13:0:64:83:419:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:not.

81:3387:183436:13:14:64:546:617:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:lines in figures 2 and 3 in the main text, as both are caused by the same combination of a low TFP
81:3388:183534:14:13:64:546:603:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:realization and an increase inσωin period 1.  The blue lines in figure 10 show dynamics after the
81:3389:183631:13:14:64:547:590:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:economy is hit only by the increase inσω, with stable TFP. The plots show that this pure uncertainty
81:3390:183731:14:13:64:546:576:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:shock has much smaller negative effects on output, consumption and investment than the combination
81:3391:183829:13:14:64:546:563:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:that causes a financial recession.  This feature of our model is consistent with the empirical finding
81:3392:183931:14:13:64:546:549:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:that uncertainty shocks alone have at most moderate negative effects on output and investment, see
81:3393:184029:13:18:64:342:536:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:for example Bachmann and Bayer (2013) or Vavra (2014).
81:3394:184083:18:14:75:547:518:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:A  closer  look  at  the  balance  sheet  variables  in  the  bottom  panel  reveals  that  the  fundamental
81:3395:184191:14:13:64:546:504:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:difference  between  both  types  of  shocks  lies  in  the  response  of  intermediaries.   The  losses  suffered
81:3396:184305:13:14:64:546:491:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:on loans during a financial crisis are only marginally larger than those from the uncertainty shock.
81:3397:184405:14:13:64:546:477:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:However, the financial sector does not shrink after the uncertainty shock. Rather, firms raise more debt
81:3398:184509:13:14:64:546:464:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:(bottom left panel) despite a temporarily smaller capital stock (top right panel), effectively increasing
81:3399:184614:14:13:64:546:450:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:leverage.  Banks reduce deposit funding only marginally (bottom middle).  The spikes in bank failure
81:3400:184714:13:14:64:546:437:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:rate and credit spread are less than half of those experienced in a financial recession.  We can conclude
81:3401:184819:14:13:64:546:423:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:that only the combination of TFP and uncertainty shock activates the intermediary-based financial
81:3402:184916:13:18:64:119:410:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:accelerator.
81:3403:184928:18:14:75:547:392:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:Why are financial recessions so much worse despite similar losses from borrower defaults for banks?
81:3404:185027:14:13:64:546:378:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:Figure 11 shows that the dynamics of the corporate bond price (top right) are the key amplifying force.
81:3405:185130:13:14:64:546:365:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:This price drops sharply in financial recessions, causing large market value losses for intermediaries.
81:3406:185233:14:13:64:546:351:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:This large drop in price is driven by two main forces.  First, the negative TFP shock reduces bank
81:3407:185331:13:14:64:546:338:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:demand for corporate bonds, as seen in Figure 3 in the main text.  Second, the losses on corporate
81:3408:185429:14:13:64:546:324:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:bonds caused by the uncertainty shock reduce bank capital, and thus amplify the first effect of reduced
81:3409:185532:13:14:64:546:311:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:demand on prices.  The stronger financial accelerator means that intermediary net worth falls only half
81:3410:185635:14:13:64:546:297:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:as much in an uncertainty shock episode compared to a financial recession (bottom right).  As a result,
81:3411:185738:13:14:64:546:284:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:intermediaries  are  not  forced  to  shrink  as  they  are  in  a  financial  recession.   Continuity  in  lending
81:3412:185853:14:13:64:546:270:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:to  borrower-entrepreneurs  prevents  a  sharp  reduction  in  investment  and  the  capital  price  (bottom
81:3413:185961:13:14:64:546:257:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:left) despite intermediary losses on loans.  In the third period of a financial recession,  intermediary
81:3414:186065:14:14:64:546:243:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:wealth overshoots as banks earn large spreads due to the sharp drop in the risk-free rate. Intermediaries
81:3415:186170:14:13:64:546:229:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:deplete this extra wealth to gradually expand lending again as the production sector recovers to normal
81:3416:186273:13:14:64:546:216:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:levels of capital.  These dynamics are not present in an uncertainty shock episode, since lending never
81:3417:186376:14:37:64:185:202:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:contracted to begin with.
81:3418:186401:37:24:64:313:165:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:D.2    Drivers of Financial Leverage
81:3419:186437:24:14:64:546:141:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:This appendix explores what model ingredients contribute quantitatively to the high financial leverage
81:3420:186539:14:14:64:546:127:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:that the benchmark model is able to generate.  Specifically, we turn off the three financial frictions, one
81:3421:186646:14:13:64:546:113:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:at the time:  (1) the bankruptcy option for banks, (2) equity adjustment costs (σI= 0), and (3) the
81:3422:186745:13:14:64:546:100:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:tax shield for financial firms.  Table 8 contains the results.  The main finding is that financial leverage
81:3423:186852:14:13:64:546:86:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:is affected very little by these financial frictions.  In other words, the main driver of the high financial
81:3424:186960:13:0:64:546:73:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:leverage is the wedge between the subjective time discount rate of borrowers and savers.  This wedge
82:3425:187062:0:142:67:543:717:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Figure 10:  Financial Recession vs.  Uncertainty Shock:  Macro Quantities and Balance Sheets

83:3532:188128:142:35:126:485:399:10:g_d0_f20:10:g_d0_f6:Blue line:uncertainty shock,red line:financial recession,black line:no shock
83:3533:188204:35:14:75:547:364:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:Furthermore, we see that when banks are not allowed to default, they stay away from their leverage
83:3534:188302:14:13:64:546:350:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:constraint  more  often.   Without  equity  adjustment  costs,  it  becomes  much  cheaper  to  recapitalize
83:3535:188410:13:14:64:546:337:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:banks  for  their  shareholders.   This  acts  like  a  reduction  in  risk  aversion  for  bank  shareholders  and
83:3536:188525:14:14:64:546:323:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:their leverage constraint becomes binding all the time.  The slightly higher financial leverage results
83:3537:188628:14:13:64:546:309:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:in  significantly  more  bank  bankruptcies.   The  effective  reduction  in  risk  aversion  also  lowers  the
83:3538:188739:13:14:64:546:296:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:required compensation for risk banks receive, as shown in the lower credit spread and excess return
83:3539:188838:14:13:64:546:282:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:on corporate bonds, despite a slightly higher loss rate on corporate loans.  The cheaper cost of debt
83:3540:188939:13:14:64:546:269:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:in turn incentivizes non-financial firms to increase leverage.  In sum, a reduction in the cost of equity
83:3541:189044:14:17:64:496:255:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:finance for banks has a stronger effect on non-financial leverage than on financial leverage.
83:3542:189137:17:14:75:547:238:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:The model without tax shield features higher credit spread and excess return and lower loss rates.
83:3543:189235:14:13:64:546:224:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:The banks manage to pass through the loss of their tax shield to their customers, the non-financial
83:3544:189334:13:14:64:546:211:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:firms.  Their compensation per unit of risk increases, providing incentives to increase financial leverage
83:3545:189440:14:37:64:449:197:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:(modestly).  The increased cost of credit coincides with lower corporate leverage.
83:3546:189522:37:25:64:343:160:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:D.3    Credit Spread and Risk Premium
83:3547:189559:25:13:64:546:135:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:One important quantitative success of the model is its ability to generate a high unconditional credit
83:3548:189661:13:14:64:546:122:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:spread while matching the observed amount of default risk.  The credit spread is also highly volatile
83:3549:189762:14:13:64:546:108:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:(2.94% standard deviation) and more than twice as high in financial recessions than in expansions.
83:3550:189860:13:14:64:546:95:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:The  rise  in  the  credit  spread  in  financial  recessions  to  4.28%  reflects  not  only  the  increase  in  the
83:3551:189977:14:13:64:546:81:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:quantity default risk but also an increase in the price of credit risk.  The model generates a high and
83:3552:190080:13:0:64:546:68:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:counter-cyclical  price  of  credit  risk,  which  itself  comes  from  the  high  and  counter-cyclical  “shadow

84:3562:190551:12:11:123:464:597:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:Market corp leverage (in %)35.836.938.833.6
84:3563:190594:11:36:123:464:586:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:Book corp leverage (in %)35.236.237.233.3
84:3564:190635:36:18:64:225:550:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:SDF” for the intermediary sector.
84:3565:190668:18:35:75:241:532:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:The intermediary SDF is given by:
84:3566:190701:35:0:194:274:497:11:g_d0_f9:8:g_d0_f4:MIt,t+1=MBt,t+1
84:3567:190716:0:11:276:285:516:11:g_d0_f11:11:g_d0_f11:(
84:3568:190717:11:16:286:364:505:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:1 +σI(dIt+1− ̄d)
84:3569:190733:16:0:291:359:489:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:1 +σI(dIt− ̄d)
84:3570:190747:0:19:365:384:516:11:g_d0_f11:8:g_d0_f4:)−1
84:3571:190750:19:35:387:417:497:11:g_d0_f18:11:g_d0_f18:F-,t+1,
84:3572:190757:35:11:64:546:462:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:whereMBt,t+1is  the  borrower  SDF,F-,t+1is  the  probability  of  intermediary  failure  int+ 1,  and
84:3573:190859:11:9:87:91:451:8:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f4:1
84:3574:190860:9:15:65:371:442:8:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f6:1+σI(dIt− ̄d)is the marginal value of wealth to intermediaries int.
84:3575:190927:15:13:75:547:427:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:Figure 12 shows the histogram of the intermediary wealth share plotted against two different mea-
84:3576:191024:13:14:64:546:414:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:sures of credit risk compensation earned by intermediaries.  The solid red line plots the credit spread,
84:3577:191128:14:16:64:547:400:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:the difference between the yieldrmton corporate bonds and the risk-free rate.  We compute the bond
84:3578:191226:16:0:64:150:384:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:yield asrmt= log
84:3579:191242:0:8:152:159:396:11:g_d0_f11:11:g_d0_f11:(
84:3580:191243:8:8:163:167:388:8:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f4:1
84:3581:191244:8:0:160:191:380:8:g_d0_f8:11:g_d0_f18:qmt+δ
84:3582:191249:0:12:191:198:396:11:g_d0_f11:11:g_d0_f11:)
84:3583:191250:12:17:197:546:384:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:.  This is a simple way of transforming the price of the long-term bond
84:3584:191321:17:14:64:546:367:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:into  a  yield;  however,  note  that  this  definition  assumes  a  default-free  payment  stream  (1,δ,δ2,...)
84:3585:191433:14:13:64:546:353:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:occurring in the future.  Consistent with the result in He and Krishnamurty (2013), the credit spread
84:3586:191534:13:14:64:546:340:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:is high when the financial intermediary’s wealth share is low.  Since our model has defaultable debt,
84:3587:191635:14:13:64:546:326:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:the increase in the credit spread reflects both risk-neutral compensation for expected defaults and a
84:3588:191736:13:18:64:161:313:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:credit risk premium.
84:3589:191756:18:13:75:547:295:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:To  shed  further  light  on  the  source  of  the  high  credit  spread,  we  compute  the  expected  excess
84:3590:191865:13:14:64:546:282:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:return (EER) on corporate loans earned by the intermediary.  The EER consists both of the credit
84:3591:191961:14:14:64:546:268:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:risk  premium,  defined  as  the  (negative)  covariance  of  the  intermediary’s  stochastic  discount  factor
84:3592:192072:14:13:64:546:254:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:with  the  corporate  bond’s  excess  return,  and  an  additional  component  that  reflects  the  tightness
84:3593:192181:13:14:64:546:241:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:of the intermediary’s leverage constraint.  This component arises because the marginal agent in the
84:3594:192280:14:13:64:546:227:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:market for risk-free debt is the saver household, while corporate bonds are priced by the constrained
84:3595:192381:13:14:64:546:214:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:intermediary.   The  market  risk  free  rate  is  lower  than  the  “shadow”  risk  free  rate  implied  by  the
84:3596:192494:14:13:64:546:200:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:intermediary SDF. Given log preferences, most of the action in the EER comes from the constraint
84:3597:192590:13:14:64:546:187:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:tightness  component.   When  intermediary  wealth  is  relatively  high,  the  leverage  constraint  is  not
84:3598:192699:14:13:64:546:173:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:binding  and  the  EER  is  approximately  zero.   Low  levels  of  intermediary  wealth  result  from  credit
84:3599:192809:13:14:64:546:160:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:losses, and the lowest levels occur during financial crises.  At these times, credit risk increases and the
84:3600:192916:14:13:64:546:146:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:intermediary becomes constrained.  In the worst crisis episodes when intermediary wealth reaches zero
84:3601:193017:13:0:64:300:133:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:or drops below zero, the EER reaches 20 percent.

85:3625:193381:36:29:64:379:419:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:D.4    Counter-cyclical Capital Requirements
85:3626:193425:29:24:64:228:390:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:D.5    Policy transitions
85:3627:193450:24:14:64:546:366:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:The tables above only compare the ergodic distributions of economies with different policy parameters.
85:3628:193552:14:13:64:546:352:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:How  does  an  unanticipated  policy  change  to  a  tighter  or  looser  capital  requirement  affect  output,
85:3629:193663:13:14:64:546:339:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:consumption, and the welfare of borrowers and savers in the short term?  Figure 14 plots the evolution
85:3630:193765:14:14:64:547:325:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:of these variables after a policy change from the benchmark to either a higher (ξ=.90) or a lower
85:3631:193862:14:13:64:547:311:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:(ξ=.97) capital requirement.  In the long run, output, consumption, and agent welfare converge to
85:3632:193959:13:14:64:546:298:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:their  ergodic  means  in  tables  4  and  5.   In  the  short  run,  consumption  “overshoots”  in  both  cases.
85:3633:194072:14:13:64:546:284:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:Tightening the capital requirement by 4 p.p.  leads a contraction in GDP as investment drops.  But
85:3634:194170:13:14:64:546:271:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:lower investment also causes a consumption boom in the short run as the economy transitions to a
85:3635:194266:14:37:64:219:257:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:permanently lower capital stock.
85:3636:194298:37:25:64:343:220:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:D.6    Effect of Equity Adjustment Cost
85:3637:194337:25:13:64:547:195:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:Table 9 shows the effect of larger or smaller equity adjustment costs (σI) relative to the benchmark
85:3638:194437:13:14:64:546:182:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:economy.  The overall take-away from this comparison is that larger equity frictions in the intermedia-
85:3639:194540:14:13:64:546:168:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:tion have a similar effect to tightening the intermediaries’ capital requirement.  Higher marginal equity
85:3640:194645:13:14:64:547:155:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:adjustments costs (columnsσI= 6,σI= 7) lead to a smaller non-financial sector, both in terms of
85:3641:194740:14:13:64:546:141:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:assets  and  liabilities.   Corporate  leverage  declines,  and  as  a  result,  fewer  firms  default,  causing  an
85:3642:194856:13:18:64:287:128:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:overall decline in loss rates on corporate loans.
85:3643:194905:18:13:75:547:110:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:Even though intermediaries face less credit risk, they reduce their own leverage and their constraint
85:3644:195006:13:14:64:547:97:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:becomes  binding  much  less  frequently  asσIis  increased.   Consequently,  intermediary  failures  are
85:3645:195111:14:13:64:546:83:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:almost  completely  eliminated  atσI=  7.   An  important  difference  to  the  macro-prudential  policy
85:3646:195215:13:0:64:546:70:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:exercise with tighter capital requirements is the effect on bank profitability.  In both cases (tighter

87:3736:197766:0:9:416:516:548:2:Helvetica:2:Helvetica:0.09Loan spread
87:3737:197781:9:9:476:502:539:2:Helvetica:2:Helvetica:bench
87:3738:197786:9:118:480:535:530:2:Helvetica:2:Helvetica:={93%, 95%}
87:3739:197797:118:12:64:547:412:10:g_d0_f20:10:g_d0_f20:Blue line:responses to financial recession in economy with counter-cyclical capital requirements;Black line:
87:3740:197905:12:35:64:539:400:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:responses to financial recession in benchmark economy.  The underlying shocks in the two cases are identical.
87:3741:198014:35:14:64:546:365:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:capital  constraint  and  higher  equity  adjustment  cost),  intermediaries  effectively  become  more  risk
87:3742:198123:14:13:64:546:351:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:averse  and  require  larger  compensation  for  bearing  risk,  as  evidenced  by  the  large  increase  in  the
87:3743:198236:13:14:64:547:338:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:excess return on loans (row 21).  However, increasingσIincreases the franchise value of intermediaries
87:3744:198338:14:13:64:546:324:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:(row 15), since it raises the risk premium while at the same time not requiring banks to raise more
87:3745:198437:13:18:64:453:311:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:equity.  Hence greaterσIraises the return on bank equity, while lowerξdoes not.
87:3746:198516:18:14:75:547:293:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:The overall welfare effects of larger equity adjustment frictions are comparable to the effects of tighter
87:3747:198622:14:13:64:547:279:11:g_d0_f18:11:g_d0_f6:ξ.  Locally the reduction in bankruptcies of producers and intermediaries dominates the reduction in
87:3748:198722:13:14:64:546:266:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:the size of the capital stock, leading to a small aggregate welfare gain based on the population-weighted
87:3749:198827:14:13:64:546:252:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:measure (row 22).  Like tighter capital regulation, greaterσIbenefits equity owners of producers at
87:3750:198926:13:18:64:167:239:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:the expense of savers.
87:3751:198948:18:13:75:547:221:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:The effects on macroeconomic volatility are nonlinear based on the same opposing forces that are
87:3752:199044:13:14:64:546:208:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:at play with tighter capital constraints:  since higher intermediation frictions increase the cost of debt
87:3753:199150:14:13:64:546:194:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:funding,  producers reduce the debt share of financing,  which makes financial recessions less severe.
87:3754:199252:13:14:64:546:181:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:At  the  same  time,  greater  intermediation  frictions  hamper  banks’  ability  to  absorb  aggregate  risk
87:3755:199362:14:14:64:547:167:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:through their balance sheet.  The net effect, at least locally around the benchmark level ofσI, is that
87:3756:199465:14:13:64:546:153:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:aggregate investment and consumption growth become less volatile with lower equity adjustment costs
87:3757:199564:13:14:64:547:140:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:(σI= 3,σI= 4), and risk sharing improves (MU ratio in row 40 becomes less volatile).  Interestingly,
87:3758:199664:14:13:64:547:126:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:this  is  also  the  case  for  slightly  higher  adjustment  costs  (σI=  6).   However,  as  we  increaseσIto
87:3759:199775:13:14:64:546:113:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:7,  the  impairment  of  banks’  risk-bearing  capacity  dominates  the  reduction  in  risk:  both  aggregate
87:3760:199885:14:13:64:546:99:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:consumption and investment growth are more volatile, and risk sharing between borrowers and savers
87:3761:199983:13:0:64:181:86:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:becomes worse (row 39).

88:3794:200381:36:24:64:375:433:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:D.7    Sensitivity of Macro-prudential Policy
88:3795:200426:24:14:64:546:409:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:In this appendix we study how sensitive the macro-prudential policy conclusions are to specific model
88:3796:200527:14:13:64:546:395:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:ingredients/parameter  constellations.   In  each  experiment,  we  compare  the  effects  of  relaxing  bank
88:3797:200636:13:14:64:546:382:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:capital requirements by two percentage points versus tightening them by two percentage points, around
88:3798:200737:14:13:64:547:368:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:the benchmark model.  In other words, we study a four percentage point relaxation fromξ=.92 to
88:3799:200831:13:14:64:547:355:11:g_d0_f18:11:g_d0_f6:ξ=.96.   The  first  column  of  Table  10  reports  the  results  from  this  particular  relaxation  for  the
88:3800:200942:14:14:64:546:341:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:benchmark model.  Firm loss rates and bank bankruptcies both increase, the size of the banking sector
88:3801:201043:14:13:64:546:327:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:and the economy as a whole increase, investment volatility falls modestly while consumption growth
88:3802:201141:13:14:64:546:314:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:volatility rises modestly,  and aggregate welfare falls since the gains to the savers are insufficient to
88:3803:201246:14:24:64:536:300:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:offset the losses to the borrowers.  All these results are in line with our discussion in the main text.

89:3820:201986:0:14:75:547:715:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:The other columns of Table 10 study the same change in macro-prudential policy in a model without
89:3821:202083:14:13:64:546:701:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:bankruptcy option (column 2), in a model without equity issuance costs (column 3), in a model without
89:3822:202184:13:14:64:546:688:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:tax shield for banks (column 4), in a model with more patient borrowers (column 5,βBincreases by
89:3823:202280:14:13:64:547:674:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:0.15), and less patient savers (columns 6,βSdecreases by 0.15).  The latter two changes decrease the
89:3824:202380:13:18:64:545:661:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:wedge between the patience of borrowers and savers and reduce the need for intermediation services.
89:3825:202479:18:14:75:547:643:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:The main finding is that the aggregate welfare changes from macro-prudential policy are robust to
89:3826:202576:14:13:64:546:629:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:these parameter variations.  In all experiments, welfare decreases in response to the four percentage
89:3827:202677:13:14:64:546:616:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:point increase in maximum allowable financial sector leverage from 92% to 96%. The range of estimates
89:3828:202778:14:13:64:546:602:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:is -0.35%, when banks are not allowed to fail (and hence cannot be bailed out), to -1.01%.  In all cases,
89:3829:202883:13:14:64:546:589:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:we see more fragility in the form of higher corporate loss rates and higher bank bankruptcies (except
89:3830:202984:14:13:64:546:575:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:of course when banks are not allowed to go bankrupt).  When it is easier and cheaper for shareholders
89:3831:203085:13:14:64:546:562:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:to recapitalize banks, the size of the banking sector is naturally less sensitive to a change in macro-
89:3832:203188:14:13:64:546:548:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:prudential regulation.  The basic trade-off between a larger banking sector and size of the economy
89:3833:203287:13:14:64:546:535:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:and more financial fragility is also present in every model.  The quantitative slope of that trade-off
89:3834:203389:14:13:64:546:521:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:depends on the model details.  The only results that are more fragile are those on macro-economic
89:3835:203486:13:14:64:546:508:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:volatility.  That should not come as a surprise since, even in the benchmark model, macro-economic
89:3836:203584:14:14:64:547:494:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:volatility is non-monotonic inξ.  Risk sharing tends to improve (MU vol falls) as macro-prudential
89:3837:203682:14:13:64:546:480:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:policy is relaxed, reflecting the financial sector’s improved ability to absorb aggregate risk when it is
89:3838:203787:13:14:64:546:467:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:larger.  The one exception is when bank equity can be costlessly adjusted,  which is also the model
89:3839:203886:14:0:64:528:453:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:when the banking sector size changes the least and macro-economic volatility increases the most.
